Current Affairs Commentary

Promoting Domestic Goods Factory Enterprises

— Liu

Recently, the Shanghai Municipal Social Bureau has sought to improve the organization of domestic goods marketplaces and has stipulated management methods. All those who organize or collect domestic goods from local manufacturers in the city to hold temporary domestic goods marketplaces or domestic goods exhibitions in other cities must register with the Bureau and abide by its rules. Those who violate the rules will be dealt with. As for domestic goods manufacturers' groups, there are no separate laws or regulations governing their organization, resulting in scattered organization, inconsistent actions, and affecting the progress of their business. Therefore, a meeting will be held today (16th) to petition the Sixth Plenary Session for the promulgation of such laws. Both of these are the beginning of the improvement of domestic goods factory enterprises.

In recent years, domestic goods marketplaces (including domestic goods exhibitions, domestic goods movements, etc.) have emerged one after another. Within one city, they spring up simultaneously in the east, west, south, and north. Within one country, they are held in different provinces and cities, almost becoming "fair-like" and "temple-like." However, the fact that they have penetrated deep into the people is a gratifying phenomenon. However, in order to compete for sales, each factory seeks lower prices and does not mind the poor quality of goods. The appearance is beautiful but not durable. The names of the goods are the same, but the quality varies greatly, which is self-defeating. The handicrafts in various places have been destroyed by foreign goods and are now suffering from the impact of domestic goods factory enterprises. If the products of domestic goods factories can meet the needs of the people, it is still a case of "Chu bow, Chu gain," and the benefits do not flow abroad. If not, it will serve as a counter-advertisement for foreign goods and strengthen the people's desire to buy foreign goods. Goods have fine and coarse qualities, and prices have expensive and cheap ranges. It is impossible to expect them to be uniform. However, there should be corresponding standards between their grade differences. Whether a good is durable and whether it is worth the price paid for it can be judged by comparison. If the price is cheap but not durable, and the price is more expensive but durable, people will naturally choose the latter without being persuaded. Therefore, setting prices for goods must take into account the economics of the user to make plans, so that their sales can be long-lasting. If they rely solely on the power of advertising, do not hesitate to exaggerate and distort the truth. When everything tried is false, not only will they lose the effect of advertising, but they will also incur the resentment of buyers. After that, even if there are good products, people will not believe them. For the sake of the future, domestic goods factories should cherish the glory of the two words "domestic goods" and pay special attention to the truth of domestic goods. Passing off foreign goods as domestic goods to confuse customers is undesirable. Even if the intention is for customers to try it once, it is not a proper way. As for borrowing the name of promoting domestic goods to reap personal fame and gain, as well as poor organization and improper management, leaving customers with a bad impression and causing participating manufacturers unnecessary losses, it will not work without the competent authorities' effective supervision and strict crackdown.

The biggest difficulty currently facing domestic goods factories is still the pressure from foreign goods. Increasing import tariffs cannot prevent the dumping of foreign goods, but will increase the competition for foreign merchants to set up factories locally. Most of the foreign goods that sell well now do not have independent manufacturing plants in Shanghai, but have compounding workshops. The convenience that domestic goods factories have is shared by them. Moreover, they have skilled technology and are good at management, which is far beyond the reach of domestic goods factories. They also have special forces backing them. It seems that domestic goods factories will also share the same fate as handicrafts. The domestic goods factory industry is aware of the dangers of the situation and must unite their front and take consistent steps to resist external encroachment and seek internal unity. If this cannot be done, how can we talk about industrial control?

Security Team and Militia Painstakingly Suppress Bandits in Zunhua: Remnants Fleeing Towards Malan Pass

(Tianjin) Yang Er's bandit gang was besieged by the security team led by Zhang Qingyu on the 12th. After a fierce battle lasting half a day, the bandits were defeated and fled. Yang led more than 200 of the remnants and arrived at Huanghuashan on the 13th, looting various villages. Zhang Qingyu's troops pursued and attacked them fiercely in the evening. The bandits fled towards Malan Pass. The militias of Xinglong and Jixian counties blocked the bandits from intruding. They arrived at the border on the 14th to deploy defenses. A part of the militia of the third district of Zunhua County was also transferred to assist in the defense. (15th Special Dispatch)

(Tianjin) There are many bandits in Xinglong County. County Magistrate Cha Jiang has requested the province to approve the organization of a temporary guerrilla police force to cooperate with the militia in suppressing bandits. He also plans to order each village to form scattered squads, with 100 able-bodied men drawn from every three villages, to defend themselves against bandits. (15th Special Dispatch)

Contents of the Shantou Case Resolution: Confiscated Soybean and Rice Smuggled Goods Returned; All Imported Goods Hereafter Subject to Taxation in Accordance with Regulations

(Hong Kong) Gan Jiehou and Deng Longguang arrived in Shantou one after the other to negotiate with the Japanese consul, together with Li Hanhun, Zhang Jinghui, and others. The smuggling case has been completely resolved. The contents include: 1. Our side will return the confiscated smuggled goods such as soybeans and rice. 2. The local ruffians who were captured for smuggling will be dealt with by our law. 3. All goods imported hereafter will be subject to taxation in accordance with regulations. (15th Special Dispatch)

(Hong Kong) In the terms of the Shantou case resolution, the article stating that Japanese merchants must pay taxes on imported goods in accordance with regulations refers only to customs duties. Other special taxes, such as agricultural product special taxes, are generally exempted. (15th Special Dispatch)

(Hong Kong) The American warship USS Asheville, stationed in Guangzhou, was ordered to pass through Hong Kong and open to Shantou on the morning of the 15th. (15th Special Dispatch)

(Hong Kong) Consul-General Kawai of Japan, stationed in Guangdong, arrived in Hong Kong on the evening of the 15th and will take the Ryuta Maru to Shanghai on the 16th to attend a meeting. According to reports, the Shantou case was resolved on the 14th, and Guangdong agreed to return the seized goods. Hereafter, Japanese goods imported will only be subject to customs duties and exempted from other taxes. The Japanese warship left Shantou on the 15th, and Usuda, the Japanese military attaché stationed in Guangdong, also went to Shanghai. (15th Special Dispatch)

(Guangzhou) Today, according to Chinese and Japanese authorities here, the Shantou negotiations are expected to be resolved peacefully within days. Reuters has learned that the rumor that the Japanese naval authorities have issued an ultimatum to local officials in Shantou is unfounded. It is also heard that the negotiations between the Japanese consul in Shantou and the municipal government have been progressing smoothly in recent days, and no unexpected incidents are expected to occur. Both Chinese and Japanese authorities here issued statements of reassurance tonight, which greatly comforted the public. Kawai, the Japanese Consul-General in Guangzhou, departed for Hong Kong this afternoon to attend a meeting in Shanghai. (15th Reuters Electric)

(Washington) Naval Department officials today denied that the dispatch of the cruiser USS Asheville to Shantou had been formally reported, but stated that the Asian Fleet had the right to move warships without notifying Washington. (14th National Electric)

(Hong Kong) Foreign consular officials here stated that the US warship USS Asheville was ordered to sail to Shantou yesterday due to the tense Sino-Japanese negotiations in Shantou. It is heard that a British warship will also depart from here for Shantou this afternoon. However, the British naval authorities are unwilling to release any information. Rumors say that the Japanese naval authorities have issued an ultimatum to local officials in Shantou, stating that if the Chinese customs do not stop collecting special taxes on Japanese and Taiwanese rice, Japanese marines will land tomorrow. The Japanese claim that this tax violates existing treaties. (15th Reuters Electric)

(Guangzhou) According to sources in charge, the situation in Shantou remains tense. The Chinese authorities refuse to acknowledge Japan's demand to stop collecting special taxes on Japanese rice. According to a key figure, the departure of the American warship USS Asheville yesterday was not originally ordered to go to Shantou; the order was received after departure. Consular officials hinted that the ship's going to Shantou was due to the transmission of information. (15th Reuters Electric)

American Female Lecturer at Central University Dies Tragically Under Beijige Pavilion: Police Department is Investigating

(Nanjing) At about 5:00 am on the 15th, soldiers and police discovered the body of a foreign woman on a slope on Xiaochuan Road, Wu Miao Bay, under the Beijige Pavilion. Her head was facing northwest and her feet were facing southeast. They reported to Chief Zhang Mengsong of the Sixth Bureau, who went to the scene to inspect and reported to the Police Department. The Police Department sent personnel to investigate. The female corpse was about 40 years old, wearing a Western-style suit and leather shoes, with a woman's hat, umbrella, and lecture notes left on the ground. Upon inspection, the woman's hat was made in San Francisco, USA, and the lecture notes were in English cursive, with the content being preparatory material for physiology. The investigation revealed that the deceased was the wife of Xu Shiju, a technician at the Ministry of Health. Xu is from Fenghua, Zhejiang, and is currently the Director of the Jiangning Experimental County Health Institute. His wife, originally from California, USA, had the Chinese name Xu Wansuzhen and was a doctor of medicine. Mrs. Xu had been in China for more than ten years and had been a professor of physiology at Qilu University in Jinan for many years. Last year, she married at Yenching University. After marriage, she went to Hunan with her husband and served as a technician at the Health Experiment Office. In early September of this year, she came to Beijing with her husband. Xu held his current position at the Ministry of Health, while Mrs. Xu served as a lecturer at the midwifery school of the Ministry of Health and a lecturer in physiology at Central University. They resided in Tushan Town, Jiangning County. Every Monday afternoon from 7:00 pm to 9:00 pm, Mrs. Xu had classes at Central University. At about 5:00 pm on the 14th, Mrs. Xu left the obstetrics school of Central Hospital. She told her husband that she was going to Central University to teach. Unexpectedly, she did not return all night. The Capital Court Prosecutor's Office sent forensic doctors and examiners to conduct an examination. As a result, only slight marks were found on the deceased's left neck, which were by no means fatal injuries. After consultation between the court and the Ministry of Health, it was decided to transport the body to Central Hospital for an autopsy to clarify the matter. Central Hospital performed the autopsy at about 2:00 pm. Liu Ruiheng, Director of the Ministry of Health, and Baker, the US Consul General in Beijing, personally went to observe. The results of the autopsy will not be clear until the 16th. Chen Zhuo, Director of the Police Department, attached great importance to the occurrence of this case. He invited Xu Shiju to the department to inquire in detail about his wife's situation and strictly ordered his subordinates to investigate so that the truth of the case could be revealed. (16th Special Dispatch)

Chiang Dingwen Arrives in Yanping: Scheduled to Inspect Defense Affairs in Various Places Starting Today

(Fuzhou) Chiang Dingwen arrived in Yanping on the 15th and is scheduled to go to Sha County, Jian'ou, Shaowu, and other counties on the 16th to inspect defense affairs and examine the pacification achievements of the defense forces. (15th Special Dispatch)

Main Force of Communist Bandits in Northern Shaanxi Concentrated in the Luochuan Area

(Taiyuan) The main force of the communist bandits in northern Shaanxi is now concentrated in the Luochuan area. Our army is adopting a strategy of steady advance to avoid being calculated by the bandits. He will go to the Yu Mausoleum to worship Yu on the 16th and participate in an air defense drill in the evening. (15th Special Dispatch)

Shuyang: The Army-Run River Embankment Breaches Again

(Qingjiangpu) The Shuyang flooded area has 33 townships in the 5th, 6th, 7th, 8th and 9th districts. On the morning of the 14th, the Army-Run River embankment breached again at Zhuzhuang, washing away 50 to 60 houses and flooding 30 hectares of fields. (15th Special Dispatch)

(Xuzhou) According to Hai Xun, the Army-Run River, eight li south of Shuyang City, was impacted by strong winds and waves last night. The Huangying Township section suddenly collapsed, and the entire embankment shook. Civilians crawled on the embankment, but their attempts to block it were ineffective, and many were swept away by the flood. In an instant, the entire embankment overflowed, and the water flowed through Danzhuang directly to the Qian River embankment. Shuyang City is under tight defense, and all city gates have been blocked overnight. The area south of the city is a vast expanse of water, collapsing houses, submerging fields, and sweeping away people, livestock, and other animals. Shuyang City is now urgently planning to defend the former Shuyang River embankment and city walls to divert the water. (15th Special Dispatch)

The West Bank of the Salt River Continues to Collapse: The Sound of Waves Can Be Heard Inside Banpu Dike

(Xuzhou) The water level in Banpu, the seat of Guanyun County, has dropped, but the water level in Dayi Mountain has risen sharply. Although water barriers have been built in the streets and lanes inside the dike, the surrounding water level is too high, resulting in excessive water pressure. Water sprouts are surging up in the stone cracks on the streets, threatening to submerge the area. Seven sections of the Chenwei area of the west bank of the Salt River have continued to breach, and the water is flowing towards the territory of Donghai. The area is six li away from Banpu, and the sound of the surging flood can be heard inside the Banpu dike. At the same time, the new embankment on the east bank of the Salt River has also collapsed, with more than 30 li of damaged areas waiting to be built. The Guanyun County Government is transporting sacks to repair it. (15th Special Dispatch)

(Xuzhou) After the Donghai Special Commissioner's Office stipulated the excavation of the Shaoxiang River to discharge the water volume of the Salt River, it was recently measured that the Shaoxiang River was higher than the Salt River. It was changed to excavate the northeast river bay for discharge. The diversion canal opened in Xinpu passes through the Yizhong (righteous tomb), and a notice has now been issued to relocate the burial. Work will begin soon. According to general observations, Donghai is downstream of Guanyun. Although the water level in Banpu has dropped, the water is overflowing. If it is not thoroughly discharged and the water is given a place to go, harm cannot be avoided. (15th Special Dispatch)

The Embankment of the Liutang River in the Four Counties' Jurisdictions is Raised

(Qingjiangpu) Commissioner Wang of Huaiyin telegraphed to the counties of Huaiyin, Lianshui, Siyang, and Suxian, ordering them to raise the Liutang River embankment in their jurisdictions by five feet and widen it by three zhang uniformly, with completion by the 20th. (15th Special Dispatch)

The Three Provinces of Hubei, Jiangxi, and Anhui Decide to Jointly Repair the Mahua Embankment

(Hankou) The governments of the three provinces of Hubei, Jiangxi, and Anhui have decided to jointly repair the Mahua Embankment. Xiong Shihui and the Yangtze River Conservancy have agreed to convene representatives in the province and go to Xunyang immediately to discuss the progress together. (15th Special Dispatch)

The Hubei Flood Relief Association is Preparing for Winter Emergency Relief: The Central Government Promises to Allocate Funds for Work Relief

(Hankou) The Flood Relief Association has decided to organize winter emergency relief and is discussing fundraising methods. (15th Special Dispatch)

(Hankou) Wu Guozhen is in Beijing seeking relief. The central government has agreed to allocate huge sums for work relief. (15th)

Lu Han Directs River Bureau to Build Office, Hastens Protection of Jucheng Embankment, and Cables Economic Committee for Funds to Quickly Block the Breach

(Jinan) The collapse of the Jucheng Embankment continues unabated, posing extreme danger. If it breaches, the entire county town will be submerged, and within the river bend areas of Fanxian, Shou Zhang, Yanggu, and other counties, tens of thousands of acres of fertile land will be completely flooded. A telegram has been sent to River Bureau Director Zhang Lianjia, who is attending a meeting in Kaifeng, and to Office Director Zhang Honglie, urging them to quickly go and supervise the efforts to protect the embankment. Furthermore, the Dongzhuang breach needs 750,000 units of material before the first of next month, and 540,000 units of material costs before December 1st. A telegram has already been sent to the Economic Committee requesting prompt allocation of funds. (Fifteenth Dispatch)

Four Provinces' Breach Blocking, Embankment Restoration Conference Opens

(Kaifeng) The Four Provinces' Breach Blocking and Embankment Restoration Conference was held at the Huangli Association at around 4 PM on the 15th. Attendees included Kong Xiangrong, Xu Xinwu, Zhang Hanying, Wang Yujun, Lu Zhang Honglie, Zhang Lianjia, Zhou Li, Ji Qishouan, Su Yu Shufang, and Yu Zhu Tong. Directors of each group of the association were also present. Chairman Kong Xiangrong delivered a report. Discussions on the proposals were still ongoing at around 7 PM. (Fifteenth Dispatch)

It is reported that the Chairman of the Relief Commission, Xu Shiying, indicated that he would expedite the allocation of funds to be remitted for relief efforts. (Fifteenth Dispatch)

Ministry of Finance Issues Order: Mineral Products Exempted from Transit Tax

(Nanjing) On the 15th, the Ministry of Finance instructed the superintendents of all customs offices that all mineral products with tax receipts already paid, upon inspection by customs during transit to verify that the goods match the documentation, should be uniformly exempted from transit tax. The original receipt should be stamped for release. The customs offices should implement the said method of exempting transit tax from October 16th of this year. In addition to instructing the Inspector General of Customs to comply, immediate compliance is also required. (Fifteenth Dispatch)

Page 7

Paris Carries Out Diplomatic Reconciliation Efforts. Laval Meets With British and Italian Ambassadors. Asks Italy to Propose Minimum Armistice Conditions. Papal Representative Willing to Mediate.

(Paris) French Prime Minister and Foreign Minister Laval met today with British Ambassador Clerk, Italian Ambassador Cerutti, and Papal Representative Marion, to seek new efforts to advance world peace. It is understood that Britain has agreed not to request the League of Nations to implement stricter sanctions within ten days, pending a response from Italian Prime Minister Mussolini. It is reported that Laval has requested Mussolini to specify the minimum acceptable armistice conditions, and it is also understood that Mr. Marion has also requested the Pope to urge Mr. Mussolini to accept a peaceful resolution. (Fifteenth National Telegram)

(Paris) There is currently no confirmed information regarding the content of French Prime Minister Laval's talks with the British and Italian ambassadors yesterday. However, the French side acknowledges that Laval is currently adopting diplomatic reconciliation efforts, which are confidential. According to French newspapers, the assertion that Laval is awaiting Mussolini's minimum conditions cannot be confirmed. News of Laval's initiation of reconciliation has aroused satisfaction among people in Rome, but news regarding this matter from Italian official circles is still silent. It is widely believed that Italy will make every effort to support a solution that is compatible with its dignity. At the same time, Rome has received a report that Chief of the General Staff, General Badoglio, has arrived in Massawa. (Fifteenth Reuters Telegram)

Differing Opinions on Peaceful Resolution of the Dispute Between Britain and Italy. Britain Insists on the Original Plan, Which Italy Finds Difficult to Accept.

(Rome) Regarding the peaceful resolution of the Italian-Abyssinian dispute, it is generally believed that it will be difficult for Britain and Italy to find a compromise solution, and that mutual acceptance is unlikely to be possible, at least at present. Italy still insists on administering the border areas of Abyssinia under a mandate system, while Britain insists that only a small part can be mandated, with Abyssinia gaining access to the sea as an exchange condition. Although Italy has not put forward any plan on this issue, and Italian diplomatic circles have repeatedly stated that the Italian government has no intention of putting forward such a plan, based on what is reported in Italian newspapers, the speeches made by Italy's chief representative to the League of Nations, Aloisi, and the broadcasts made to the American people, Italy's views are no more than the following: (1) Italy does not reject the peaceful resolution; (2) Abyssinian territory must be divided into two parts, one being the mainland territory of Abyssinia and the other being the provinces annexed in recent decades. Italy has already signed treaties with Abyssinia before the establishment of the League of Nations and should naturally enjoy special rights in these provinces; (3) If the Covenant of the League of Nations can be interpreted more appropriately, it can naturally be integrated with the current situation. Sugimura, the Japanese Ambassador to Italy, once drafted a plan advocating that the border provinces of Abyssinia should be administered by Italy under a mandate system, while the mainland territory should be administered by the League of Nations under a mandate system. Italy can accept this plan. Political figures here believe that although Article 22 of the Covenant of the League of Nations only stipulates that the colonies of defeated countries, such as Germany and Austria, may adopt the mandate system, its scope of application may be expanded. It is also said that Abyssinia is, in practice, under the supervision of foreign advisers, and Abyssinia has also declared on its own initiative that it is prepared to accept any assistance from the League of Nations that can promote its political and economic level. Therefore, the mandate system that Italy can adopt for the border provinces of Abyssinia belongs to "Class B Mandate" (see Article 22, Paragraph 5 of the Covenant of the League of Nations). In other words, Italy is not allowed to freely establish an army in this mandated territory. If so, Britain's concerns about the establishment of indigenous troops near its colonies of Kenya and the Egyptian Sudan, or under foreign management, can be dispelled. As for the plan set by Britain, it was proposed by British Secretary of State for Dominion Affairs Eden when he visited Rome in May of this year, and has not changed so far, that is, to cede the Ogaden region of Abyssinia to Italy and allow Italy to enjoy economic privileges in Abyssinia, while giving Abyssinia a seaport in British Somaliland, which was rejected by Italy. The reasons are (1) the Ogaden region is a desert area; (2) the so-called economic privileges are unreliable, and what is the difference between this and the privileges granted to Italy by the 1928 Italian-Abyssinian Treaty; (3) if a sea passage is given to Abyssinia, it will naturally enable Abyssinia to expand its military equipment, and the threat to Italian territory in East Africa will also be expanded. Italy rejected this proposal before the East African war started, and now that it has occupied several sections of Abyssinian territory, it is even more difficult to accept. Moreover, Britain has previously declared that it will refuse to negotiate before the Italian army withdraws from Abyssinia, or at least before military operations cease. Italy says that the precondition for negotiations is to suspend sanctions. With such differences in opinion, how can there be any hope? (Fifteenth Havas Telegram)

British Chancellor of the Exchequer States: The Door to Negotiations is Not Closed. Prepare Early for Difficulties. Defence Programme Is Not For Aggression.

(London) Chancellor of the Exchequer Chamberlain said in a speech in Glasgow today that the British government had stated previously that if Italy did not resort to force in the Italian-Abyssinian dispute, Britain would be willing to help Italy fulfill its legitimate aspirations. Even today, after Italy has already started the war, Britain has never retracted this statement. "We do not want to close the door that was opened to Italy not long ago." Referring to the suggestion that the general election be postponed until next spring, the Chancellor asked the public, "Do we have the right to say that the crisis will be over by next spring? Do not deceive yourselves. We are not at the end of a crisis, but at the beginning of what may be a long era of hardship and fear. In this era, crises of the most serious nature may recur." The Chancellor then referred to Britain's defence programme, stating clearly that it was not intended for aggression. He said, "What we are undertaking is the absolute minimum necessary to achieve our objectives, and we do not want to go beyond this. Our efforts to obtain a general agreement on disarmament are not being relaxed." (Fourteenth Reuters Telegram)

League of Nations Adjustment Committee Passes Financial Sanctions Plan. Representatives of Hungary and Austria Abstain.

(Geneva) The League of Nations General Assembly Sanctions Plan Adjustment Committee (hereinafter referred to as the Sanctions Committee) held a plenary meeting at 6 PM today. Representatives from all 53 member states of the League of Nations, excluding the parties involved, Italy and Abyssinia, attended. The meeting was very short. It unanimously passed the financial sanctions plan drafted by the Eighteen-Nation Committee. Before the vote on the plan, Hungarian representative Nickel declared that Hungary was a debtor nation and had nothing to do with financial sanctions, so it abstained from voting. Austrian representative Schüller also made the same statement. Representatives from Uruguay and Venezuela declared that they had to consult with their respective governments. Argentine representative Gracio declared that "Argentina will vote in favor of the financial sanctions plan, but it should be stated that there are one million Italian expatriates in Argentina, so some of the clauses in the plan are quite difficult for the Argentine government to implement. This should be considered by the Sanctions Committee." At this point, the Sanctions Committee passed the financial sanctions plan against Italy.

French Suggestions

The Sanctions Committee then passed a motion proposed by the French delegation. The motion suggested the following four items: (1) The Eighteen-Nation Subcommittee should immediately study the implementation plan for League of Nations member states to prohibit the export of various raw materials and finished products used for military purposes to Italy and stop the import of Italian goods. A special committee should be set up to study this plan. (2) The Eighteen-Nation Subcommittee should simultaneously study the implementation plan for economic mutual assistance among League of Nations member states in accordance with Section 3 of Article 16 of the Covenant. Another committee should be set up to study this plan. (3) The Eighteen-Nation Subcommittee should request the above two committees to carry out their work as soon as possible. (4) The above two committees should each draft specific plans and submit them to the Eighteen-Nation Committee for submission to the Sanctions Committee for approval and implementation.

Appointment of Two Committees

After the above motion was passed by the Sanctions Committee, two committees were appointed immediately: (1) the Economic Sanctions Committee, including fourteen countries such as Portugal, France, the Soviet Union, Poland, Spain, Canada, the Netherlands, Sweden, Switzerland, Argentina, Belgium, Turkey, Romania, and Mexico; (2) the Economic Mutual Assistance Committee, including nine countries such as Portugal, France, the Soviet Union, Poland, Spain, the Union of South Africa, Greece, Romania, and Yugoslavia. This is the result of today's plenary meeting of the Sanctions Committee. Since the establishment of the Sanctions Committee, it has completed the two major steps of embargoing arms and financial sanctions in just a few days, and is now starting to work on economic sanctions. The speed and agility of its work is unprecedented in the history of the League of Nations. Therefore, some political figures feel that if the Sanctions Committee continues to progress at this rate, the League of Nations may eventually become a tool of conflict. (Fourteenth Havas Telegram)

(Geneva) Spanish representative Contos was elected today as chairman of the Economic Mutual Assistance Committee. This committee will seek to reduce the sacrifices made by some countries due to participating in economic sanctions against Italy. When explaining the purpose of this committee, Contos declared that some countries did not intend to obtain compensation from other countries, saying that we must all make sacrifices in order to restore peace. The sacrifices needed for peace are less than those needed for war. However, in order to comply with Article 16 of the Covenant of the League of Nations, we must have an agreement in order to reduce losses and inconveniences. The committee decided to compile statistics on Italy's foreign trade and submit them to tomorrow's meeting. (Fifteenth Reuters Telegram)

Full Text of the Sanctions Plan

(Geneva) The League of Nations General Assembly Sanctions Committee passed a plan tonight to implement financial sanctions against Italy in accordance with Article 16 of the Covenant. The full text is as follows:

For the convenience of League of Nations member states in fulfilling their obligations under Article 16 of the Covenant, the following measures are hereby adopted:

(1) The governments of League of Nations member states shall immediately take various steps to ensure that the following transactions are completely prohibited: (A) Directly or indirectly providing loans to the Italian government and subscribing to bonds issued directly or indirectly by the Italian government domestically or abroad; (B) Directly or indirectly lending to the Italian government various bank loans and other loans of a nature, and fulfilling contracts to lend directly or indirectly to the Italian government in the form of advances or other means; (C) Directly or indirectly providing loans to public institutions, natural persons, and legal persons within the Italian territory, and subscribing to bonds issued by them domestically or abroad; (D) Directly or indirectly lending to natural persons and legal persons within the Italian territory bank loans and other loans of a nature, and fulfilling contracts to lend directly or indirectly to these natural persons and legal persons in the form of advances or other means; (E) Issuing shares on behalf of public institutions, natural persons, and legal persons within the Italian territory, or subscribing to shares or any kind of capital issued by them domestically or abroad.

(2) The governments of League of Nations member states agree to prohibit the various transactions mentioned in Items A to E above. All such transactions, whether conducted by nationals of their own country or by intermediaries from other countries, are prohibited.

(3) The League of Nations member states are requested to notify the Secretariat of the League of Nations as soon as possible of the measures taken in accordance with the above clauses. (Fourteenth Havas Telegram)

The Plan Is Quite Thorough

(Geneva) The progress in financial sanctions is due to the efforts of Greek representative Maximos, chairman of the Financial Subcommittee, and French technical expert Courant. Maximos handled the financial proposals at the meeting of the Eighteen-Nation Committee with competence and speed. He said that the resolutions were very thorough, and that any possible form of lending or financial business, whether directly or indirectly to the Italian government, was almost entirely included. (Fifteenth Reuters Telegram)

Can Be Implemented This Month

The Sanctions Committee will reconvene this afternoon. If the current progress can be maintained, everything can be decided before the end of this week. It is widely expected that financial sanctions can be implemented around October 31. (Fifteenth Reuters Telegram)

(Geneva) The British representative suggested that October 31 be the final date for the governments of League of Nations member states to approve the implementation of financial and economic sanctions against Italy. This proposal was passed by the Eighteen-Nation Committee today. Previously, South American representatives had stated that member states must approve the actions of their representatives in Geneva by their respective parliaments, and that the resolutions of the League of Nations Committee could not force countries to implement them. Therefore, Britain made this suggestion. (Fourteenth National Telegram)

Soviet Representative Advocates Opening New Markets for Sanctioning Countries

(Geneva) When the Soviet representative, Potemkin, discussed the issue of economic sanctions at the Sanctions Handling Committee, he strongly stated that sanctions must be carried out resolutely and effectively, and must be universal, otherwise they would be ineffective. Potemkin mentioned that some countries would not participate in sanctions, and some countries even refused to participate. He also expressed his willingness to ask the US government to prohibit the export of certain commodities (i.e., those specified in the form prescribed by President Roosevelt). As for dealing with countries that refuse to participate in sanctions, would it not be better to limit the necessary loans to these countries to the minimum and limit the import of goods used for military industries to these countries? As for the countries that suffer losses due to the implementation of economic sanctions, we should find ways to distribute these losses proportionally or open up new markets for these countries. (Fourteenth TASS Telegram)

Japan Actively Approaches China, Adopts a Wait-and-See Attitude Towards the Italian-Abyssinian Dispute

(Tokyo) Italian Ambassador to Japan, Auriti, visited Vice Minister of Foreign Affairs Shigemitsu at the Ministry of Foreign Affairs at 11:30 this morning to listen to the proceedings of the League of Nations, inquire about Japan's opinion on the League of Nations' economic sanctions against Italy, and hear about Lytton's activities in China and Japan's new policy towards China. The meeting lasted for 30 minutes before Auriti departed. (Fifteenth Den-tsu Telegram)

(Tokyo) Today, when the Italian Ambassador met with Vice Minister Shigemitsu, he inquired about Japan's attitude towards the League of Nations' economic sanctions against Italy. Vice Minister Shigemitsu seemed to have stated the following: Japan is of course greatly concerned about the future development of the Italian-Abyssinian dispute. However, both Italy and Abyssinia have close friendly relations with Japan, and because the dispute is in Europe, Japan has no intention of taking sides. The wait-and-see attitude initially adopted has not changed to date. Recently, the League of Nations has implemented economic sanctions against Italy and has reportedly invited non-member states such as Japan, the United States, and Germany to participate. However, Japan has not heard anything about this. If the League of Nations has invited Japan to join, Japan does not need to express its attitude towards the issue of sanctions within the League of Nations' internal actions. (Fifteenth Den-tsu Telegram)

British Conservative Party Members of Parliament Petition Government Not to Impose Sanctions

(London) Forty members of the Conservative Party in the House of Commons held a meeting the other day and unanimously resolved to request the government not to advocate for the implementation of sanctions against Italy at the League of Nations, and not to participate, for fear that the implementation of sanctions would lead to war. These members of parliament have recently appointed a delegation, led by former Colonial Secretary Amery, to meet with Prime Minister Baldwin to ask him to reassure the people that Britain will neither propose nor participate in sanctions that could lead to war. (Fifteenth Havas Telegram)

Britain, Belgium, and the Netherlands Comply With League of Nations Resolution, Cancel Arms Embargo on Abyssinia

(Geneva) British Secretary of State for Foreign Affairs, Eden, recently notified the Secretariat of the League of Nations in writing that the British government, in accordance with the resolution of the League of Nations General Assembly Sanctions Committee, has recently revoked the order to embargo arms to Abyssinia. As for the arms embargo on Italy, it will continue to be maintained in accordance with the current methods. (Fourteenth Reuters Telegram)

(London) Regarding the effectiveness of economic sanctions against Italy, it has recently been reported by responsible parties that the goods embargoed for export by the United States do not include kerosene and raw materials. If the Soviet Union also takes this step, the fuel needed for Italian aircraft, tanks, warships, and merchant ships will be impossible to prevent. According to news from Berlin, Germany does not seem to be participating in sanctions. However, officials believe that no matter what the attitude of other countries is, Britain will not change its current firm stance. (Fourteenth Havas)

American Ambassador Explains America's Neutral Position to Britain

(London) Reuters has learned that US Ambassador to London, Bingham, recently met with British Foreign Secretary Hoare and gave a responsible explanation of America's neutral position. In the first meeting, Bingham further clarified President Roosevelt's declaration of October 5 (i.e., declaring that any American who voluntarily engages in transactions with Italy or Abyssinia must do so at their own risk). In the second meeting, Hoare made some comments on Bingham's statement, but did not ask what attitude the United States would take if there were any decisions on sanctions against Italy in Geneva. (Fifteenth Reuters Telegram)

Hull's Important Speech Advocating International Joint Action to Restore Peace and Prosperity

(Washington) Secretary of State Hull gave a radio address today advocating a triple international effort for peace and prosperity. Hull applied for international action to be implemented simultaneously: (1) Actively reforming international trade; (2) Gradually restoring monetary stability; (3) Securing international agreements that ensure affordable prices for all important raw materials needed everywhere. Hull said, "Every conflict leaves seeds for future conflicts. This is extremely obvious. Now, to overcome the causes of conflict, many countries must act simultaneously." The raw materials mentioned by Hull echo the recent remarks made by British Foreign Secretary Samuel Hoare on this issue, which proves that the United States is not opposed to participating in discussions. People regard Hull's words on monetary stability as particularly important, because US Treasury Secretary Morgenthau, who is currently in Paris, told reporters yesterday that the United States is prepared to discuss monetary stability and exchange rates. Morgenthau visited the French Finance Minister yesterday and visited French Prime Minister Laval again today. (Fifteenth Reuters Telegram)

US Shipbuilding Plan to Add Nineteen Warships of Various Sizes and Increase Naval Personnel to 200,000

(Washington) According to a document released by the US Navy Department today, the United States plans to build one battleship, twelve destroyers, and six submarines in the fiscal year 1937. Naval personnel will be increased to 200,000. The United States also plans to add naval auxiliary ships, such as transport ships, tugboats, barges, and military supply ships, in the fiscal year 1936. (Fourteenth Reuters Telegram)

(Tokyo) In an effort to strengthen national defence on the Pacific coast, the US Navy authorities plan to build a large-scale important military base on San Clemente Island, 50 nautical miles from the southern California bay. San Clemente Island is only a rocky islet, but if military facilities are added, its status will become more important. Its interests to the United States in the Pacific are like those of Malta to Britain in the Mediterranean. It is reported that shipyards, aircraft landing fields, and storage depots are already under construction on the island. (Fifteenth Hua Lian Telegram)

Regarding the Naval Issue, Japan's Reply Content Opposes the British Proposal

(Tokyo) On September 28, the British government sent a note to Japan proposing to convene a disarmament conference. The relevant Japanese ministries studied countermeasures and recently reached a consensus. After the cabinet meeting today, it was immediately telegraphed to Fujii, the acting ambassador to the United Kingdom. The gist of the telegram is as follows: "Japan's policy is to reduce the burden on the people based on the principle of non-aggression and non-threat. Although it is prepared to participate in military conferences convened in accordance with this policy, the British proposal this time is not consistent with Japan's policy. Mutual implementation of short-term warship construction plans, etc., may hinder a country's autonomous realization of military preparations, and a single agreement on qualitative disarmament alone will not achieve the real purpose of disarmament, so we strongly oppose the British government's proposal." (Fifteenth Den-tsu Telegram)

Shipbuilding Statistics of Various Countries

(London) According to Lloyd's Quarterly Report, as of September 30, there were a total of 110 ships under construction in Britain and Ireland, totaling 530,554 tons. On the same day, there were a total of 178 ships under construction in foreign countries, totaling 667,415 tons. Among them, Germany had the most, totaling 268,340 tons, and Sweden had the least, totaling 8,900 tons. (Fifteenth Reuters Telegram)

Using New-Style Deadly Weapons: Italian Forces Penetrate Deep into Southern Abyssinia; Poison Gas Bombs Cause Numerous Casualties; Northern Route Simultaneously Takes Offensive; Abyssinian Army Concentrates Preparations for War

(London) A Daily Mail reporter stationed in the field received a telephone report from a European engineer in the Worka-Gouden province, stating that in the bloody battle in the Jerro-Goubi area, the Abyssinian army had suffered as many as 18,000 casualties. The Italian army is now using a new type of poison gas, causing Abyssinian soldiers and civilians alike to suffocate and flee northward in a frenzy. There was a major battle on Saturday in the Dalo area, where 4,000 Abyssinian soldiers and civilians died. The Italian side used 200 aircraft to cover General Graziani's troops as they advanced. Bombardment and poison gas bombs rained down on the Abyssinian lines. After the air attacks, they were followed by tanks. The Italian southern route has penetrated 31 miles into Abyssinian territory, and the front line has expanded from Walwal to Damot. However, the large Abyssinian army providing support from the rear has also concentrated approximately 200,000 men in the areas of Jijiga, Harar, and Tounsa, all under the strict orders of the Emperor to defend the border line of the plateau. This army is guided by foreign military advisors, such as Turkish General Vehip Pasha and German General von Riem, etc. Swiss engineers working in the Shebelle River basin reported that a large contingent of the Abyssinian army has crossed the Jubba River and is advancing rapidly, intending to attack Italian Somaliland in order to cut off the communication lines of General Graziani's forces. It is reported that General Taibono, the Italian northern route commander, personally flew hundreds of miles into Abyssinian territory last Wednesday. The Daily Mail reporter also stated that Abyssinia's Minister to France and chief representative to the League of Nations, Haile Wereide, has been appointed as the commander-in-chief of the Abyssinian army. It is said that Mr. Haile is about to depart from Geneva to return to his country and assume command of the front lines. (National Telegram, 15th)

Addis Ababa: According to a non-official telegram from Makale today, the Italian army has resumed its offensive on the northern front. The Italian army is advancing rapidly with tanks and armored vehicles on the plains between Houchane and Abaro (southeast of Adwa). The speed of their advance has startled the vanguard of General Seyoum's Abyssinian northern route command. General Seyoum is currently avoiding contact with the Italian army. It is anticipated that the Abyssinian army will defend in the mountains northwest and northeast of Makale. At the same time, a portion of the 250,000-strong army commanded by General Gassa has crossed the Tacazze River. If the Italian army advances towards Makale, this route of the Abyssinian army will threaten the Italian army's right flank. General Gassa is currently cooperating with General Seyoum. General Seyoum has been receiving a steady stream of reinforcements in recent days, but is currently unwilling to engage in a major decisive battle with the Italian army and is retreating in the direction of Makale. Today, 20,000 fresh troops arrived in Addis Ababa from Wa, Kaffa. The rear troops arriving in the capital are continuous, but there are not enough weapons to supply them. Therefore, the Emperor may order some of them to return to their hometowns. (Reuters Telegram, 15th)

Italian Army on the Northern Route Consolidates Rear Positions; Adwa Border Highway Completed; Chief of Staff Arrives at Massawa Port

(Rome) The Italian army's front line on the northern route, which connects the three cities of Adigrat, Adwa, and Aksum, has now been arranged to become a base for the Italian army's offensive. However, before Chief of Staff General Badoglio arrives at the front lines, an offensive will not be launched immediately. The highway connecting Adwa to the border has recently been completed. The first batch of transport trucks has already arrived in this city from the rear. Military experts attach great importance to this project, because there are two new-style highways from Italian Eritrea to the front lines: one to Adwa and one to Adigrat. (Havas Telegram, 15th)

Rome: News has just been received here from Italian Eritrea confirming that Chief of Staff General Badoglio arrived at the port of Massawa yesterday afternoon. It is reported that the General departed from the port of Naples on the Conte Biancamano steamship on the 10th of this month to go to East Africa. He has now arrived at the port of Massawa in five days, so he must have transferred to an airplane en route, hence the speed. It is generally believed that General Badoglio's rapid trip to the front lines is a sign of a renewed offensive by the Italian army on the northern route. (Havas Telegram, 15th)

Large Italian Army Enters Aksum City; Not Bombed Due to Being a Religious Holy Site; Italian Army on the Southern Route Halts Advance Temporarily Due to Rain

(Rome) A special correspondent of the "Fascist Party Work Report" reported on the Italian army's occupation of Aksum, stating that this morning, the Archbishop of Aksum personally surrendered to General Taibono, the High Commissioner for East Africa, and presented the keys to the city gates. A large Italian army then marched into the city without resistance. The first to enter the city were the Askaris of the 23rd Regiment. Large numbers of reinforcements followed. Most of the residents in the city surrendered to the Italian army with their livestock. The Abyssinian army also surrendered en masse. (Havas Telegram, 14th)

(Rome) This afternoon, it was announced here that the Archbishop of the holy city of Aksum had today presented the keys of the city to General Taibono, the commander-in-chief of the Italian army in East Africa. At the same time, according to news from Adwa, Aksum was taken without a fight. Italian outposts have reached the outskirts of the city. The Italian army did not bombard the city due to its religious nature. The Italians believe that with the fall of Aksum, the first act of the war in East Africa will be completed, and the second act will begin soon, and it will not encounter stubborn resistance, because Italian planes flew into the interior for reconnaissance and reported that no enemy troops were seen at all. At the same time, the Italian army advancing to Jerro-Goubi in the Worka-Gouden province has been stopped by heavy rain at Jerrohai and has temporarily halted its advance. (Reuters Telegram, 15th)

Abyssinian Ammunition Depot Bombed

(Rome) According to news received here today, three Italian planes flew south from Makale near Adwa and bombed an Abyssinian ammunition depot. The Abyssinian army attempted to drive away the planes with rifle fire and shrapnel cannons. (Reuters Telegram, 15th)

Abyssinian Chiefs Surrender to the Italian Army One After Another

(Rome) Several chiefs of important regions in Abyssinia, such as Balambaras Kaggalasmaao, etc., have surrendered to the Italian army one after another. Their guards were all armed with rifles manufactured by British and Belgian companies. Furthermore, Egyptian Coptic priests from thirteen places such as Ribano, Surada, Anda, and Mariavie visited General Maravigna, the commander of the Italian army's right flank, and claimed that Grazmatch Guffsa, a descendant of the old Abyssinian royal family, surrendered to the Italian army due to an internal rebellion within his tribe.

(Rome) Semi-official sources announced that the military authorities in East Africa are planning to reorganize the subordinates of Grazmatch Guffsa, a surrendered Abyssinian general, into a formal native army. Also, 500 Abyssinian prisoners of war captured by the Italian army will be sent to the front lines to build roads. It is reported that these prisoners of war had been starving for five days when they were captured. It is also heard that the total area of land occupied by the Italian army in Abyssinia has reached 4,000 square kilometers. (Havas Telegram, 14th)

Two Abyssinian Tribes Fight Each Other

(London) According to unconfirmed news from Dagahbur, in the southeastern corner of Abyssinia, bordering British Somaliland and Italian Somaliland, the civilians of the Isaaq and Mijertein Somali tribes engaged in a fierce battle today. It is reported that there were many casualties on both sides. It is heard that the Dolbahanta tribe has risen up to assist the Mijertein tribe. The British authorities have ordered them to refrain from taking any action, stating that if they do not comply, they will revoke their protection of them. (Reuters Telegram, 4th)

Large Italian Army Continues to Be Sent to East Africa in Batches

Naples: A large number of troops will be sent to the front lines in East Africa this week. The dates of their departure have been scheduled as follows:

(1) The steamship "Italia" will depart for the port of Massawa in East Africa tomorrow, carrying 80 officers and 1,184 soldiers belonging to the "Gran Sasso" Division, including a specially trained flamethrower unit. (2) The hospital ship "Neptune" and the steamship "Viminale" will depart for the port of Massawa on the 16th, carrying 32 officers and 884 soldiers from the anti-aircraft unit and motorcycle detachment belonging to the "Gran Sasso" Division. (3) The steamship "Strombolo" and the steamship "Saturn" will depart separately for the Italian Somaliland and Eritrean colonies on the 17th. The former will carry 70 officers and 806 soldiers from the medical unit, and the latter will carry 227 officers and 3,845 soldiers from the engineering battalion. (4) The steamship "Sicilia" will depart for the Italian Somaliland colony on the 18th, carrying 69 officers and 1,900 soldiers from the machine gun battalion. On the same day, the steamship "Pietro Orseolo" will also carry 62 officers and 1,300 soldiers from the medical unit to East Africa. (5) The steamship "Umbria" will depart for the Italian Somaliland colony on the 19th, carrying 62 officers and 2,026 soldiers from various special units. In addition, there are six more steamships fully loaded with ammunition and military supplies that will depart within two days. (Havas Telegram, 15th)

Abyssinian Emperor Expresses Determination to Resist to the End; Minister of War to Personally Go to the Front Lines to Supervise the Battle; Generals Prepare for a Major Counter-Offensive

Addis Ababa: According to a report from our special correspondent Ochsner, the Abyssinian government spokesperson did not deny the reports of the fall of Adwa and the surrender of the entire Tigray province to the Italian army, but reiterated repeatedly that the Emperor is determined not to succumb to force and will not cede an inch of territory. The Abyssinian government neither confirmed nor denied the report of Grazmatch Guffsa, a descendant of the Tigray royal family, surrendering to the Italian army. (Havas Telegram, 14th)

Addis Ababa: According to our special correspondent's investigation, Minister of War Mulugeta will soon depart for Dessie in Wollo province, and may lead a strong force from there to the front lines in northern Abyssinia. Mulugeta is one of the most important figures in Abyssinia and is generally regarded as the Emperor's right-hand man. After he goes to the front lines, the Emperor will follow him, but the date of departure has not yet been determined. Once the departure for the front lines, the Abyssinian army will begin large-scale military operations.

Harar: Abyssinian chieftain Nasibu held a military conference here today, discussing plans for a major counter-offensive against the Italian army in the Worka-Gouden province with his subordinate generals. The generals all claimed that their spears and broadswords, coupled with their personal courage, would be enough to defeat the enemy. The Abyssinians here all believe that the Emperor has imprisoned the Italian ambassador and that the Abyssinian army has won every battle since the start of the war. (National Telegram, 14th)

Addis Ababa: According to responsible sources, several more native soldiers from Italian Eritrea have deserted from the Italian army and crossed the border into Abyssinia near Artisjabo to join General Tsahay. On the southern front, the terrain is very similar to a desert, flat and easy for large-scale troop movements, so the Italian army is advancing very quickly. It is reported that the Italian army is advancing towards the Shebelle River basin in the Worka-Gouden province and has occupied several positions in that province along the way without encountering serious resistance. However, the Abyssinian radio station in Jerro-Goubi, also in the Worka-Gouden province, is still operating as usual, indicating that the Italian army has not yet occupied the area and is only conducting aerial reconnaissance over the area. The Abyssinian government is still very tight-lipped about news from the front lines, so foreigners infer that the situation on the front lines must be very tense. However, according to general observations, although the Italian army is currently advancing, it has not yet made contact with large units of the Abyssinian army, so there have been no large-scale battles between the two sides so far. (Havas Telegram, 15th)

Italian Ambassador Still in Addis Ababa; Confined to a Room, No Different From House Arrest; Abyssinian Ambassador to Italy Ordered to Return Home

Addis Ababa: Foreigners here find the attitude of the Italian ambassador to Abyssinia, Vinci, quite strange. Vinci, along with the Italian army attaché Gagliardini and his loyal servant Ciaffani, has been confined to his residence for five days, refusing to see guests. The British and French ambassadors have attempted to visit him, but have been refused. It has been rumored that the Italian ambassador has departed three times, but each time has failed to materialize. The Italian ambassador originally intended to wait for the staff of the Italian consulate in Magalo to arrive here before departing together, but now that the Magalo consulate staff will arrive here soon, Vinci still has no intention of departing. He is voluntarily confining himself in a foreign country. Some say that he anticipates that the war will end soon and wants to remain in Abyssinia as a peace envoy, but his true intentions are unknown. A Havas reporter met today with the Greek servant who prepares meals for Vinci, who told the reporter, "These three men are confined to a room, and even I have not been able to see them. Each meal, I hand the food to the guard at the door, who passes it on to them. After an hour, I collect the dishes from the guard, and I have never been able to see them." (Havas Telegram, 14th)

Addis Ababa: It is heard that Italian ambassador Count Vinci will depart from here on Wednesday for the town of Haddaama on the Addis Ababa to Djibouti railway, where he will meet with the Italian consular staff who have traveled there from Magalo, and together they will go to the coast. (Reuters Telegram, 15th)

(Rome) Abyssinian Chargé d'Affaires in Rome, Afework, notified Italian Prime Minister Mussolini today that he had received a telegram from the Abyssinian government ordering him to return home immediately. (Reuters Telegram, 14th)

Addis Ababa Scene: Emperor Busy Directing Military Affairs; Residents Calm As Usual

Addis Ababa: It has been ten days since the Italian army invaded Abyssinia, but daily life in the Abyssinian capital has not changed. The natives are as calm as usual. Chieftains from various regions come to the capital every day to pay their respects to the Emperor, and then lead their troops to the northern and southern fronts. Military bands and soldiers parade through the streets one after another, but the people have become accustomed to it and pay little attention. (Havas Telegram, 14th)

Canadian General Election Results: Liberal Party Wins; Conservative Cabinet Shaken

Ottawa: Judging from the current general election results, the Liberal Party has indeed won a major victory. Of the 245 seats in the Canadian House of Commons, the Liberal Party has won 133 seats, the Conservative Party has only 31 seats, and the others have only won 5 seats each. Although Canadian Prime Minister Bennett has been re-elected, 18 of his cabinet members have been defeated. (Reuters Telegram, 15th)

Ottawa: The final results of the Canadian House of Commons election have just been announced. The Liberal Party won 143 seats, the Conservative Party won 35 seats, the Social Credit Party won 8 seats, the Reconstruction Party won 1 seat, the Cooperative Commonwealth Federation won 3 seats, and the Labor-Farmer Party won 1 seat. Tonight, former Prime Minister Mackenzie King, leader of the Liberal Party, declared, "The results of this general election are nothing less than an expression of the national will, ruling in favor of free trade policies at home and abroad, advocating the conclusion of a reciprocal agreement with the United States, and advocating the re-establishment of trade relations with Japan based on mutual benefit. In addition, the election results also demonstrate that the people advocate for the re-establishment of state control over lending and the issuance of banknotes." (Havas Telegram, 14th)

Harbin: Famous Russian Commits Suicide Out of Pessimism; Suicide Note States Inability to Continue Business Ventures

(Harbin) A famous White Russian, Mr. Buyanovsky, committed suicide by hanging himself in the bathroom this afternoon. His suicide note stated that he was pessimistic about the world and unable to continue his business ventures. Mr. Buyanovsky was the president of the Far Eastern Bank and also served as the chairman of the Chamber of Commerce. The suicide note also stated that the bank's deposits were sufficient to cover all debts, and that depositors need not worry about their principal and interest and could rest assured. Mr. Buyanovsky had a very high reputation in Harbin. After the shocking news broke, the entire city was astonished. (Reuters Telegram, 15th)

International Commercial Telegram

——October 15th Reuters Exclusive Commercial Telegram——

Gold and Silver

British Gold: Today's gold price fell by half a penny to 141 shillings and 9 pence.

British Silver: Today's silver market remained very quiet. The spot price was 29 pence 375, and the forward price was 29 pence 4375, the same as yesterday's price. The United States and India bought in, and China sold out.

Exchange Rates

British-American: This morning's foreign exchange market was uneventful, with light trading and little price fluctuation. The opening price for British-American exchange was four dollars and ninety-three and one eighth cents, which was 0.0625 lower than yesterday's closing price for American-British exchange. It rose one eighth of a cent at noon, but fell one eighth of a cent an hour later. The price was four dollars and ninety-four and three eighths cents at 2:00 PM.

British-French: The British-French exchange rate opened one pound higher at 74 francs 41. The price remained unchanged at 2:00 PM.

Cotton and Wheat

American Cotton: The cotton market also trended downwards today. At 1:00 PM, the January contract fell by three points to 6.05.

British Cotton: Although the Liverpool price fell, the New York cotton market opened higher. Dealers continued to buy in, pushing prices higher. However, trading was not very active after the opening, and prices did not continue to rise. Some quarters expect that the Supreme Court will rule most of the regulations of the Agricultural Adjustment Administration as illegal.

British Wheat: The wheat market trended downward again today. At 1:00 PM, the December contract fell by half a penny to six shillings, four pence and seven eighths.

American Wheat: The Chicago wheat market opened three eighths higher this morning, with active trading and rising prices. The results of the Canadian general election were a factor in the rising wheat prices. The coarse grain market was volatile, but prices were also higher.

Rubber

London: The rubber market was stable today. The transaction price for the January-March contract was 6 pence 3125, the same as yesterday's closing price. The price remained unchanged at noon.

New York: The New York rubber market opened slightly higher, but many parties closed out positions, causing the market price to fall by one eighth of a point. Fortunately, the sentiment was still stable, and the decline stopped.

Securities

New York: The stock market opened firm this morning. Although there was some profit-taking when prices were high, the rising trend continued, especially for film stocks. The Dow Jones 30 stocks average opened three quarters of a point higher at 135.37. The prices are as follows:
