Survey Group and Japanese Economic Circles Hold First Informal Meeting

Discuss Finance, Trade, Industrial Raw Materials, etc. Wu Dingchang's Speech Shows Close Agreement on Both Sides' Opinions

Tokyo Communication: After the economic survey group arrived in Tokyo, they were invited by the Japan Economic Federation and the Japan-China Business Association to gather leaders from the banking and business sectors in Tokyo. At 10 a.m. on the 10th, at the Bank Club, the first informal meeting was held to exchange views. All members of the group attended. The Japanese attendees included: Fukai, President of the Bank of Japan; Kodama, President of Yokohama Specie Bank; Kato, President of the Bank of Korea; Akashi, President of Dai-Ichi Bank; Kikumoto, Chairman of Mitsui Bank; Yūki, President of Industrial Bank of Japan; Yasuda, President of Bank of Taiwan; Seta, Chairman of Mitsubishi Bank; Mori, Vice President of Yasuda Bank; Inoue, Chairman of Mitsui Bussan; Kushida, Director of Mitsubishi; Miyake, Chairman of 大仓; Kadono, Vice President; Otani, Vice President of Nippon Yusen; Gō Seinosuke, Chairman of Tokyo Electric Light; Fukao, President of Nisshin Kisen; and Ōfuchi, Director of Mantetsu's Tokyo branch, a total of twenty-seven people. The scope of discussion was roughly divided into four areas: finance, trade, industrial products, and raw materials. The opinions of both parties were very harmonious and continued until 2:30 p.m., and it was agreed to continue detailed discussions within days. At 3:00 p.m., a tea party was held at the Foreign Minister's official residence, hosted by Hirota and the two vice ministers and bureau chiefs. During the meeting, there was casual conversation. In the evening at 6:00 p.m., a welcoming dinner party was hosted by the aforementioned two business groups at the Industry Club. Leaders from the financial and business sectors attended, and Ambassador Jiang and counselors and secretaries from the embassy were invited to participate. At the beginning of the dinner, the host, 乡城之助, Chairman of the Economic Federation, delivered a speech, saying that "the relationship between China and Japan is close, and there should be possibilities for economic cooperation. Moreover, at this time, countries around the world are seeking economic cooperation. There is a particular need for economic cooperation between China and Japan. Unfortunately, the political relationship has not been satisfactory for many years, and I feel very sorry. This time, leaders of the economic circles on the front line of China have come to our country, which is a good opportunity. I hope that this opportunity can be used to achieve the goal of economic cooperation between the two countries," and so on. Later, Wu Dingchang, the head of the survey group, delivered a long speech (the original text is recorded later), which won warm applause from the entire venue. Both parties considered it satisfactory, and the atmosphere was unusually harmonious. After that, there was free conversation, and both parties unanimously advocated proceeding with the organization of a cooperation mechanism. Specific plans are being discussed. It wasn't until about 10 p.m. that everyone parted happily.

Wu Dingchang said in his speech, "We had intended to come to Japan several years ago to investigate the economy in preparation for cooperation. However, after the launch, it was not permitted by the political environment between the two countries, and it was delayed and failed to materialize. It is extremely regrettable. However, our aspirations have finally come to fruition today. It is so pleasant to be able to gather with influential people from both China and Japan, exchange opinions, and discuss economic cooperation between the two countries. Therefore, we firmly believe that the relationship between China and Japan is created by natural forces. Anyone who tries to cut off this relationship by artificial means is doing something useless and harmful to both sides. However, these useless and harmful events occur from time to time, which is enough to delay the progress of economic cooperation between the two countries. This is a clear fact. Therefore, while we are doing our best in economic cooperation between the two countries, we cannot but sincerely hope that the two countries will pay attention to improving the political environment in the future, so that we can carry out economic cooperation. In today's world, when the economic power of international cooperation is expanding, if countries A and B can sincerely seek economic cooperation, it will naturally be the mutual happiness of the people of both countries, not to mention more. Especially for China and Japan, one has already advanced to become an industrial country, and the other is still an agricultural country. There are few points of conflict in the products of the two countries. Moreover, for the few conflicting products, such as cotton cloth, silk, tea, and matches, there is still room for consultation to avoid competition, so as to make up for the deficiencies with the surpluses. In terms of economy, it is originally a mutually beneficial matter. In addition, due to geographical relations, there is no reason to abandon what is near and seek what is far if the goods needed between China and Japan can be supplied to each other. Therefore, China to Japan and Japan to China, from the standpoint of international economics, stand on an advantageous position that no other country can compete with. It is easy to seek cooperation in this position. However, in order to make economic cooperation between China and Japan a concrete fact, there must be concrete research and concrete plans. This great cause cannot be accomplished by a few empty words. This requires the efforts of comrades from both countries. Although we are weak, we dare not refuse the labor for the sake of the economic future of the two countries. There is an argument here that the success of China-Japan economic cooperation depends entirely on whether there is sincerity between the two countries. This statement is seemingly right but not. In general, nothing can be successful without sincerity, not to mention economic cooperation. However, how can anything be successful with sincerity but without a plan, not to mention economic cooperation? Empty talk about sincerity is too abstract. Therefore, we believe that the success of China-Japan economic cooperation depends primarily on whether there is an appropriate and feasible plan. If there is, then those without sincerity will inevitably generate sincerity, and those with sincerity can increase sincerity. We dare to assert that if the cooperation plan is good and mutually beneficial to the national economies of the two countries, no one in the two countries can give it皮对. Moreover, now that there are knowledgeable people in both countries who are sincere about economic cooperation between the two countries, how can the cooperation plan be achieved by the simple and abstract principle of advocating Japanese capital, using Japanese technology, and exchanging Chinese raw materials for Japanese industrial products? We must recognize that economic cooperation between the two countries is a century-old undertaking, and it is by no means for temporary gains. It is only possible to cooperate with some Japanese capital, hire a few Japanese technicians, and increase Sino-Japanese exports and imports by a few percentages in the short term, and cannot maintain its smooth progress permanently, so it is impossible to talk about economic cooperation between the two countries. China-Japan economic cooperation must establish a concept that promoting the general economic development of Japan is beneficial to China, and promoting the general economic development of China is beneficial to Japan. Each should cooperate and help each other for the sake of its own interests, and then can it conform to the true meaning of economic cooperation. We dare to assert that those in the Japanese economic circle with vision have long believed that the development of China's national economy is beneficial to the Japanese national economy without a doubt. Based on this concept, research on the issue of capital cooperation between the two countries, technical assistance, especially the entire trade issue between the two countries, will surely lead to the discovery of a good and concrete plan, sweeping away the previous suspicions and establishing a foundation for sincere cooperation. We must clearly acknowledge that the reason why the economic problems between China and Japan have not been able to get on the track of cooperation so far is entirely due to a misunderstanding that the economic interests of the two countries conflict. Based on this concept, each uses strategies, one side actively conducts, and the other side passively resists, resulting in mutual accusations of insincerity and difficult cooperation. If we want to truly do our best for the permanent peace of the two countries and put economic cooperation into practice, we must have a painful realization about the past. After the Manchurian Incident, in the past three years, China's international trade volume has decreased sharply. Compared with 1934 and 1931, the import and export volume has decreased by more than one-half. Japan has given up its position as the top place in China's international trade table, which it has continued to hold since 1910. Moreover, in these two years, imports have exceeded exports by about 2.1 billion yuan. China's export of gold and silver to make up for the trade deficit is about 700 million yuan. If China's national economy is not prosperous, what is its impact on international trade, especially on Sino-Japanese trade? It is as clear as looking at the palm of your hand, and there is no need to say more. Therefore, for Japan's sake, especially for China's sake, we cannot but work hard for the two countries to seek economic cooperation, so as to develop the economy of the Chinese people and further develop the economy of the Japanese people. We came here with this great mission, wanting to conduct factual investigations and listen to opinions from all parties. First, we present a general outline, and we ask for your opinions. As for various concrete methods, we cannot exhaust them at this moment with one word. We also plan to have more opportunities for both parties to conduct detailed research separately, negotiate to avoid conflicts, cooperate to carry out non-conflicts, find ways to alleviate suspicions, and implement them immediately without suspicions, and make continuous efforts to discover a good plan for the entire economic cooperation between the two countries. We believe that China-Japan economic cooperation is inevitable and possible, and it depends on our efforts.

Wuchang Headquarters Closed - Remnant Bandits in Hubei Province Have Been Eliminated

Hankou Communication: Chairman Chiang, because the Gan bandits fled west and the situation in Sichuan and Hunan was once tense, and for the convenience of command, specially moved the Nanchang Headquarters to Wuchang, with Zhang Xueliang as the director of the headquarters. It was formally established on March 1. At that time, Chairman Chiang had already come to Hankou from Gan. The senior personnel of the headquarters were all selected and appointed by Chiang. Later, Chairman Chiang went to Sichuan to supervise the suppression, which lasted for several months. Zhu De, Mao Zedong, Xu Xiangqian, and Zhang Guotao's bandits were all unable to gain a foothold in Sichuan and fled one after another, while He Long and Xiao Ke's remnant bandits were still scurrying in the border areas of Sichuan, Hunan, and Hubei. The center of gravity of bandit suppression was shifted to the Shaanxi-Gansu area in the north and to the upper reaches of the Yangtze River in the south. In order to meet the needs of the situation, Chairman Chiang specially established a headquarters in Xi'an, a headquarters in Sichuan, and an administrative office in Yichang, respectively, to supervise the suppression nearby. At this point, the Wuchang Headquarters was no longer necessary, so he ordered preparations to be made for its closure. Zhang Xueliang, the director of the headquarters, had already gone to Xi'an to take up his new post as deputy commander. The Wuchang Headquarters was in charge of Chief of Staff Qian Dajun, who is currently handling the closure. It is heard that the closure will be completed on the 20th, and the staff from various places will be transferred to work in the Xi'an Headquarters, Sichuan Headquarters, and Yichang Administrative Office.

In the sound of the closure of the headquarters, let's review the achievements of bandit suppression in Hubei Province. There are almost no large remnant bandits in the entire province. There are no traces of bandits in eastern, central, and northern Hubei. The He bandits in western Hubei retreat as soon as they commit a crime, and the southern Hubei area has also been cleared. According to Chen Jicheng, the commander of the bandit suppression in the border area of Hunan, Hubei, and Jiangxi and the newly appointed garrison commander of Wuhan, the counties in southern Hubei, because they are adjacent to Hunan and Jiangxi, have been ravaged by remnant bandits for a long time in the past. Since the national army has worked hard to advance and suppress them, the large gangs have been wiped out. Now the bandit leader Xu Yegang has been beheaded, and the scattered bandits have dispersed. Therefore, the southern Hubei area is extremely calm. Only in Pingliu, Hunan, there are hundreds of bandits lurking in the mountains, but they are just struggling to survive. As for the recovered counties in southern Hubei, they have now emerged from the post-disaster period and are seeking to recuperate. The harvest in each county this year is good, and the vitality is expected to be restored. As for the border headquarters, it is still located in Puqi, and I plan to come and go to Puqi and Hankou to preside over it in the future. (14th)

Merchants and Businessmen from Six Provinces in Hubei Strongly Reject Water Police Fees

Believe that the law is heavy, the administration is complicated, and it is burdensome to both superiors and subordinates. Call for revisions. The wording is very indignant.

Hankou Communication: Ship merchants from six provinces, including Hunan, Hubei, Jiangxi, Sichuan, Henan, and Shaanxi, believe that the Hubei Water Police Department has promulgated ship registration regulations that are not connected with the central legal system and the administration of various provinces, resulting in a duplicate registration that harms the people, and the implementing personnel deliberately create difficulties, which is particularly inconvenient for merchants. Therefore, they have specially selected representatives to submit petitions to the headquarters, provincial party department, provincial government, the supervisory commissioner's office of Hunan and Hubei, and the provincial tax administration committee, urging them to make revisions. The wording is very sharp. The main points are divided into three points: (1) Police and navigation administration, duplicate registration. Ships are based on rivers, which cannot be limited to one province. The province's standalone laws should pay attention to the central laws and regulations system and avoid conflicts with the regulations of neighboring provinces. The police can only register ships operating in the local docks within their duties. For ships that have already been registered in neighboring provinces and other commercial ports, they can only implement inspection. It is impossible to confuse navigation administration as one. The central China route runs through ten provinces, including Guangdong, Guangxi, Hunan, Hubei, Anhui, Jiangsu, Sichuan, Jiangxi, Henan, and Shaanxi. If Hubei Province issues flags and licenses, it cannot prohibit other provinces from imitating them, with one ship flying so many flags and licenses. Although the procedures are cumbersome, they are chaotic and undisciplined, which will lose the national image to foreigners. This is the first point that should be revised in the regulations. (2) Registration fees, similar to taxes. Ship registration is the same in nature as the household registration handled by the land police. There is no reason to take additional expenses from the people. The regulations stipulate that old boats of 20 or more stones should be charged 3 jiao, and those less than 20 stones should be charged 5 fen. The fees are so different for the same license and the same procedure. What is this if not a new tax rule? The water police collect fees, and the financial department lists them as revenue. What is this if not collecting taxes in the name of the police? The price of each flag is 2 jiao, regardless of its value. The price of a license is different for the same item, regardless of its uniformity. Although it is not harsh to pay 7 jiao per boat per year, it is already close to miscellaneous. The end of gathering cannot be opened, and if it is opened, it cannot be cleaned up. Making money in an improper way, other provinces will follow suit, and the people's burden will be increased. In terms of business, there is a business tax, and in terms of books and documents, there is a stamp tax. There is a navigation tax, and the police also have a tax. At a time when the economy is depressed, the people's economy is bankrupt. What ability do they have to make unnecessary supplies? This is the second point that registration should be free. (3) Poor regulations, difficult registration. Boat households apply for registration, fill out forms, provide guarantees, pay fees, verify guarantees, inspect boats, and receive flags and licenses. The procedures are extremely troublesome, so it often takes more than ten days, and at least a week, to obtain them. Ship merchants operate and take advantage of opportunities. Recently, many people have missed opportunities due to difficult registration. There are also those who could not bear to lose the opportunity and drove out of the river secretly, and encountered a hurricane and capsized. Water police officers and staff originally have no tea fee regulations. In order to avoid difficulties, they have to pay each other tea fees. This is the third point that troubles should be eliminated. The Ministry of Communications' Ship Registration Law has no duplicate registration for the registration of seaports and commercial transport. The fees for registration and licensing of docks are also strictly limited. Under the central administrative rule, how can Hubei Province create its own atmosphere, break the established rules of the police, and open a precedent for harshness and miscellaneousness? The representatives are entrusted by ship merchants from six provinces and should submit a petition to your camp department. It is hoped that you will allow and order revisions to remove the cumbersome and harshness, so as to facilitate commercial transportation.

Jiangxi Education Circles Dedicate Airplanes to the National Government

More than 10,000 students from 74 schools attended. The National Government sent Chen Qingyun to receive the plane and give a speech.

Nanchang Communication: The Jiangxi circles, because of the severity of the national crisis and the urgency of foreign insults, specially formed the Aviation Salvation Committee, and separately donated funds to purchase aircraft for self-defense. Then, Chen Qingyun, Director of the Aviation Committee, gave a speech on behalf of the National Government. The speech briefly stated that the modern era is a three-dimensional war, and the air force occupies a major position. Our country's air force is extremely young, and all sectors of the people must provide spiritual and material assistance to build the air force so that it can stand on its own in the dangerous international situation and not be exploited by others. In addition, Chairman Chiang's speech said, "The Jiangxi Education Aircraft is scheduled to hold a donation ceremony and naming ceremony, which shows the sincere patriotism of the Jiangxi education circles, which is commendable and gratifying. We should actively transport them and encourage the wish to be like tasting the bitter gall and lying on the new grass. We should be diligent and tireless and strive to contribute to the Ling Han's merits. There are high hopes for the many scholars." After the speech was over, Liu Heng (principal of 女中), Yan Jinfu from middle school, and Lai Caisheng from primary school, representatives of the teachers and students, carried the aircraft authorization certificate and respectfully presented the aircraft to the National Government. After Chen Qingyun, the representative of the National Government, accepted it, he bowed to each other. Then, the curtain on the head of the aircraft was unveiled, and Xiong Suixiu and Hu Zhaowen, female students from 一中, threw bottles at No. 1 and No. 2, respectively. The two aircraft took off in formation amidst the loud music and thunderous applause. At the same time, the five fighter jets of Longhai, Jiaoji, Zhengtai, and Pinghan also took off in formation to perform various stunts. The students threw their hats into the air and cheered, and six student representatives were selected to take a plane around the city for a week before dispersing at about 5 p.m. (October 10th)

Large Export of Anhui Rice

Over 900,000 Shi Exported from Wuhu, and Another Million Shi from Other Places

Wuhu Correspondence: Since the 15th year of the Republic, Anhui Province has been affected by the economic decline in the country. Although it has substantial agricultural resources, the production and sales are not well-regulated. The dumping of foreign goods and rice has not only hurt farmers due to low grain prices, but also stopped the millions of shi of rice that were previously shipped to Guangdong, Chaozhou, and other regions. As a result, rural areas are declining daily, and the overall economy and political construction of the province are also exhausted and difficult. Although there were widespread floods in the Yangtze and Huai Rivers this year, southern and central Anhui were minimally affected, and the agricultural harvest of rice was abundant. The export market is also showing signs of recovery. In recent months, the amount of rice directly shipped from Wuhu has reached over 900,000 shi. The amount shipped by sail from Wuwei, Hexian, Dangtu, and other counties also exceeds one million shi. In addition, the by-products and miscellaneous grains, such as rapeseed, rapeseed cake, honey dates, Xuan paper, eggs, cotton, tung oil, etc., shipped from the Jiangnan Railway and Yangtze River by steamer and sail to Tianjin-Pukou and Xun-Han, are also substantial. This is a rare phenomenon in recent years. Regarding rice prices, since the new grain has been harvested, they have gradually risen. From around six yuan, it has recently increased to seven yuan and six or seven jiao for superior rice, and seven yuan and two or three jiao for medium rice. Rice boats from Sanhe, Lujiang, and other places are flocking to Wuhu to sell their rice, with daily sales reaching over 10,000 bags. Iron boats are also constantly coming and going, which has brought prosperity to merchants and is quite promising. (14th)

Robbery and Murder of a Farmhand in Lumu

At around 1:00 AM on the 15th, several armed bandits suddenly arrived at Xu Zhuang in Lumu Township and broke into the home of villager Zhu Yuanhe, robbing at will. They stole over 130 silver dollars. One of the bandits, named Shi Xiaodi, was grabbed by a farmhand, Mr. Lu, from the Zhu family. Unexpectedly, another bandit pulled out a pistol and shot the farmhand in the back, hitting a vital spot. He died from the injuries shortly after. The bandit Shi Xiaodi was captured by neighbors, while the other bandits escaped. It was later learned that the leader of the bandits was an out-of-towner, Chuan Laowozi, who lived in Lumu Town and has now disappeared. The victim reported the incident to the local police station in the morning, and the captured bandit Shi Xiaodi was taken to the station for interrogation. At the same time, a strict search was ordered to bring Chuan Laowozi to justice. The local prosecutor's office sent personnel to the village for inspection that afternoon.

Local News

International Trade Bureau Announces Economic Situation in the First Half of the Year

Frequent Disasters Affect Agricultural Losses Significantly; Tight Credit and Shrinking Credit Stifle Industry and Commerce

Shanghai Times Agency reports: According to the International Trade Bureau, the general economic situation in China in the first half of this year has not escaped the panic. Agricultural production suffered significant losses due to frequent disasters. Industry and commerce suffered from the continued decline in prices, and factories and shops were closed or bankrupt. As for finance, although there has been some return of silver, the tight credit situation remains the same as before. However, various measures taken by the government this year to save the financial panic and revitalize transportation and industry have been implemented one after another. The Shanghai Times Agency reporter interviewed He Bingxian, Director of the Bureau, yesterday, who provided the following information:

Frequent Natural Disasters and Reduced Production

Last year, China suffered particularly severe natural disasters, and agricultural products suffered losses. This year, continuing the disasters of the previous year, a spring famine occurred in the spring, followed by floods and typhoons. The floods caused by the Yellow River in North China and the Pearl River in South China were particularly serious. At the same time, floods also occurred in the Yangtze River. Under this widespread disaster situation, it is difficult to expect a bumper harvest of agricultural crops in the first half of the year. Wheat harvests were good in Jiangsu and Zhejiang, but poor in Hebei, Shandong, and Henan. However, as a whole, the wheat planting area in the first half of the year increased by about 7% compared to last year. As for rice, water and drought alternated. Although there are no estimates yet, its output will inevitably be affected by natural disasters. According to the first estimate of the China Cotton Industry Statistics Association, cotton production will be reduced compared with the previous year. In terms of tea, black tea production is better, while green tea is somewhat inferior. In terms of silk, Jiangsu Province produced about 300,000 dan of spring cocoons, and Zhejiang Province could produce 18,000 dan of silk.

Industry and Commerce Decline Further

In the first half of this year, Chinese industry and commerce deteriorated further. Prices continued to fall, with a trend of getting worse. Under this catastrophic price situation, industry and commerce were unable to maintain themselves. As a result, factories were closing one after another, and shops were declaring liquidation one after another. In terms of various industries, cotton yarn prices were not good, and the low price and slow sales of yarn were the most worrying. The reduction of working hours and the closure of yarn factories have become an unprecedented crisis. As for the silk industry, the first half of this year showed no improvement in the spring season, but gradually improved in the summer. Sales in Europe have shown significant development. The flour industry fluctuated, mainly due to the tightening of Chinese finance and the excessive import of foreign rice. Although the match industry has not seen any recovery, the organization of the Six Provinces Match Merchants Joint Business Office by the Great China Company and others to implement production and sales cooperation is not necessarily a good phenomenon. In addition, the Ministry of Industry established an alcohol factory in March, opening the first precedent for the National Government to directly run industries.

Economic Panic and Financial Construction

In terms of finance, this year continued the outflow of silver from last year's frenzy. Economic and financial panic led to various phenomena. From the surface, silver has gradually stabilized since the beginning of this year and has even returned to some extent, but in reality, the tight credit situation and shrinking credit are still extremely dangerous. As the financial situation became increasingly tight, there were repeated reports of silver shops declaring liquidation. However, there were several things in the Chinese financial community in the first half of this year that were worth noting, namely, the establishment of six new banks nationwide, the establishment of 63 new branch banks, the government's issuance of 100 million yuan of financial bonds, the postal savings bureau's implementation of rural lending, and the implementation of centralized collection and settlement of bills and notes by the silver industry. All of these are financial constructions in the midst of financial panic.

Overview of Fiscal Conditions in the First Half of the Year

The budget for the 24th year of the Republic of China had an expenditure and revenue of 957,154,006 yuan. The government reduced all unnecessary expenditures this year, while education, diplomacy, construction, and industry expenses were all increased. The issuance of public bonds this year included 100 million yuan of financial bonds, 100 million yuan of customs bonds, and 13 million yuan of local bonds issued by various provinces and cities. The most important fiscal measures in this period were the announcement of reduced export taxes, the formulation of income tax principles, and the proposed establishment of an inheritance tax law. The estimated revenue from customs, salt, stamp, and tobacco and alcohol taxes this year is lower than last year, while government and construction expenses are increasing daily, so it is necessary to open up new sources of revenue. In addition, the continued abolition of harsh and miscellaneous taxes and the implementation of fixed county budgets are also important aspects of this year's fiscal measures.

As a result, forty votes were cast, and Jin Zongcheng was elected as a member of the Public Works Department Land Committee with thirty-eight votes. Refreshments were served at the end. The meeting adjourned at 6:00 PM. The association sent a letter to the Public Works Department of the Shanghai International Settlement last night, stating, "To the Director, this is to inform you that since Mr. Wang Boyuan, the member of the Land Committee of your department for the years 1935-1936 of the Republic of China, has resigned, Mr. Jin Zongcheng was elected by ballot at the general meeting on October 15 to fill the term of the aforementioned member. In addition to notifying Mr. Jin Zongcheng, we are writing to inform you for your information. We have duly noted your letter of October 9. "

Jin's Biography

Jin Zongcheng, a native of Zhenhai, Zhejiang, is 41 years old. He served as the Chief Accountant of the Jiangsu Bank and practiced at the Irving Trust Company in the United States. He is currently a director and business department manager of the Shanghai Commercial and Savings Bank, a director of the New New Company, a director of the China Travel Service, a director of the Gongqin Iron Factory, and a director of the China United Assurance Company. Mr. Jin also served as the manager of the foreign exchange department, the manager of the inspection department, and the manager of the branch management department of the Shanghai Bank.

The Flood Relief Association Holds a General Donation and Publishes a Letter to Compatriots, Asking All Sectors to Donate Generously

Central News Agency reports: The Shanghai Municipal Joint Relief Association for Flood Disasters in Various Provinces stated that this year's flash floods in the Jiang, Huai, He, and Han Rivers have caused disasters one after another. The disaster victims are everywhere, and their misery is unprecedented in nearly a hundred years. Therefore, they are appealing to all parties for donations to save the people in distress. In order to achieve significant and macro effects and gather strength from everyone, the association has entrusted various banks, money shops, companies, and shops in Shanghai to raise general donations, divided into seven categories: one jiao, two jiao, four jiao, one yuan, two yuan, four yuan, and ten yuan, to be donated voluntarily by everyone. The association's letter to compatriots is found, recorded as follows: "1. Our country has suffered frequent disasters in recent years. This year, since the beginning of summer, continuous rain has caused flash floods in the Jiang, Huai, He, and Han Rivers, causing disasters in more than ten provinces, including Lu, E, Wan, and Gan. There are hundreds of thousands of disaster victims, more than in the 20th year of the Republic. The victims are emaciated and huddled on the roadside, and their misery is unprecedented. As autumn turns to winter, we look at those poor people who are displaced, hungry, and cold, waiting for rescue. Compassion is in everyone's heart. Putting ourselves in their place, how can we not be saddened? Shanghai is the richest area in the country, but in recent years, the market has been sluggish, and all industries are in decline. In addition, the decline of the rural economy in the interior has had an impact. The prosperity of the past is almost like the setting sun. However, even though society is poor, it should show the spirit of mutual rescue and self-rescue among Chinese people. Moreover, today's Shanghai society has inevitable luxuries and consumption. With a little frugality, there is still some extra capacity. We live in Shanghai in peace, with clothes and food. How can we not have compassion and care for our compatriots in various places who are groaning in hardship in the floods and after the floods, needing clothes, food, and medicine? This year's disaster area is vast, and there are many disaster victims. Without unified donations and mass contributions, it is impossible to overcome the difficulties. Therefore, the association is holding a general donation for flood disasters, divided into seven categories: one jiao, two jiao, four jiao, one yuan, two yuan, four yuan, and ten yuan. We hope that all compatriots and people from all walks of life in the city will generously donate, seeking to do their best, regardless of the amount, and embrace the principle of rescuing others as if they were drowning, saving people is saving oneself, and contributing actively. The country, society, and the future of the nation depend on it. " In addition, the association received eight yuan, nine jiao, and four fen from Pujisi Temple; one thousand two hundred and eighty-two yuan and six jiao from nine households, including Yang Xianxiang; ten yuan from Xu Fu's memorial aid to Zhen Daoxian; thirty-two yuan from the Central Bank on behalf of the Allied Bank; twenty yuan from Fang Jinren; one hundred and forty-six yuan and two jiao and nine fen from Wang Dezhong, Chen Minsong, and other representatives of Chinese colleagues at the Tengyue Customs; and one hundred and sixty-two yuan from Wang Songqing and other four households collected by the Shanghai Bank.

The New Voice News Agency reports that the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company is a giant of China's self-operated shipping industry, founded in the eleventh year of the Tongzhi reign (1872). Silk Factories Running Out of Raw Materials Due to Zhejiang Province's Monopoly on Cocoon Purchases. Guilds and Labor Unions are Appealing for Relief

This year, due to Zhejiang Province's monopoly on cocoon purchases, Shanghai silk factories are experiencing a severe shortage of raw materials and extreme panic. The silk reeling labor union has decided to appeal to the central government for relief. Details are as follows:

Unqualified Registration

Since Zhejiang Province's Department of Construction monopolized spring cocoon purchases this year, silk factories in Shanghai have been affected. Therefore, the number of silk factories that have started operations this year has sharply decreased compared to previous years. When the Zhejiang Department of Construction's Silkworm and Silk Monopoly Committee handled autumn cocoons, it divided the entire province into ten cocoon zones, stipulating that they could be openly purchased, but a separate regulation for registering cocoon businesses was established, with harsh content (for example, eight cocoon stoves could be registered, but they must be wood-fired stoves, etc.). Therefore, of those Shanghai silk factories that went to purchase, only seven businesses were registered, and the rest were unqualified.

Raw Materials Cut Off

This year, Zhejiang produced over 20,000 dan of dried cocoons, most of which were purchased by Wuxi Yongtai (as Yongtai had signed a contract with the Department of Construction at a high price to monopolize sales). The rest was preferentially purchased by Zhejiang silk factories. In total, Shanghai silk factories purchased less than 3,000 dan of Zhejiang cocoons. At the same time, Zhejiang Province produced more cocoons than Jiangsu Province. After Shanghai silk factories were deemed unqualified for registration in Zhejiang Province, Jiangsu Province's businesses were also monopolized by factories from other places, resulting in a cutoff of raw materials.

Request for Relief

Due to the shortage of raw materials, the Hubu Huyuanji, Houji, Yongji, and Xieyuan factories in Zhabei have announced shutdowns. Currently, there are still 20 factories in Zhabei, 9 in Hongkou, 2 in the concession, and 2 in Nanshi Longhua, for a total of 31 factories. On average, they need 400 dan of dried cocoons per day for reeling, but the 3,000 dan of Zhejiang cocoons can only last for one week. Therefore, silk factories will all shut down this year. The silk factory guild has decided to hold a meeting in the next few days to discuss how to deal with the Zhejiang Province monopoly. The four district six division two silk reeling labor union believes that 20,000 workers are about to lose their jobs, so it has decided to jointly appeal to the central government for relief.

Factories Must Register Promptly: Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Issues Notice

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce yesterday issued a notice to its members in various industries, stating that on the 14th of this month, it received Instruction No. 8168 from the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs, which cited Instruction No. 1543 from the Municipal Government, which cited Consultation No. 13214 from the Ministry of Industry, which stated that the Ministry had previously amended and promulgated the Regulations for Factory Registration, which had no compulsory registration provision, in May of this year, and requested compliance. However, nearly three months have passed, and the number of factories applying for registration is still very small, and the overall situation of domestic industry is still unclear, making it impossible to carry out any industrial administration. Therefore, another consultation is being made to urge prompt registration. If there is further delay, strict enforcement will be carried out in accordance with Article 12 of the Regulations for Factory Registration, in order to emphasize the importance of official orders. In response to this, it was noted that the amended Regulations for Factory Registration had been previously forwarded, and now the previous consultation is being forwarded again, ordering the bureau to comply and promptly forward it to unregistered factories to comply as well, applying for registration with the bureau before the end of this month, and paying the certificate fee of one yuan and stamp tax of two jiao in accordance with the regulations for registration, and not to wait and see and make a mistake. Having received this, it is noted that the chamber has already been ordered to issue a notice and urge compliance with the law, and now the previous consultation is being forwarded again, and the chamber is instructed to forward it to the factories under its jurisdiction for prompt registration, without further delay.

Notice from the Bureau of Social Affairs

The Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs, in order to handle the registration of various factories, collects certificate fees in accordance with regulations, and registration applicants must pay in person at the bureau. It has not sent personnel to collect fees from various factories. The bureau is deeply concerned that someone may be posing as its staff, and specially notified all factories yesterday to be vigilant, stating that in this factory registration, in addition to posting notices in newspapers and separately ordering and instructing the Municipal Chamber of Commerce and various factory groups to comply, the bureau has not separately sent letters or personnel to urge compliance. The certificate fee and stamp tax totaling one yuan and two jiao collected in accordance with regulations should be paid by the registration bureau to the bureau to obtain a formal receipt, and the bureau has not sent personnel to collect fees from various factories. If anyone is falsely using the bureau's name to swindle and cheat, they should be immediately handed over to the nearest public security agency for investigation, and the bureau should be notified as well. This notice.

Article 15 of Chapter 5, Organization, states that "The Reserve shall have 15 executive committee members, 5 of whom shall be ex officio members, namely the current standing committee members of this guild, 5 shall be nominated from the current executive committee members of this guild, and the remaining 5 shall be elected from the basic member representatives, with a term of two years." The first executive committee meeting will be held soon, and according to Article 16 of the articles of association, "The Reserve shall have 5 standing committee members, who shall be elected by the executive committee members," and Article 17, "The Reserve shall have a chairman, who shall be elected by the standing committee members."

Powers of the Committee Members

A reporter from the New Voice News Agency inquired at the Money Reserve and learned that Article 21 of Chapter 6, Executive Committee, of the amended articles of association states that the powers of the executive committee are as follows: (1) Matters concerning the collection, valuation, safekeeping, and disposal of quasi-property and cash; (2) Matters concerning the design of basic members and members; (3) Matters concerning the review and approval of various rules of this Reserve; (4) Matters concerning the preparation of budget estimates; (5) Matters concerning the review and approval of budget estimates. Article 26 of Chapter 7, Inspection Committee, states that the powers of the inspection committee are as follows: (1) Matters concerning the inspection of all account books and records of this Reserve; (2) Matters concerning the inventory of reserve assets.

French Concession Taxpayers Association Holds Joint Meeting of Directors and Supervisors Yesterday

Vegetable Vendors on Kangti Road Petitioned Chairman Du Yesterday, Requesting Him to Negotiate with the French Authorities to Resume Business

The French Concession Chinese Taxpayers Association convened a joint meeting of directors and supervisors at 3:00 PM yesterday. Those present included Du Yuesheng, Zhang Yin, Shang Muzi, Gu Wensheng, Huang Xianggu, Tong Lizhang, Gong Jingdang, Sun Gengshan (represented by Wu Guowei), Dong Kechang, Qu Zhenhua, Dai Chunfeng, Zhu Shengmao, Jin Liren, Du Gang, Li Weiliang, Tong Qinfu, Su Gongxuan (represented by Dai), Mao Yun (represented by Huang), Xu Xiuting, and 19 others.

Chairman's Report

The meeting was conducted according to etiquette, chaired by Du Yuesheng and recorded by Shao Bingyuan. First, the chairman reported on the following matters: (1) Reporting that the association received 5,000 yuan in regular expenses subsidized by the Ministry of Finance of the National Government, and there is still 10,000 yuan, with 5,000 yuan to be received every four months, totaling three times a year; (2) The receiving agency is the National Treasury Bureau of the Ministry of Finance, located on the Central Bank building.

Matters for Discussion

(1) Regarding the amendment of the association's articles of association, Commissioner Huang Xianggu has drafted the original text and sent it to the commissioners. After the commissioners have amended it, they will gather opinions and set another date for the Commissioners of the Zun case to pass and implement it; (2) Regarding the re-election of the association's fourth committee, it was resolved that it should be completed this year; (3) Regarding the decision on the association's regular expenses, it was resolved that it should be temporarily set at 500 yuan to 600 yuan per month; (4) Regarding the decision on the association's office staff, it was resolved that there should be one French secretary, one Chinese secretary, and several staff members. Other office staff and salaries will be discussed and decided by the standing committee members, and the chairman will report and implement it; (5) The work and office hours of the association's staff will be determined separately, but the most important thing is that a copy of the events of each meeting of the Municipal Council should be sent to the association first, and the French secretary should translate it into Chinese on schedule and send it to the commissioners for reference; (6) Regarding the relocation of the association's office, it was resolved that the office should be located on the second floor of the Zhonghui Building, and the relocation procedures should be carried out. Shang Mujang, Huang Xianggu, Long Jingyan, Zhu Shengmao, and Jin Liren were nominated to purchase all the necessary equipment, etc. After the above resolutions were discussed, just as the meeting was about to adjourn, more than 30 vegetable vendors who had been banned by the French police on Kangti Road, supporting the old and carrying the young, arrived at the meeting, knelt down and begged, and petitioned Chairman Du for relief. Chairman Du came forward to comfort the vegetable vendors and asked them to wait for mediation. They then left happily.

Petition

Respectfully presented, the vegetable vendors have been banned by the French police from setting up stalls on Kangti Road for more than a month. They previously petitioned your association to uphold justice and provide assistance, and 51 shops on Kangti Road also jointly wrote to your association requesting negotiations. However, many days have passed since then, and we have not heard any expression from your association, and the requests of the shops have not been replied to. The vegetable vendors have lost their livelihoods and have been running around and appealing all day long, but have not been able to resume business. More than a dozen vendors have been found to be starving. If they cannot resume business, it is feared that the entire group will starve, which will have a significant impact on society. Therefore, we are submitting a continuation of the petition, requesting that your association investigate the previous petition and allow negotiations to be carried out.

Hu Wenhu Talks About the Need to Establish a Liaison Organization for Overseas Chinese to Promote Industrial and Commercial Development... Guiding Overseas Chinese in Allied Countries

According to the Central News Agency, Hu Wenhu, a leader of overseas Chinese in Southeast Asia, led a team of overseas Chinese from Malaya back to China to participate in the National Games, which was warmly welcomed by all sectors of society. After arriving in Shanghai, Hu was very busy with social engagements, but he took the time to go to the sports field every day to watch the competition, which shows that he pays great attention to sports. The reporter met him on the platform yesterday and took the opportunity to talk with him and ask for his impressions of this visit. Hu was sincere and made very meaningful remarks to the reporter. According to Hu, he led the team back to China to participate in the National Games, and he was warmly welcomed by all sectors of society, which is very touching. From this, it can be seen that the Chinese government and compatriots care for overseas Chinese in every possible way. However, in the past, overseas Chinese were far away from their motherland, and were very isolated from the situation in their motherland. There have been times when overseas Chinese who returned to China were oppressed and bullied by local bullies, corrupt officials, and corrupt bureaucrats, which almost made overseas Chinese regard returning to China as a dangerous path. Even those who wanted to return to China to invest and start businesses were afraid to try easily due to various obstacles. Domestic compatriots have the same feeling towards overseas Chinese. Therefore, if we want to communicate the voices of China and Southeast Asia and connect the feelings of overseas Chinese, we must further have a liaison agency or organization. It is Hu's opinion that if we can unite enthusiastic people from the industrial and commercial circles at home and abroad to organize a kind of liaison agency, respond to each other, assist each other, promote the prosperity of industry and commerce, guide overseas Chinese who return to China, and effectively guarantee them, he is very willing to do his best and work together if such an organization can be realized.

Ge Gongzhen Returns to China: Arrives in Shanghai Yesterday from Vladivostok

Ge Gongzhen, previously entrusted by the Central Propaganda Department, accompanied the League of Nations Northeast Investigation Team to Geneva to participate in the League of Nations Special Assembly. After the event, he was entrusted by the Shanghai Daily Newspaper Association to attend the International Press Experts Conference held in the capital of Spain. Simultaneously, he took the opportunity to visit France, Italy, Germany, Austria, Czechoslovakia, the Soviet Union, and various states to investigate communication enterprises and major news agencies, and to discuss methods of exchanging news. He spent a relatively long time in the Soviet Union, traveling over 80,000 li to visit major industrial and agricultural areas. After being abroad for more than three years, he arrived in Shanghai yesterday aboard the Russian ship "Northern" from Vladivostok. Ge spoke about the recent situation in Europe, believing that the trend of military competition among various countries means that war is inevitable. He predicts that the extent of the region and the weight of sacrifice will certainly be even more severe than the previous World War. At that time, China's being drawn into the vortex will be unavoidable, and the difficulty of the situation will be a hundred times worse than it is today. However, we must not be blinded by objective factors and become overly complacent. Consider the Soviet Union, which also experienced civil war and international interference, and was covered in scars. Following this, there was famine, but since burying its head in construction, the national strength has risen day by day. The difficulty lies in not relying on foreign capital, but only on labor. Our country has a vast territory, abundant resources, and a population the same size as the Soviet Union. The backwardness of industry and agriculture, the decline of agriculture, and the lack of universal education are also similar. Therefore, the Soviet Union's process of establishing heavy industry, military industry, and state farms has much to offer us for reflection. Moreover, our country has a naturally mild climate, fertile land, abundant and cheap labor, and is far superior to the Soviet Union. It only needs leadership, unified will, trust in science, and attention to organization. The Soviet Union's Five-Year Plan, which was successful in four and a half years, could perhaps be shortened in our country. Difficult times build a nation, but only if we are self-confident, that is, confident that the Chinese nation absolutely has the ability to save China, and so on.

Japanese Newspaper Reports: China's Cement Industry Self-Sufficient

The Japanese-language Mainichi Shimbun reports that China's cement industry has recently been able to supply the needs of the country. Previously, it relied solely on imports from foreign countries, but now it has surpassed them. The important cement companies in China are the Qixin Cement Company in Tangshan, the Shanghai Cement Company in Longhua, and the China Cement Company in Longtan. The total output of these companies in 1934 was approximately 2.4 million yuan. The output of Shanghai Cement Company and China Cement Company is similar, and Qixin Company produces slightly more. There is also considerable production in Hubei, Guangdong, Shanghai, and Jiangsu. Currently, the Chinese government and Chinese industrialists are planning to establish a large-scale cement plant in Nanjing, located in Qixia Mountain, named the Jiangnan Cement Company, with a capital of 2.4 million yuan. The Sanquan Cement Company in Guangdong has been producing 1,200 barrels per day since it started production last year, and recently added new-style machinery worth 2.5 million yuan, which can be called the only cement factory in China. According to a survey by foreign experts, the total cement consumption in China is approximately 5.2 million barrels per year, and still requires 7 million barrels. If the production capacity can be fully utilized, it will not only be self-sufficient, but also have a surplus for export.

Japanese National Smuggles Silver, Refuses Inspection by Customs Officers, Later Discovered by Japanese Police

The Da Mei Evening News reports that on Sunday, a certain Japanese national residing at No. 180 Kunshan Road was carrying luggage to the Huishan Wharf to board a Japanese ship to return to his country. Customs anti-smuggling officers suspected that he was carrying silver in his luggage and wanted to inspect it, but the Japanese national refused, nearly causing a riot. Later, a police officer from the Japanese Consulate intervened and escorted the Japanese national and his luggage to the Japanese Consulate, where an amount of smuggled silver was found. Today, a spokesperson for the Japanese Consulate stated that they will take appropriate action to punish this person, and also said that the Japanese authorities have been doing their best to assist the Chinese authorities in implementing the ban on silver smuggling, and will continue to do so in the future. However, they will not allow customs officials to arrest or search Japanese nationals.

Robbers Shoot and Kill Indian Woman, Open Fire and Resist Arrest, Bullets Fly Everywhere, Three Passersby Wounded by Bullets, One Robber Shot Dead by Chinese Police, Flesh and Blood a Blur

No. 1032 Foch Road in the French Concession is rented by an Indian named Lubauk Singh (transliteration). Lubauk is 37 years old this year, and his wife, Boshen Tieke (transliteration), is 38 years old this year. The couple has been in Shanghai for a long time, doing nothing and living off of lending money at high interest rates, with a generous income, leading robbers to mistakenly believe that there was a large sum of gold hidden in their home, and thus they conceived a desire to possess it. At 7:15 yesterday morning, not long after Lubauk and his wife got up, five robbers wearing short clothes and speaking with a Northern accent resembling people from Jiangbei rushed in, showing two pistols and threatening them not to make a sound. As they were about to search and rob, Lubauk's wife, Boshen Tieke, disregarding the danger, stepped forward to stop them, infuriating the robbers, who immediately fired a shot at her, hitting a vital point, and she immediately fell to the ground, dying instantly. Seeing that they had caused trouble, the robbers did not have time to search and rob, and immediately turned around and fled. Seeing his wife shot, Lubauk was unwilling to let it go, so he closely followed the robbers, chasing and shouting "robbers" along the way. The robbers fled towards Maichqi Road. Lubauk chased to the intersection and reported to Chinese Constable No. 1701, who was stationed there, who assisted in the pursuit, blowing the police whistle. Seeing constables chasing closely behind, the robbers opened fire along the way to resist arrest, bullets flying everywhere, injuring passersby Ni Caigen (25 years old, from Ningbo), who lived at No. 1 Baoanpo, Maichqi Road, and was a tailor (bullet wound to the right foot), Cai Jinkui (23 years old, from Pudong), who lived at No. 8 Julais Road, and was a mason (bullet graze to the chest), and an elderly woman about 50 years old (surname unknown, living at Liu's Residence), who was wounded in the head by a bullet, and other two people fell to the ground. At that time, the Chinese constable in charge of the second district of the Foch Road police station heard the sound of gunfire and shouts of "robbers" and rushed to intercept and arrest them, firing back at the entrance of No. 209 Maichqi Road. A bullet hit the head of a robber holding a gun, penetrating his forehead and causing him to fall to the ground with his brain spilling out, dying instantly. His face was covered in blood and gore. The robber was about 40 years old, wearing a black padded jacket, blue cloth trousers, a monk's haircut, black cloth shoes, and grey socks, with a pistol still in his hand. The remaining robbers fled without a trace in an instant. The Foch Road police station immediately summoned an ambulance to rush to the scene and send the three injured passersby to Guangci Hospital for treatment. Meanwhile, detectives rushed to investigate, and brought back to the police station the pistol in the dead robber's hand, and the robber's body was taken to the Tongren Fuyuan branch autopsy center. The body of the victim, Boshen Tieke, was taken by car to the Feilun Road autopsy center to await inspection by the relevant British Consulate official. At noon, the French police station reported to Prosecutor Wang Zai of the Special No. 2 Court, who, accompanied by forensic clerk Di, confirmed the robber's death and ordered Tongren Fuyuan Hall to take photos and bury him. After the three injured were admitted to the hospital, Ni and Cai's injuries were relatively minor, and they were bandaged by the doctor and discharged home. The old woman's injuries were more serious and she was kept in the hospital for treatment. After the incident, special agents from the French police station rushed to surround and search the scene of the incident, detaining a suspected rickshaw driver from Jiangbei, who was taken to the police station. It was found that he had previously committed a robbery case and had a record. He is currently under investigation. Meanwhile, the Western Inspector General ordered all detectives on duty to strictly apprehend the robbers who were at large and bring them to justice for interrogation.

Passenger Commits Suicide by Jumping into the Sea on the New Jiangtian Steamer from Ningbo to Shanghai

Investigation Reveals He Was an Employee of the Shunji Machinery Factory in Ningbo, and Took This Desperate Measure Due to Unrepayable Debt

The New Jiangtian steamer of the state-run China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, which runs the Shanghai-Ningbo line, sailed from Ningbo to Shanghai the day before yesterday (the 14th). Before casting off the mooring ropes, a passenger, about 50 years old, boarded cabin number 66 of the ship. The tea attendant, Shao Bingyan, provided attentive service. The passenger identified himself as Zhang, had no luggage, and seemed quite relaxed. After the ship cast off the mooring ropes, he ordered the tea attendant to buy wine and drank wildly, behaving quite lavishly. At 9:00 PM, the Zhang-named guest walked out of his room and gazed at the scenery by the ship's railing before returning to his room to rest. He went out again at around 10:00 PM, and had not returned by noon. The tea attendant grew suspicious and notified other colleagues on the ship to inquire separately, and also sent people to look for him in the toilets, but there was no trace of him. Realizing that something untoward had happened, they re-examined the items in the room and found a long gown, a cigarette case containing 15 cigarettes, a one-yuan Zhejiang Local Bank banknote, a business card of Wu Yunjin, and two small knives. Also, a letter was found in the long gown, using an envelope from Shunji Machinery Factory. The envelope was addressed to "Mr. Zhang Xiang of Shunji Factory, Tujiang Lane, Jiangbei Bank of Ningbo". The original letter read: "Brother Shiheng, please read. I owe a large amount of money to the factory, which I cannot repay. The amount owed is about 3,000 to 4,000 yuan. I have no choice but to take this desperate measure," and so on. It was then learned that the passenger had committed suicide by jumping into the sea. The tea attendant reported the situation to the purser and submitted the letter and other items so that family members could come to identify the body.

Dispute over Property Inheritance After Wang Yaochen's Death: Lu Xingyuan Accused of Forgery

Wang Yaochen Owned Much Property in Both Xiamen and Shanghai; His Will Left the Property to His Concubine, but His Legal Wife Believed It Was Not Her Husband's Handwriting

Lu Xingyuan, a Cantonese who formerly served as the President of the Shanghai Provisional Court and the Court of Appeal, became a lawyer in Shanghai after retiring. He is now accused of forging a will on behalf of Wang Yaochen, a French national from Xiamen, Fujian, who entrusted him to draft the will during his lifetime, giving it to Wang's concubine, Du Ruizhen, for safekeeping. Wang's wife, Ouyang Shunying, believes it to be forged and has hired a lawyer to file a criminal complaint for forgery in the First Special District District Court. In addition to Lu Xingyuan, the defendants also include Du Ruizhen (also known as Wang Du or Wang Ruizhen) and Shi Zhinan (also known as Shi Yuankai), the executor of the will. Wang Yaochen, also known as Wang Youyu, was originally from Xiamen but became a French national.

Ouyang Shunying married Wang at the age of eighteen and gave birth to a son named Shengduan. However, several years ago, he suffered from a mental illness, and treatment was ineffective. Therefore, although he is now grown up, he is like a disabled person, living with his mother in their hometown of Juanxia Shizai in Xiamen, in a house they built themselves. Du Ruizhen is Wang's concubine and resides at No. 17 Yugu Village, Yuyuan Road, in this city. Wang would travel between Xiamen and Shanghai. Two years ago, he came to Shanghai from Xiamen and never returned to his hometown. He died of illness in his Shanghai residence on October 18 of last year, at the age of fifty. When his wife in her hometown heard the news, she was filled with grief and, while still in mourning, published a notice in the Shenbao and Xinbao newspapers stating that all of Wang Yaochen's real estate in Shanghai and Xiamen would be inherited by her and her son. Anyone with objections was asked to present evidence within two weeks. At the end of the advertising period, there was no response at first. It was not until January 24 of this year that Huang Yizhu, a wealthy merchant from Xiamen, and Huang Yuqi, the owner of Changxing Firm in Shanghai, sent a letter to Ouyang Shunying informing her that Wang Yaochen had borrowed 6,000 yuan from them and requested recognition of their debt. On March 17, Du Ruizhen suddenly instructed Wang Shengqiang, Wang Yaochen's nephew, to send a letter to the French Consulate in Xiamen, stating that Wang Yaochen had made a will three days before his death, leaving all his property to Du, and requesting that the will be registered. When Ouyang Shunying heard about this, she examined the will and believed that the signature on it was definitely not her husband's handwriting, and that the application for registration was also beyond the deadline advertised in the newspaper. Therefore, she strongly denied the validity of the will. The French Consulate in Xiamen, because there was a dispute, did not approve the registration. Later, Ouyang found out that the will had been drafted by Lu Xingyuan, the original lawyer, and that it stated that Shi Yuankai, the executor of the will, had the power to manage, dispose of, sell, mortgage, and redeem the property, which she found even more outrageous. She immediately initiated legal proceedings in Xiamen. Unexpectedly, Du Ruizhen, seeing that the French Consul had refused to register, quickly changed her plans and secretly transferred 5 mu, 8 fen, 1 li, and 8 hao of land located on Petain Road, under the name of Wang Yaochen's father, Wang Wende (alias Zhong), who had passed away decades ago. First, it was mortgaged to a foreigner, and then, on May 23, it was entrusted to the trust department of the Bank of China for sale, obtaining a price of 91,000 yuan. She also planned to sell the Shanghai property and then take over the Xiamen property. Ouyang was determined to fight to keep the inheritance, so she hired lawyers Liu Shifang and others to file a criminal lawsuit against Du Ruizhen and Lu Xingyuan, accusing the defendants of colluding to forge the will, impersonating the name of Wang Wende, who had been dead for a long time, stealing the inheritance, and inciting Huang Yuqi of Changxing Firm to pursue the loan, causing the plaintiff to be overwhelmed. Therefore, the first defendant, Du Ruizhen, is guilty of violating Articles 210, 216, 217, and 320, paragraph 2 of the Criminal Law. The second defendant, Lu Xingyuan, is guilty of violating Articles 210, 217, and 215 of the Criminal Law. The third defendant, Shi Zhinan, is guilty of violating Article 30 of the Criminal Law. She requests that they be punished according to the law and that the stolen land be returned. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Xiao Fen opened the court to hear the case. The defendant Lu Xingyuan appeared in court, but the other two defendants did not appear because they could not be summoned. First, the plaintiff, Ouyang Shunying, stated that she is 51 years old and married Wang Yaochen 34 years ago, and gave birth to only one son, Shengduan. She then stated the facts of the lawsuit. Because she spoke in the Min dialect and her voice was as fine as a fly's, it was difficult to hear. What she said was roughly the same as the above. The defendant Lu Xingyuan then stood in the witness box and answered the charges. He said that the plaintiff was not present when Wang Yaochen entrusted him to write the will, so how could she know that it was forged? The will was written on October 15 of last year, when Wang called me to his residence and wrote it on three sheets of paper. Wang was already ill, and after I read it to him, he signed it himself. He also presented the original will to the court and stated that the details of the matter had been described in detail in his reply. The court ruled that the case still needed investigation and rescheduled the hearing for the afternoon of October 22.

Young Woman Pleads for Separate Residence, Moving and Affectionate Words

Since the situation is worse than sleeping in the same bed with different dreams, the hope of being like a pair of mandarin ducks that grow together on the same branch has been dashed.

Shao Xu, a young woman from Zhenhai, recently hired Peng Qixiu and Xu Wufang, two lawyers, to file a petition in the mediation court of the district court, requesting to live separately from her husband, Shao Renfen (brother of Shao, the owner of the Tianyi Film Company in this city), and to return 30,000 yuan for clothing expenses and 50,000 yuan for living expenses, a total of 80,000 yuan. Her petition is written in parallel prose with rhyming couplets, with moving and affectionate words, stating roughly that she has been abused and abandoned, and that the situation is truly unbearable. From the beginning of her marriage to the defendant, their relationship was harmonious and their bond was strong. Later, because her younger sister was getting married in Ningbo, she used this as an excuse to return to Ningbo for about two weeks. When her mother accompanied her back in the spring, she initially thought that like the eyebrow pencil, which is used to draw beautiful eyebrows, they would be briefly separated before being reunited. Like the poem about the alarm pillow, she would wait to compose it late at night. They would pour out their feelings of separation to each other and talk about their mutual longing. They would surely be tender and affectionate, admiring Liang Hong and Meng Guang under the eaves, and tuning the zither and se in the room. Who would have thought that the defendant would imitate Liu Xiahui by closing the door and acting out an evil drama in the mud? Regardless of the raging wind and rain, he only opened his mouth to speak harsh words. Even if she called and pleaded ten thousand times, she only received anger in response. Neighbors did not understand, but fortunately she had the protection of her crown. Her lips and tongue were exhausted before they finally got along. From then on, the young woman felt as if she were a recluse in a retreat, a bowl of cold porridge was like food that had been begged for, and five nights in a cold quilt made her feel like she had a tragic fate. She forced a smile through tear-filled eyes, not daring to call her mother-in-law evil. She hid her sorrow in a smiling face, but what could she do? Crying and laughter were both wrong, and she could not distinguish between bitter and salty. She endured hardship and swallowed her anger. The Shanghai War broke out the following year, and she was ordered by her mother-in-law to go to Ningbo to take refuge. When she returned to Shanghai on April 18 after the war, the defendant treated her as before. She had not been near the dressing table for a long time, and her mood was even more cold. Occasionally, when they met, he showed extreme contempt, avoiding her as if she were a leper and treating her like a servant. She, a mere weak woman, was bound by the rules and teachings, and had long heard the words of joining hands in the bridal chamber. The thought of being buried together in the same grave was truly heartbreaking. Since the situation was worse than sleeping in the same bed with different dreams, the hope of being like a pair of mandarin ducks that grow together on the same branch had been dashed. Alas, the heart of the cold-hearted man was like iron, and the life of the drifting woman was inhumane. If she was shackled for a long time, she would not care about her life. Therefore, she listed all the hardships and appealed to the court, asking to live separately in order to preserve her remaining breath. After receiving the petition, the court summoned the defendant Shao Renfen to court at 11:00 AM yesterday, but he did not appear. Only the petitioner Shao Xu and her lawyers Peng and Xu appeared in court. Shao Xu testified that she was 25 years old, from Zhenhai, Zhejiang, and currently lived in her uncle's home outside Dadongmen Bridge. In 1929, she formally married Shao Renfen according to the orders of her parents and the words of the matchmaker. Earlier, because her younger sister was getting married, she returned to Ningbo. When she returned to her husband's home, the door was tightly closed. Her husband spat blood and blamed her for not returning sooner, making things difficult for her in every way. At the beginning of their marriage, for about a month, their relationship was quite good. Now, she sleeps upstairs and he sleeps downstairs, as if they were strangers. She asked to be allowed to live separately. The judge asked how she would like to be supported. She replied that she needed 120 yuan per month for living expenses, and since she was 25 years old now, she would need over 50,000 yuan to live until she was 60 years old, and also the return of 30,000 yuan for clothing expenses. The judge said, "Is the defendant able to bear such a huge sum?" She replied, "The defendant is the owner of Tianyi Film Company and also runs Jintaichang Paint Store, owning assets of over one million yuan. It is not excessive to ask for only 80,000 yuan now." After hearing the testimony, the judge ruled that because the defendant did not appear today, the mediation was unsuccessful. She was ordered to pay the litigation fees and file a formal lawsuit. After the ruling, the court was adjourned.

Yi Yi Xuan Association: Problem of Selling Opium

The accountant and tea servers all strongly deny it. The judge finds the facts clear and schedules the sentencing.

The Yi Yi Xuan Association, established by Cantonese expatriates in Shanghai, has been around for decades. Recently, the relevant police station discovered that it was running a gambling den and selling opium at its premises at No. 5, Sanhe Lane, Jiangxi Road, and sent undercover agents to search the premises. They seized a quantity of opium paste and paraphernalia, along with the association's accountant, a Cantonese man named Wang Shaoqing, the tea server, Tan Gui, and opium smokers, Hu Tian, ​​who were taken to the First Special District District Court. Hu was sentenced to a fine of 60 yuan and sent to the hospital for 20 days of rehabilitation. Wang and Tan were detained pending further investigation to determine whether they were selling opium privately. This was reported in the previous newspapers. Yesterday morning, Judge Feng Shide continued to bring the defendants before the court for further investigation. However, no one admitted to selling opium paste, and all claimed that the opium was brought by the members themselves and placed in the association. Even the opium paraphernalia was brought to the association by the members, which is why there were markings on the ash trays. Judge Feng pointed out that the case file clearly stated that Tan Gui had received several tens of yuan from the sale of opium residue, and that the character "earth" (土, slang for opium) also appeared in the accounting books. He repeatedly questioned the two defendants, but they were evasive throughout. The court then ruled that the facts were clear and ordered the start of the debate. First, police lawyer Wang Yaotang spoke, saying that based on the evidence in the case, the evidence against the two defendants for selling opium seemed weak, but the fact that they sold opium residue was clear, and they should be punished according to the law. As for the association's gambling and opium sales, which violated the association's rules, this could be pursued in a separate case. Next, the defendants' lawyer, Fan Ganglian, argued that those who came to the association were all wealthy men, and the defendants dared not interfere even if they saw them smoking opium, because if they were not careful and provoked their anger, they would lose their jobs. The money from the sale of opium residue cannot be equated with the sale of opium. He requested that the judge make a clear distinction. Judge Feng then ruled that the sentence would be announced next Tuesday, and the two defendants were taken back to the police station for detention.

Yao Fuquan and Six Others Arrived; The Eighty-Fourth Group Has Already Returned to Their Hometowns

They are currently lodging at the Laogongxin Inn at the Sixteenth Bund and plan to petition the Municipal Public Security Bureau and the Overseas Chinese Affairs Bureau today for relief. According to a reporter from the Daily News, the eighty-fourth group of fourteen people, including Yao Chenggu, who arrived in Shanghai a few days ago, were issued half-price tickets by the Public Security and Overseas Chinese Affairs Bureaus and have returned to their hometown of Wenzhou to make a living.

Fish Traders Request a Fish Market; Hire Advanced Fisheries Experts as Managers; The Fish Market is Carefully Considering

According to the Guowen News Agency, the Ministry of Industry's fish market, which has been under construction since bidding last year, is now fully completed. It was originally planned to open at the end of last month, but the opening was delayed due to the market's organizational law and the fish traders' concerns about the imperial system. Currently, the market preparation office is drafting an organizational law for submission to the ministry for review while also addressing the fish traders' concerns. Originally, after the market opened for business, all the fish traders in the Sixteenth Bund area of ​​the city would have to close. The market plans to imitate the Japanese central wholesale market model and use the closed fish trader owners as brokers in the market. However, they would have to pay a deposit of 3,000 yuan upon entering the market, and the commission given would only be 3%, while the fish traders in the past charged 11% per 100 yuan of value as commission, which is a significant difference. Therefore, there is strong opposition. According to a person in the fishing industry who told the reporter yesterday, in order to achieve a comprehensive solution, the market will accommodate the opinions of the fish traders as much as possible. It is said that the fish traders requested that the market should hire advanced members of the local fishing industry or people related to fish traders to serve as managers or assistant managers in order to achieve thorough cooperation. The market is still considering this proposal.
