The Maoli Collides with the Sanbei

The Sanbei is Out of Service for Repairs; The Maoli Continues to Sail as Usual

The Maoli, a ship of the Maoli Company in the South City, returned to Shanghai from Chongming yesterday. At 11:35 p.m. on the 14th, while sailing to the Niutougang of Beisha, it collided with the Sanbei, a ship of the Sanbei Company on the same route, which had arrived earlier. The Maoli turned around as usual at the dock, and its bow crashed into the left outer cabin of the bow of the Sanbei, which was anchored. The iron plates were damaged in the collision. The two shipowners inspected the damage together, and the Sanbei first weighed anchor and sailed to Qinglonggang to load and unload cargo and passengers. Unexpectedly, after anchoring in Qinglonggang, the Maoli followed and sailed to the vicinity of the Sanbei, again colliding with the left outer cabin of the bow of the Sanbei. After the two collisions, the damage to the Sanbei was even greater than before. However, because the damage was on the upper part of the ship, it did not cause water damage, and it was still able to barely sail to Shanghai. After entering the port yesterday, it unloaded cargo and passengers at the South City Wharf, and the shipowner reported to the company. The Maoli also returned to Shanghai. The Sanbei Company reported the details of the incident to the Navigation Administration Bureau and requested that a surveyor be sent to the South City Wharf to board the ship for inspection. The surveyor saw that three pieces of the iron plate on the outer rail of the bow of the Sanbei had been destroyed, and the wooden frame on the ship had also been destroyed, damaging several feet, causing considerable damage. Then, the surveyor inspected the Maoli and saw that the bow of the ship was also bent inward due to the collision, but it was not broken and had been newly repaired not long ago, so it did not hinder navigation. The surveyor of the Navigation Administration Bureau asked the shipowners of the Sanbei and Maoli about the cause of the accident. First, the owner of the Sanbei reported that the ship was hit while anchored. Then, the owner of the Maoli said that the collision was caused by the water turbulence during the turning. Because the Sanbei was more severely damaged, the company decided to suspend operations and immediately begin repairs. The Maoli was damaged in the bow, but it did not affect navigation, and the Navigation Administration Bureau allowed it to continue to operate. At 5 p.m. yesterday, the Maoli had normally loaded cargo and passengers and set off for Chongsha.

The Commercial Press Small Loan Fund Committee is Established

Because the main factory of the Commercial Press was destroyed and closed down, all employees were dismissed with government approval. Since the resumption of business in August of the 21st year, most of the old employees who have been reinstated and those who indirectly serve the company outside have been rehired, but there are still a few unemployed people staying in Shanghai. In order to help them solve their employment problems, the company has decided to allocate 50,000 yuan from the Class B special reserve fund to establish a Small Loan Fund Committee, appointing Li Dachao, Zhu Maocheng, He Qingru, Hua Weizhong, Zhou Youju, Zhang Shuliang, Yu Zhonghua, Shi Jiuyun, and Xu Baiqi as members, and cooperating with the Shanghai Vocational Guidance Institute. Yesterday, the establishment meeting was held at the Bank Club on Hong Kong Road. Zhu Maocheng was elected as the chairman, and Li Dachao, He Qingru, and Shi Jiuyun were elected as standing committee members. Xu Baiqi was elected as the secretary. The committee hired Yang Chongyu, Huang Jingwan, and Zhuang Tongsan as staff members. The office is located at the Chinese Vocational Education Society at the intersection of Hualong Road and Huanlong Road in this port. On the 21st of this month, registration and investigation procedures will begin. It is commendable that the company is so enthusiastic about helping its employees and has such a comprehensive plan. The company's declaration, the charter of the fund committee, and the detailed rules of procedure are attached below.

Declaration: Notice to all. According to the company's charter, if there is a surplus in the annual account, a certain percentage will be allocated to the public welfare fund, which is the source of resources for the welfare undertakings of all employees, the reconstruction fund of the Oriental Library, etc. Since the resumption of business in August of the 21st year of the Republic of China, after suffering deep pain and hardship, we have relied on the diligence and hard work of our colleagues internally and the guidance and support of the society externally. Fortunately, there has been a slight surplus in recent years, and the public welfare fund has been replenished. To date, colleague welfare undertakings, such as disease assistance, life insurance, incentive savings, and children's education, have been successively established, and the reconstruction of the Oriental Library is gradually taking shape. In view of the result of the social depression, the number of unemployed people in Shanghai is increasing. Among the old employees of the company who were laid off due to the January 28th Incident, more than a thousand people have been reinstated one after another. Including those who indirectly serve the company and those who have other jobs, there should also be no less than a thousand people. However, there are still quite a few people who are currently unemployed or who have been employed and then unemployed again and are stranded in Shanghai. At a time when industry and commerce are declining, the solution to the employment problem is becoming increasingly difficult. The company is also affected by the depression and is gradually falling into overproduction. It is difficult to fulfill the wish of building thousands of mansions, and it is also impossible to give out robes everywhere. Therefore, based on the meaning of helping oneself and helping others, we will seek to help others and help oneself. We believe that if the unemployed are determined to help themselves, even if it is difficult to find jobs in large enterprises due to the depression, small-scale business efforts may still be possible. The combination of labor and capital is production. Everyone has labor, but what is lacking is capital. However, capital has great uses for large amounts and small uses for small amounts. It is common to see people who use tens of yuan of capital for small-scale business and are able to support themselves. The key to their success is nothing more than obtaining a small amount of capital and then acting carefully under the guidance of experienced people. The company is willing to do its best to allocate 50,000 yuan from the public welfare fund to establish a small loan fund to help the old employees who are unemployed and stranded in Shanghai solve the problem of capital. We have also extended invitations to people who are enthusiastic about social undertakings to organize a committee to preside over its distribution, and we are cooperating with the experienced Shanghai Vocational Guidance Institute to provide guidance on employment issues to the old employees who are unemployed and stranded in Shanghai. However, the key to success ultimately depends on the ability of the operators to be diligent and cautious. Therefore, the final problem still depends on the self-planning solution of each individual. The matter is a pioneering effort, and the success or failure of its experiment is closely related to social problems and is not limited to the livelihoods of a few people. In addition to sincerely hoping that unemployed old employees will use assistance to work hard to help themselves, we hope that people of all walks of life will teach us. Sincerely, Commercial Press, October, 24th year.

Charter: Charter of the Commercial Press Small Loan Fund Committee. Article 1. The Commercial Press (hereinafter referred to as "Commercial") has established the Small Loan Fund Committee (hereinafter referred to as "Committee") with a loan of 50,000 yuan from the Class B special reserve fund by the board of directors in order to support old employees who were unemployed due to the January 28th Incident. Article 2. The Committee is organized by the General Administration of Commercial, which hires people who are enthusiastic about social undertakings and Commercial employees. The rules of procedure of the Committee are formulated by the General Administration of Commercial. Article 3. The Committee cooperates with the Vocational Guidance Institute to facilitate the performance of its duties. Article 4. Those who were formally employed by Commercial before January 28th and meet the following conditions may apply to the Committee for a small loan: A. Those who have been unemployed since the January 28th Incident or who have been employed in the middle but are now unemployed for more than half a year. B. Those who are willing to engage in small-scale business but do not have the resources to raise capital. C. Those who are currently stranded in the urban area of ​​Shanghai. Article 5. Those who have one of the following circumstances may not apply for a small loan: A. Those who hold shares in Commercial. B. Those whose father or son is currently employed by Commercial. C. Those whose husband or wife is currently employed by Commercial. D. Those whose husband is currently employed. E. Those who were employed by Commercial after the January 28th Incident and were dismissed due to negligence. Article 6. The amount of the small loan is limited to 40 yuan per person, without interest. Each person may only apply once. However, if the father, son, and spouse are all applicants for the loan, only one person will be loaned the full amount of 40 yuan, and the others will be loaned half the amount. Article 7. Applicants for small loans must find a store or an individual with a legitimate occupation as a guarantor and bear joint and several liability for repayment. Article 8. After receiving the application, the Committee will approve the loan for those who pass the review, and will reject the loan with a statement of reasons for those who do not pass the review. If the Committee deems it necessary, it may issue the loan amount to some applicants in two installments. The first installment will be half the amount, and the other half will be issued after six months, depending on the performance of each applicant. Article 9. After receiving the loan, the applicant should earnestly engage in small-scale business and repay 5% of the loan amount every month starting from the third month, with the total amount being repaid in 20 months. Article 10. Those who repay the small loan on time will be awarded a certificate of good credit by the Committee as encouragement. Article 11. If the application for the small loan is untrue or the loan is not repaid by the deadline, the guarantor shall be responsible for repaying it. However, if the applicant for the loan dies or suffers from a disability before repaying the full amount, the guarantor may be exempted from the liability for the unpaid portion. Article 12. The total amount of small loans is limited to the fund. Once the limit is reached, it will be stopped. However, the loans that have been issued will be re-loaned as the fund after being repaid one after another. Article 13. In addition to handling small loans, the Committee should provide vocational guidance to applicants for loans within the possible scope with the assistance of the Shanghai Vocational Guidance Institute. Article 14. The committee members are all honorary positions, but the expenses required for the committee's office should be budgeted by the committee and approved by the General Administration of Commercial before being paid separately, and the small loan fund must not be used. Article 15. The period of existence of the Committee shall be until the end of the 26th year of the Republic of China. Upon expiration, the fund shall be liquidated and returned to Commercial. Article 16. During the period of existence of the Committee, the Board of Directors of Commercial may amend this charter if it deems necessary, and may terminate the work of the Committee early.

Zhang Shuiqi of the Eastern Travel Agency Arrives in Shanghai to Discuss That There Will Be No Through Train Service Between Customs and Abroad

Business is Still Good, With an Annual Income of More Than Two Million Yuan; The Currency System of the Puppet State is Different, Causing Us Considerable Losses

—The Meeting in Peiping Only Discussed Technical Issues—

Mr. Zhang Shuiqi, the manager of the Eastern Travel Agency, which organizes the through train service between customs and abroad on the Peiping-Shenyang route, left Peiping a few days ago and arrived in Shanghai on the Shanghai-Ping-Tong train yesterday morning. He stayed at a hotel. The Dagong News Agency reporter visited him and he gave a detailed account of the business situation of the Peiping-Shenyang through train and the situation inside and outside the customs. The details are as follows:

Business is Still Good, But There Are Still Losses

After the opening of the through train service on the Beining Railway on July 1st of last year, there were not many passengers at the time, and the business did not improve. However, it gradually improved. Now there are many passengers, with an annual income of 2 million yuan. However, the expenses of the Eastern Travel Agency are about more than 90,000 yuan per year, and its expenses are taken from the 5% ticket commission. Therefore, based on an annual income of 2 million yuan, it can make up for the past losses. However, the Travel Agency and the Beining Railway Bureau do not have the same market value for the currency systems of the puppet state and China. One yuan of the puppet currency is only equivalent to 7 jiao of Chinese currency. Therefore, passengers from Peiping-Tianjin to Shenyang often buy tickets to Shanhaiguan first, and then buy tickets to the puppet state at Shanhaiguan. This section of the fare can be calculated in puppet currency, and there are fewer passengers from inside the customs to outside the customs than from outside the customs to inside the customs. Therefore, the fare sold outside the customs is also more than that inside the customs. Every time the accounts are settled, the Beining Railway Bureau suffers a considerable loss. Now, both parties have agreed to exchange the currency at the market price, so that the market value of Chinese currency and puppet currency can be balanced. After the implementation of this system, the Beining Railway and the Travel Agency will not suffer any losses.

No Through Transport; External Rumors Are Not Accurate

The Dagong News Agency reporter asked whether it was true that the rumors outside that there would be through transport between customs and abroad were true. Zhang said that this was not true, because the joint operation of passenger through trains between the Beining Railway Bureau and the South Manchuria Railway had already taken a lot of effort. Moreover, Japanese people outside the customs have an international transportation company organization. The company is large in scale, with a total capital of 10 million yuan. Most of the goods transported inside and outside the customs are handled by the company, and there is no need for it in fact.

Meetings in Peiping; Discussing Technology

As for the meeting of representatives of the Beining Railway and the South Manchuria Railway in Peiping this time, it was purely to discuss the technical problems on the current through trains, such as the procedures for ticket refunds, changes in the wording of accounting books, improvements in other minor procedures, and the regulations on currency exchange between customs and abroad. All attendees were representatives. As for the Director of the Beining Railway Bureau, Yin Tong, going to Peiping, it was not to attend the meeting, but because the Beining Railway Train Children Training Institute opened, and he went to deliver a speech. Outsiders did not know the facts and mistakenly thought that Yin's attendance was to participate in the discussion on through transport between customs and abroad. Zhang also said that his coming to Shanghai this time was because time was short and he did not have time to take care of it, so he returned to Shanghai to arrange everything. He will stay in Shanghai for a few days and then go north.

Pre-Order of Selected Famous Ming Dynasty Prose Writers

The most notable era for short prose pieces was the Ming Dynasty, with the Three Yuan of Gong'an and Zhong Tan of Jingling being highly praised by contemporaries as outstanding figures in Ming Dynasty prose. In reality, figures such as Xu Wenchang and Tang Bohu of the High Ming period, and Chen Meigong and Tang Ruoshi of the Late Ming period, were arguably no less significant than the Three Yuan and Zhong Tan. Yuan Zhonglang rarely gave approval, but he did comment on the collection of Xu Wenchang and reviewed the poems of Tang Bohu, demonstrating the brilliance of their poetry and prose. Yuan's commentary editions are now rare, only occasionally found among collectors. Now, the owner of Dadao Bookstore is releasing their treasured collections of the complete works of Xu Wenchang, Chen Meigong, Tang Ruoshi, Tang Bohu, Zhu Zhishan, and Wen Zhengming, to be published as the "Complete Works of Six Famous Ming Dynasty Prose Writers" in twelve thick volumes, priced at twenty-six yuan. A pre-order discount of fifteen percent reduces the price to only three yuan and sixty cents. Individual volumes can also be ordered separately. Fine-bound editions are also available for scholars to collect. Pre-orders will close at the end of this month, presenting a rare opportunity for those who enjoy reading short prose pieces. It is reported that the complete works of Xu Wenchang and Chen Meigong will be released first on November 10th.

Occasional Notes

Snippets

— (Zheng Yimei)

The mind must be calm, the spirit must be passionate. The shadow of flowers enhances the painter's inspiration, the trace of the moon adds to my sentimental moments.

The trend of performing Chinese plays is prevalent in Europe and America. Tracing its origins, it began in 1692 when the Italian celebrity Regudarb performed the Chinese drama "Les Chinoise" before the imperial court, at the Hotel Courgognc in Prologue.

Floral fabric is considered outdated. Some have green backgrounds with white flowers, while others have white backgrounds with green flowers. Nowadays, only women north of the Yangtze River occasionally wear it. The other day, I saw Ms. Yin Mingzhu in a specially made floral fabric cheongsam with a novel design. Wearing it for photographs enhanced her beauty, transforming the rotten into the magical. Only she could do it.

The forte of promotion is self-praise, the skill of advertising is to deceive people.

The more society evolves, the more morality declines.

Talking about poetry and literature with modern women, or discussing movies and plays with impoverished scholars, is equally clueless.

A certain celebrity, unable to vent his indignation, wrote a couplet and pasted it on his door: "The Buddha said it cannot be spoken," "Confucius said, what is to be done?" I think these two sentences can be used in other contexts. The first line refers to the past "September 18th" anniversary, while the second line refers to the future "January 28th" National Humiliation Day.

The moon gets its light from the sun. This is the statement of modern scientists. Unexpectedly, thousands of years ago, our country already had this saying. Zhang Heng's Ling Xian said: "The moon is perfect in shape and pure in quality, receiving light from the sun." This shows a glimpse of the ancient understanding of astronomy.

The Standard Worker

— Ba Ling

My neighbor, the carpenter Ah Wu, is called the "standard worker" by everyone. At first, I didn't quite understand the origin of this honorific. Later, after I investigated Ah Wu's life, I realized that this title was indeed appropriate for him.

It turns out that although Ah Wu is a worker, he is very disciplined in his life. When to get up? When to start work? When to rest? When to sleep? He always has a set time for everything. Except for special circumstances, he does not change his regular routine. He also has a standard for managing his monthly income. How much for household expenses? How much for personal spending? How much for adding things? How much for savings? Everything is spent according to the standard, without wasting a bit. Therefore, his finances never feel tight, and naturally, his spirit is also very happy.

Secondly, speaking of Ah Wu's character, he is also very amiable. He treats everyone with politeness, so everyone likes to be friends with him, and his work becomes particularly busy. However, no matter how busy he is, he always does his work happily, without uttering a single complaint.

Because Ah Wu has these strengths, everyone changed his title to "standard worker." I think this is very right, because everything about the carpenter Ah Wu is worthy of emulation by ordinary workers.

Autumn Fish Spawning Season

— Zheng Yan

On the coast, fishermen go out to sea to catch fish, dividing the year into four fishing seasons, which serve as the standard for departure and return: spring, summer, autumn, and winter. Now is the season of autumn, which is the start of the autumn fishing season. Let's talk about the "autumn fishing season":

The fishermen had not rested long from the end of the summer fishing season when autumn arrived. So, as usual, they set out to sea in their fishing boats. However, autumn is not like the other fishing seasons, where they can have calm seas and safely set up their nets to catch fish. Throughout the autumn, fishing boats drift on the ocean, almost always in an environment of wind and waves, battered by rain and waves. So, the lives of fishermen are constantly at risk of ending up in the bellies of fish and shrimp!

In the autumn fishing season, the fish caught by fishermen at sea are mostly pomfret, scaled fish, croaker, ghost crabs, scorpionfish, etc. Because the tides on the sea in autumn rise several to ten times higher than usual, coupled with the gradually cooling weather, the migration of fish becomes unpredictable, and they also do not swim upstream. Therefore, fishing is considered the most difficult in the autumn fishing season. Fishermen moor their boats at night near small islands or corners of the beach in the harbor. When it dawns, they sail their boats out to sea. After one or two days to three or four days, when the fish holds are full, they return to the fishing port to sell their catch. But, often, there are times when they don't catch many fish in three or four days. On windy and rainy nights, the waves are whipped up to the sky by the headwind. There are always several fishing boats that are unable to return, struggling for their remaining lives under the onslaught of the adverse forces!

But although they brave the deep sea, disregarding their lives, to fight the wind and waves for a living, the price they get in return is extremely meager.

Thinner Than Yellow Flowers

— Juan Yin

Debt Collection

— Zhu Weixuan

Everyone knows Little Zhang in S. Port's dance halls. It's an honor for the girls to have a dance with him.

Little Zhang became so famous because of his family's tens of thousands of dollars of ill-gotten gains. Because of this, he's able to immerse himself day and night in a life of extravagance and indulgence.

Because he spent money like water and acted generously, he naturally gained the favor of many dancers. Under the double threat of power and money, not a few dancers were tempted and lost their bodies. As for those who danced with him once, there are as many as grains of sand on the Ganges River.

His limited money couldn't stand his excessive spending. In just two or three years, his hundreds of thousands of dollars were completely waltzed away into the dancers' pockets. After Little Zhang danced away almost all his property, he abandoned his plain wife and his beautiful and lively eight-year-old daughter and quietly left S. Port, no one knows where he went.

From then on, Little Zhang's trace could not be found in the dance halls, and his image disappeared from the minds of every dancer!

Ten years later, a glittering star suddenly appeared in S. Port's X dance hall and was elected dance queen of S. Port. Her name is Zhang Lingling. Her nightly income from dance tickets is always over hundreds of dollars. So, even though she's a dancer, she's accumulated wealth.

Later, according to people familiar with the matter, this dance queen who earns ten thousand dollars a month is actually the daughter of the formerly wealthy young man—Little Zhang—who spent hundreds of thousands of dollars in the dance halls. So, the general humorous opinion is that Zhang Lingling is here to collect the debt her father incurred ten years ago. However, this method of debt collection doesn't seem very honorable, does it?

Local Customs Small Records

The Basque Ball Game is Popular in Shanghai

— Shanghai News Agency

A narrative of the Central Sports Field, Jai Alai, and Boxing

Jai alai, a ball game of the ancient Basque people, was introduced to Shanghai from Spain only six years ago, and has now become one of the most popular indoor sports in Shanghai.

In the autumn of 1928, a joint-stock company called Central Sports Field – Parc des Sports in French, Auditorium in English – emerged with the purpose of introducing jai alai and promoting boxing. After enough shares were raised and the venue was built, professional jai alai players were recruited from Cairo, Egypt, Alexandria, Virginia, and Barcelona, Spain.

The ancient jai alai competition made its first appearance before the audience at the Central Sports Field on February 7, 1929. That night, twenty-four contestants participated in this grand opening program.

The high speed of competition is one of the reasons why jai alai is most attractive to learners, but it is difficult for Shanghai athletes to learn it, so it was not until December 1930, when newly recruited artists came from overseas, that the ball game could be fully continued.

With new jai alai players coming from Cuba, Brazil, and Spain, jai alai achieved definite success in Shanghai. On August 20, 1931, the Central Sports Field performed a special program to raise money for flood relief, and the net amount of money raised for flood victims was 4,000 yuan.

In January 1932, the Central Sports Field was temporarily closed due to the outbreak of the war between China and Japan in Zhabei. It reopened on March 1. At that time, the starting time of the race was 7:00 PM, so that the audience could return home before the 10:00 PM curfew.

The general manager of the Central Sports Field and captain of the jai alai team is Jauregui Teodoro, the manager is AHaig, and the secretary and advertising director and boxing introducer is T. D. Sofoulis.

Boxing competitions are often staged as entertainment for Shanghai audiences with magnificent human body defense skills, but the attraction is not great. The best Shanghai boxers have shown their skills in many competitions in the past few years.

Although jai alai is mainly a professional sport in Shanghai, the general manager of the Central Sports Field has also had considerable success in encouraging amateur athletes to participate in this ancient Basque sport. Amateur competitions are held from time to time, and exquisite awards are given to the winners.

The Central Sports Field is backed by a group of powerful financiers, led by F. Bouvier. Bouvier is the chairman of the board of directors of the field, the manager of the Huifeng Bank, and the director of the French Racing Club (dog racing club).

The vice chairman of the board of directors is C. Ballaodra, and the other directors are: Su Fanai, Shen Changgeng, Baibaode, Nicole, and Ye Keweiwei. George is the supervisor.

Records of Fleeting Fragrance

— Originally written by Princess Deling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

Once the Empress Dowager's body and buttocks are completely covered with soap, the first step of the work is completed. The four palace maids discard the towels in their hands together, and each picks up a new towel, soaking it in warm water first, and then taking it out and wringing it dry. This time, however, no soap is applied, and the towels are wrung out more wetly. The procedure is to wipe off the soap that has just been applied and the dirt that has been wiped off by the soap, so the wiping time is also longer. After this wiping is done, there must be a final dry wipe, which requires four more towels to be replaced.

After going through three wipes like this, the Empress Dowager's upper body is of course very clean, but things are not so simple! As soon as the four palace maids put down the last towel, they busily took a jar of heated camellia dew - which the Empress Dowager applies to her face every night - and used four balls of pure white silk cotton, soaked in the dew, generously applying it to the Empress Dowager's body. After each part is completely covered, they take four other clean towels to gently pat her dry. This is really a lot of trouble!

When the wiping work is done to this point, it is of course the ultimate! The second step is to take a set of clean pajamas and trousers for the Empress Dowager, and first put on the pajamas for her, so that her upper body will not get cold. Then, the Empress Dowager herself takes off her inner trousers, completely naked to her toes, and the lower half of her body is completely exposed. Then, four other palace maids who are dedicated to rough work, receive a signal from the four palace maids inside, and carry in another bathtub, which is also wooden and covered with silver skin. Little Western Paradise

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 20: Striving for Life, Watching Clever Grandson Hug and Shed Tears, Desolate Year, Planting Wheat from the Past Brings Disaster

The old lady trembled and suddenly stretched out her hands, clasped her palms together, and bowed to Zhiqian, saying: Mr. Cheng...you are a savior in times of distress, you...saved my...my life. Zhiqian didn't have any feelings for this drifting woman from the Zhu family in the south, but seeing her pitiful appearance, he felt a burst of sadness in his heart, and he couldn't help but two lines of tears flowed down, so he turned his face away and waved his hand to them, calling out: You all come with me. He took a few steps before stopping and turning back to look. Because the sour feeling that surged from his heart had been suppressed after a few steps, the two lines of tears that were about to fall did not flow out, and he could see people. At this time, the old lady was full of energy, and she didn't know where it came from. She didn't need anyone to help her, but held Zhu Hu's arms with one hand and followed. Mrs. Hu was hiding left and right behind her, just protecting her. She said: No, no...it's okay, isn't it? Don't let my Yue'er be implicated in this matter, right? Zhiqian straightened his chest and said: It's okay, I'll take responsibility with you no matter how big the matter is. As he said that, he slowly led the way in front. When he arrived in front of Jia Duocai's room, Zhiqian called out: Mrs. Jia, come out and see, your...Yueying. Just as he was stretching his head out by the door, he saw the old lady, ran over and shouted: My grandma, with just this sentence, he had run to the old lady, grabbed the old lady's lapels with both hands and shook her randomly. Below, he couldn't say a word, he just cried. (340)

First Result of the Settlement of Overdue Loans

Settlement Totaling Over 10 Million; Transfer of 6.6 Million

Yesterday, the 15th, was the due date for the first batch of the sixth long-term settlement. All loans made and transferred before April 15 of the first half of the year were due yesterday. The total amount of overdue loans that needed to be settled yesterday was over 3.4 million yuan from the Chinese banks, over 7 million yuan from the money shops, and 1.56 million yuan from the Ningbo banks. Among them, the results of the settlement were: over 3.2 million yuan transferred by the banks, less than 200,000 yuan recovered, and over 300,000 yuan newly made. The interest rates were 8.75 yuan and 10.05 yuan. The settlement situation of the money shops was: over 6 million yuan were settled and transferred directly, about 670,000 yuan were agreed upon by both parties and transferred accordingly, and over 10 money shops made new loans. The money shops lent about 780,000 yuan to foreign firms, streets, various ports, and foreign firms, with interest rates ranging from 8.75 yuan to 10.5 yuan. The interest rates varied. Over 890,000 yuan were transferred by the Ningbo banks, and 560,000 yuan were repaid by Shanghai banks. Over 100,000 yuan of new loans were made. Old Yongtou-type loans were not released. It was found that the total amount of overdue loans settled on that day was over 10 million yuan. The total amount of long-term deposits that matured was over 2 million yuan. About half of the depositors requested to withdraw their deposits, totaling about 1 million yuan. One-third of the depositors transferred their deposits. The remaining 670,000 yuan were either from new depositors or transferred from old accounts. As for the interest rates, they had to be calculated based on the market conditions within the hall, but this market condition was expected to be released around the 27th or 28th of this month. As far as we can guess, there would be limited difference from the price at the end of April of the first half of the year, generally between 5 yuan and 5.5 yuan.

Therefore, although actual sales were not brisk, the standard was easily bullish, with all months rising by over three fen. The fact that flour prices rose despite the decline in foreign wheat seemed to reflect concerns about supply and demand.

Free Discussion

On Civilization

— He Jin

In an article discussing gender issues, Akamatsu Meiko, after clarifying the freedom and equality of the union between the sexes in primitive times, went on to make the following statement:

"Descending into the age of civilization... the so-called relationship between the sexes completely fell into the relationship of the dominating man to the enslaved woman, the dominated. There is no human relationship at all in between."

Because the original author was discussing gender issues, the elucidation of the so-called "civilization" was limited to the scope of gender issues. Therefore, they still showed some consideration for the word "civilization" that we all use in speech, in writing, and especially as decoration for special tools. However, for us, this statement is already very useful: "Descending into the age of civilization... there is no human relationship at all in between!"

The word "civilization" became fashionable in China, which, from our generation's perspective, does not seem too long ago. After the abolition of the imperial examination, students in the "new schools," even though their queues were still long, liked to write things like "In today's civilized world..." in their essays. In the West, "civilization" is treated as a family heirloom of mankind, used to casually do some "great cause". Even now, aren't there still many people who, on the one hand, shout about civilization, and on the other hand, ride on others, or even act as "stable boys" yelling until they are busy? However, those people would never say, "And when it came to the age of civilization, human relationships ceased to exist at all." They would certainly say, "The current era is becoming more and more civilized, so civilized people must educate barbarians."

But what exactly is this method of "education"? Sinclair Lewis wrote the following in his novel "Ann Vickers":

"Bang, bang, bang!" He (referring to Columbus - author's note) knocked them down (referring to the Red Indians of America - author's note) to introduce European culture to primitive America."

And so on.

This "education" method is of course extremely clever. The word "civilization" has thus become the most useful thing for the "teachers" who want to educate those "barbarians"—but the effectiveness of this "use" is not necessarily so great, because even if the minds of those "savages" are simple, they see that "the bomb falls, and those who die under it are not the "civilized" people themselves—which is certainly admirable—but when they look downward," those who die are all women and children; when they look upward, they find "civilized" people enjoying themselves in the clouds, they will be stunned, and even become "more and more confused"! They did not see the so-called "civilization," they only saw: "There is no human relationship at all in between."

In fact, this method of civilized education is not a new invention; on the contrary, it is simply a "reduced by 80%" reprint of an ancient book.

Then is "civilization" really such an undesirable thing? Actually, there is no need to say that. If we compare "civilization" to coins (how "mercenary" the comparison is!), then we can say that the coins currently circulating in the market are all "copper foreign coins" privately manufactured by a group of bored rogues for the sake of profit. Of course, there are good foreign coins. We don't have to reject even good foreign coins because of the fraudulent "copper foreign coins". The current method is to learn from the owners of "cigarette paper shops" and "exchange shops," and use nails to pierce a two-sided hole in the "copper foreign coins" that can be seen in the market! This indicates that they will not be used in the future and that they are fraudulent things (which, of course, makes those who manufacture counterfeit coins very unhappy). On the other hand, we should try our best to find real good foreign coins. However, the production of good foreign coins is not easy, not only because it requires a lot of hard work, but most importantly, it also requires the selflessness and sincerity of a good technician and inspector who can formulate the composition.

My View on the May Fourth Movement

— Shi Yin

A few days ago, Mr. Cao Juren published an article on the mold of the May Fourth Movement, concluding that we should value the historical significance of the May Fourth Movement and not value the heroes created by the circumstances who are covered in mold. Subsequently, Yang Zao wrote a long article on the actual situation of the May Fourth Movement, mainly to show the purity of the central figures of the movement at that time, which differed slightly from Mr. Cao's intent. In my opinion, we have no objection to Mr. Cao's emphasis on the entire theory of the May Fourth Movement. However, the licentiousness and depravity of the central figures of the movement at that time, as well as the tricks of selling out and seeking refuge, were already revealed, which is also undeniable. However, how could such a strange phenomenon arise from a shocking movement by noble and pure students? Mr. Cao has not yet explained this, and now I will briefly write down my opinions below:

In general, historical evolution follows the stages of social change. The occurrence of a major historical event, or the rise or fall of a class, is closely related to the culture, economy, politics, and the strength of the country at that time, as well as the bullying of foreign races. On the surface, it is controlled by a few people, but in reality, it is needed by the majority. In other words, it is produced to adapt to the times. The epoch-making May Fourth Movement is, of course, no exception. Who were the people who made the May Fourth Movement? They were students, that is, the intellectual class, that is, the class of so-called scholars in our country throughout the ages. Since the early establishment of the dynasty, scholars have occupied a superior position. Those above scholars are called grand masters, then princes and sons of heaven, and the lowest are common people. The Book of Rites says: "Rites do not go down to common people, and punishments do not go up to grand masters." Even the temples for worshiping ancestors have levels. The Book of Rites also says; The Son of Heaven has seven, the princes have five, and the grand masters have three. The scholars have one, and the common people have no temple and worship in the bedroom. Roughly speaking, scholars and above in ancient times were rulers, and common people and below were ruled. The Tang Dynasty attached the greatest importance to jinshi. At that time, the jinshi who passed the examination looked down on the yellow official. The jinshi who failed the examination could still greet the Pu Hua chief on an equal footing. (Duanyan Wenjianlu) Xue Chao had already become prime minister. Still hating not being born as a jinshi. (See Zhuyan) The jiansheng of the early Ming Dynasty could, by order of the emperor, organize land taxes and build water conservancy. (See Nanyong Zhi) Even in the remote prefectures and counties during the Qing Dynasty, talented scholars could handle litigation and enter and exit public offices. Therefore, there was a common saying at that time that there were juren grand secretaries and talented scholars and Shangshu. As for the state throughout the ages, it seems that laws are not laws, which has cultivated a kind of licentious and depraved habit among scholars, which is even more shocking. The newly appointed jinshi of the Tang Dynasty used red paper names to visit Chang'an You Pingkangfang. (This Fang is inhabited by prostitutes. See Kaiyuan Anecdotes) During the Song Dynasty, all official banquets and three school gatherings in the official government were…all prostitutes dispatched by the official to serve directly. (See Menglianglu) Wulin's old affairs describe the prostitutes of the official wine cellar, saying: "Famous prostitutes are all hidden deep in tall buildings and are not easy to call upon. …They are often occupied by people in the study, and others cannot easily climb up." It was the country that openly allowed scholars to prostitute, and scholars had the exclusive privilege to occupy noble prostitutes. Qing law officials were guilty of prostituting, and the capital was even more strictly prohibited. If caught by the patrolling censor, they would be punished with a cane, but the new Jinshi of the Qing Dynasty were the exception. At the end of the Qing Dynasty, students from Beijing Normal University wandered around the male hall (i.e., male prostitutes) outside the south city at night. When it was late at night, they could call for the city gate to be opened to return to school. These are all simple examples. Therefore, the superior status of the scholar class has not changed at all from the early days of feudal society to the end of the disguised feudal society. As for the policy of despising industry and commerce, it has been passed down in our country since ancient times. As early as the Han Dynasty, there were systems in place that forbade merchants to ride in carriages and wear silk. During the Jin Dynasty, merchants used white scarves on their foreheads to write what they were selling and their names. One foot wore white shoes and one foot wore yellow shoes. (See the note on the word merchant in Guangyun) Look at this kind of dress, isn't it more ugly than the clowns who insert jokes and make fun on the stage now. If the clothing is like this, other treatments can be inferred. However, since the Opium War (1542), although our country is still a disguised feudal society, Western imperialism has been surging eastward. Affected by it domestically, the bourgeoisie suddenly picked up. Those who have always despised him now fear that they will not be able to attach themselves to him. As for the class of seven, under this influence, they have been unable to cope with the new environment, and their former prestige will be lost. If they do not depend on the powerful, they will not be able to maintain their lives. This is just as sociologists tell us: the ruler of the political power in each era is the economically superior class in each era. At the end of the Middle Ages, capitalism was completed, and political sovereignty was exclusively occupied by the bourgeoisie and the unproductive laborers (i.e., the intellectual class) raised by them. In a certain period, unproductive laborers receive generous incomes and must be loyal to the ruling class politically. For example, monks in the Middle Ages were necessary figures to suppress and regulate the serf society in order to protect feudal property. And into capitalist society. As the monks were no longer the key to protecting capitalist property, his status and the feudal system were destroyed together. From this, employee · official · lawyer · journalist · doctor of capitalist countries. The groups or political parties organized by writers are rising instead.

The central figures of the May Fourth Movement were college students, that is, the intellectual class, that is, unproductive laborers, that is, the class of scholars in our country. They were born in an era of bourgeois prosperity, and Western culture and economy swept in. The old traditional ideas and the old social organizations have all been fundamentally shaken. Seeing that their class is approaching the end of its rope, they will collapse if they do not find a way to transform the situation. One or two heroic figures, on the one hand, need to satisfy their own desire for leadership, and on the other hand, want to maintain the past glory of their class. They seize a good topic and take an unprecedented action. So a few student representatives were born in response to the times, selling the storm and rain. On the surface, they are upright and upright, but in fact, the general skills of bureaucrats and politicians have been 『tested concretely and subtly. "The so-called" planting parties to disturb the government; the power to knock on the door and degrade; accepting bribes and slandering the court; setting up a bureau to cheat and threaten the people" (Mr. Cao quoted Qi Dong Yeyu) The old tricks of the college students in the Southern Song Dynasty were mostly reenacted as facts during the May Fourth period. In this way, the personal goals of several student representatives have already been achieved, and they have won the cheers of the people and the applause of the entire class, so the "heroes created by the times" have been realized. As for sitting in a private car, eating in a restaurant, and playing with beauties, it is a necessary act in the process of selling oneself to a political campaign, and it is also a bad habit indulged in by past scholars, which is no longer a problem.

In short, the May Fourth Movement was epoch-making, on the one hand, it ended the old situation of the college students in the Southern Song Dynasty and the past scholar class (the affairs of the college students in the Southern Song Dynasty are detailed in Zhou Mi Guixin Zazhi and Qi Dong Yeyu, which are very similar to the May Fourth Movement, which will not be described in detail here). On the other hand, the two sides created a new era for the new intellectual class. Sixteen or seventeen years have passed since the May Fourth Movement. In these sixteen or seventeen years, the phenomena that have occurred inside and outside the country's schools, as well as all the light and land activities, whether they were spread by the "May Fourth mold", are facts that everyone has seen and heard, and we don't need to argue. In short, "Don't despise the epoch-making significance of the May Fourth Movement. Don't value the nine heroes created by the times." Mr. Cao's kind of words are what we extremely agree with!

Honorable Old Woman (8)

— By Ema Shū, Translated by Ren Jun

Ringo felt as if she was about to cry out. However, a few minutes later, while she was working, she turned gloomy and pensive again, and then she began to chant Buddhist scriptures. She was still wholeheartedly entangled with the gods and Buddhas.

One evening in September, Old Woman Fan had completely cleaned the workers' dormitory, so she returned to her own home a little earlier than usual.

"Well, let me go home now to give my husband food and wipe his body. Such an old woman still has a good person waiting for her at home, haha. Please rest in peace!"

Later, not even an hour had passed when a burst of laughter and shouts, which were completely unexpected, came from the old woman in front of my house.

"Haha, honor, honor! Where is there a more glorious honor than this! Long live, long live!"

At this time, my mother, who was talking to us by the stove, unknowingly frowned and said:

"Oh, what is that old woman stirring up now? Is she crazy, or is she drunk?"

"Madam!" The old woman rushed in aggressively, shouting. "Please listen to me. My son has died in battle! An honorable death in battle! Isn't that wonderful? Eh?"

Her face was covered with tears, and her eyes were shining strangely. And she was also opening her toothless mouth to laugh. Her expression was truly miserable.

"Oh, your son has finally died in battle!" My mother's tears flowed down without her realizing it.

"Madam, why are you crying?" She sat in the doorway, laughing, and said, "There is nothing to cry about. As everyone says, this is for the country, this is an honorable death in battle. After all, my son is still wonderful. I'm really happy, so happy I can't stand it. So I've just been laughing from the beginning. Hahaha..."

She laughed even more hysterically.

According to the old woman, when she had just returned home, the people in the neighborhood had gathered there. They told her that before she had returned, the yamen had already sent notice that her son had died bravely in battle. They also used various words to comfort her.

Singapore Harbor, Part 2

— Liu Ming

"What are they doing? Rice… the red-haired devils are throwing silver coins, and the Malay ghosts are snatching them up!"

The pockmarked young man joked:

"Old man, why don't you go grab some? Send your two little devils!"

The old man saw a good number of silver coins being thrown into the sea from the first and second class area and sarcastically said to the pockmarked young man:

"You miser, are you like them? ... Look how generous they are!"

"Bah, is that generous? … They just have some ill-gotten gains and are looking for amusement!"

The pockmarked young man wiped the sweat from his face with his hand and heavily slapped the ship's railing, looking serious and earnest.

"Oh, they threw down a silver dollar!"

Several people nearby seemed surprised and envious, and they all shouted.

The old man seemed to instantly lose his humorous mood, adopting a solemn expression, and muttered to himself through clenched teeth:

"Humph, these things! …"

But from the first and second class area came the sound,

"Very good!"

On the sea surface, a dripping head and an arm holding a silver dollar emerged.

At the same time, on the deck, a voice mixed with phlegm roared out from the crowd.

"Good!"

The pockmarked young man turned around and saw that the owner of this voice was the middle-aged, fat merchant who had just returned from the pier. Standing beside him was the young man who often quoted poetry, who, with an expression of envy for the Malays, shook his head and said in a sighing tone:

"Alas, who says 'diligence is useful, play is useless'?"

The middle-aged, fat merchant was probably deeply moved by this game. He quickly wiped his face with a handkerchief, then reached into his pocket, took out a copper coin, and threw it towards a Malay man in a nearby rowboat. The Malay man quickly glanced at the thrown object, as if he immediately understood it was a copper coin. He turned his face away and shook his hand dismissively, then rowed away.

"Damn it! Isn't that money?"

The middle-aged, fat merchant said, his face turning red and displeased.

"People, they only want silver ones, bright and shiny ones are what they respect!"

Someone in the crowd said mockingly.

The pockmarked young man laughed heartily, feeling pleased.

The middle-aged, fat merchant, seeming unconvinced, lowered his sweat-covered forehead and desperately searched his pockets.

The pockmarked young man deliberately shouted loudly at the Malay men on the sea:

"Black devils, don't look down on people, we'll throw silver coins . . . "

The middle-aged, fat merchant unbuttoned his clothes, looked into his pockets while pulling at the edges, and said anxiously and irritably:

"Damn! Where did it go? Just now it was still … "

The poetry-loving young man stood beside him, pretending to help him search, and asked:

"What are you looking for?"

"That… that… fake coin!"

"Hey, didn't you just use it to buy cigarettes?" Suddenly, cheers erupted from that side, and everyone immediately turned their heads to look. The middle-aged, fat merchant took the opportunity to slip into the cabin.

The Weaver Girl's Curse

— Da Bao

For you, young,

happy men and women,

weaving patterned clothes,

Let your youth blossom,

Let your love flourish:

But the blossoms of our youth,

Wither before this loom.

Whose youth does not sprout love?

Heaven endowed us with bright eyes.

Heaven endowed us with bright eyes,

Watching the turning of the yarn,

Blurring…

Our youth

Is entirely devoted to this endless labor,

For the sake of

Decorating your life's desires.

The whole world,

Happy lovers wearing patterned clothes,

Forget,

Forget that there are still us ragged weaver girls here.

Sisters,

Weave, weave,

For these happy people,

Weave mourning clothes,

Let their youth die,

Let their happiness die,

So that we may have a moment of rest.

Sisters,

Weave, weave,

For these happy people,

Weave mourning clothes,

Let their youth die,

Let their happiness die,

For our own ragged youth,

Embroider patterned clothes!

National Games Day Six: Shanghai Wins Three Track and Field Championships; Eleven New National Records Set in Six Days; Men's Decathlon and Men's and Women's Swimming Start Today; Men's Tennis and Basketball Schedules Tightest Today

Yesterday was the sixth day of the National Games. The men's and women's track and field events have all concluded. The Shanghai team, with a great victory, won the men's field, men's track, and women's track and field championships. Yesterday, three new national records were set in the men's 400 meters and women's 200 meters and softball throw. In the past six days, a total of eleven new records have been set. In the women's 400-meter relay, the Shanghai team was disqualified due to a foul, which is a pity. The men's decathlon and men's and women's swimming will all begin today. Swimming is sure to cause a sensation due to the appearance of Yang Xiuqiong. Among the ball games, men's basketball and men's tennis are the tightest today. The men's doubles will hold the quarterfinals, and the men's singles will hold the semifinals. All the experts are out, and the gains and losses are extremely important. A full stadium is to be expected.

Women's 400-Meter Relay Final: Shanghai Team Disqualified; Wang Kai's Photo Proves Wrong Lane; Zhang Boling's Investigation Confirms Evidence; National Record Set Was Cancelled; Guangdong Team Takes Championship

In the women's 400-meter relay final, a total of six teams participated. Although the Shanghai team took first place with a score of 54.5 seconds, unfortunately, the fourth runner, Li Sen, ran in the wrong lane. The Eastern Team, which came in second, protested verbally. After an investigation by Zhang Boling, chairman of the judging committee, the evidence was confirmed, with a clear photo taken by Wang Kai as proof. Therefore, Zhang has decided to cancel the Shanghai team's first-place qualification, and the second-place Guangdong team will be promoted. The following will be promoted in order. Because there were only six teams, the sixth place is vacant. The determined rankings are as follows:

Overall Championship Scores

Men's

Shanghai 8 points Liaoning 4 points

Malaysia 3 points Beiping 2 points

Shanxi 2 points Nanjing 1 point

Women's

Shanghai 4 points Malaysia 3 points

Guangdong 2 points Fujian 1 point

Circumstances of the Final

The final was held at 2:00 PM. Qian Hangsu of Shanghai ran the first leg, Jiao Yulian the second, Peng Aipu the third, and Li Sen the fourth. The Shanghai team took the lead all the way, leaving Guangdong behind by about five or six meters. However, when the third and fourth runners handed off the baton, Peng and Li did not handle the baton well. Zhao Yunshan of Guangdong emerged, and Li Sen chased after her, winning over the Guangdong team by a shoulder. The score was 54.5 seconds, breaking the national record. Guangdong was first, Malaysia third, and Qing and Min were second.

Guangdong Team Protests

Immediately after the final, the Guangdong team suddenly discovered that Shanghai's last runner ran in the wrong lane. They quickly protested verbally to Zhang Boling, chairman of the judging committee, saying that someone had seen it, but there was only testimonial evidence, not physical evidence, so they could not speak credulously. They proposed that the photos taken by Wang Kai be examined.

Photo as Evidence

Fortunately, Wang Kai had taken photos at both the starting and ending points, which were exceptionally clear. It was discovered that in the photos taken by Wang Kai, Qian Hangsu, the first runner of Shanghai, was in the fifth lane, while Li Sen, at the ending point, was in the sixth lane. Therefore, Shanghai's foul was extremely obvious, and the evidence was confirmed. The photos on the competition results are sufficient for reference. From this, it can be seen.

Disqualification Decided

Therefore, after Zhang Boling examined the two photos, he believed that Shanghai had indeed fouled. The Guangdong team's protest did not require convening a meeting, and it was decided to directly cancel the Shanghai team's qualification. An official announcement will be published today. According to general speculation, the Shanghai team's third and fourth legs did not hand off the baton well, so it was during this period that Li Sen ran in the wrong lane. The pre-race inspection report stated that there was no error in the lines where each person was standing. The last runner of Beiping also discovered that Li Sen was in front of him, obstructing his path. Therefore, Shanghai's foul is clear. The results were still good, and it is a pity to cancel them.

Dai Shuguo Overwhelms Fu Jincheng: New Record Set in 400 Meters

Breaking the National Record Held for Seven Years

The men's 400-meter final was held at 2:10 PM on the 15th. The participants had less than twenty minutes to rest after the semi-finals. Everyone expected that Fu Jincheng and Dai Shuguo would fight a bloody battle, especially Fu, who had the highest chance of winning a championship. Eight people participated in the final. Fu was in the outermost circle, and Dai was in the innermost circle. After the starting gun, Fu and Dai immediately strode forward. Before 100 meters, they were already at the front. Dai was depressed in the semi-finals. At this time, he was determined to win, his steps were wide and light. When he was about 300 meters away, he was about one meter ahead of Fu, gritted his teeth and sprinted straight. Fu also swore to fight with all his strength, not letting go. At 350 meters, he was about to catch up, but Dai worked even harder to sprint. Fu could not catch up, and Dai finally defeated Fu Jincheng, who was frightening for a while, by about one meter, winning the championship with a result of 51.2 seconds, breaking the national record of 52.4 seconds held by Liu Changchun for seven years. After the report was heard throughout the venue, applause thundered. Li Yanxiang finished three meters behind Fu, taking third place. In this event, Shanghai got 7 points, Malaysia 5 points, Jiangsu 4 points, Liaoning 3 points, and Guangdong 3 points. After the competition, Wu Xingya gave the awards.

10,000 Meter Final: Gu Desheng Wins with Constant Strength

Sets New Record for the Games at 34 Minutes, 11.6 Seconds

Excellent Time Distribution Per Lap is Worth Emulating

The 10,000-meter race was one of the last track and field events of the Games. Participants included Shanxi's Gu Desheng, Li Denggui, Wang Huibin, Chen Shusen, and Shanghai's Wang Zhenglin, Jiangsu's Jin Zhongkang and other athletes. Most of the participants feared the reputation of Shanxi and did not dare to compete. Therefore, many temporarily withdrew. Only more than 30 people actually participated in the competition. Among them, the four bald heads of Shanxi were the most noticed by the audience. In addition, the announcer reported that "Number 205, Gu Desheng, has hope of winning,"

Zhang Liang's Strategy: Shanghai's Wang Leads First

Before the game, Shanghai's Wang Zhenglin and Zhang Liang secretly discussed a plan to challenge the tiger on the mountain. At the start, Zhang Liang would run fast, leading the Shanxi generals to follow, so that the Shanxi generals would be exhausted, and then Zhang Liang would give up, and Wang Zhenglin would take the opportunity to defeat the Shanxi athletes. After the start, Zhang Liang ran hard, but the Shanxi generals were experienced and were not moved. Zhang gave up and stopped running at 2,300 meters. In the first lap, Gu Desheng was in sixth place. In the second lap, Zhang Liang was in first place, Jin Zhongkang was in second place, and Gu Desheng was in fourth place. At 1,500 meters, Zhang Liang finished first, with a result of 4 minutes and 48 seconds.

3,000 Meters: New Record

At 3,000 meters, Gu and Wang competed fiercely. Wang Zhenglin's result was 9 minutes and 55 seconds, and Gu Desheng's result was 9 minutes and 55.4 seconds, both breaking the national record (the national 3,000-meter record is 10 minutes and 5 seconds). In the eighth lap, Li Denggui was in first place, Wang Huibin was in second place, Gu Desheng was in third place, and Huang Ruiwen of Guangxi was in fourth place. In the ninth lap, Gu Desheng jumped to lead the pack, and Wang Zhenglin also bravely surpassed Li Denggui. At this time, Jin Zhongkang was in sixth place, Niu Hongling of Shandong was in seventh place, Chen Shusen of Shanxi was in ninth place, and He Baoshan of Jiangsu was in seventh place.

5,000 Meters: Amazing Result

At 5,000 meters, Gu Desheng broke the national 5,000-meter record with 16 minutes and 53 seconds. Wang Zhenglin followed with 16 minutes and 56 seconds, also breaking the national record. From the ninth lap to the twentieth lap, Gu Desheng took the lead all the way, as if in no man's land, while Wang Zhenglin and Li Denggui competed fiercely behind him. In the sixteenth lap, Wang won over Li by about four meters.

Swift as a Swallow: Straight to the Finish Line

At 9,000 meters, Gu Desheng's stride suddenly became larger, swift as a swallow, and the others could not reach him. At this time, Gu was 80 meters away from the second place and three and a half laps ahead of the last person. Gu finished 9,500 meters in 32 minutes and 40 seconds. In the last lap, Gu's pace was even stronger, rushing straight to the finish line with a result of 34 minutes and 11.6 seconds, breaking the Games record, but it was a pity that he failed to break the national record. The second Wang Zhilin and the third Wang Huibin competed fiercely. Wang Zhenglin narrowly took the second place, and Li Denggui retreated to fourth place. Huang Ruiwen of Guangxi, a famous general, had broken the national record in Guangxi, and also won fifth place this time. Zhongkang, who is old and strong, won sixth place and deserves praise. He Baoshan was eliminated from the list in seventh place.

Full Results Are Worth Referring To

The champion Gu Desheng's result was 34 minutes and 11.6 seconds (the official record announced by the conference). According to the reporter's timing of the second and third places yesterday, Wang Zhenglin's result was 44 minutes and 32.4 seconds, and Wang Huibin's result was 34 minutes and 32.6 seconds. Hong Kong, Guangdong, and Malaya Form a Triumvirate; Swimming Begins Competition Today

The Unexpected Rise of Guangxi Province's Athletes Should Not Be Overlooked

Yang Anni, Future Mermaid, Will Dominate All

The Men's and Women's Swimming Championships will begin this afternoon at the swimming pool. Participants include nineteen units for men, namely Lu, Fei, Qing, Jiangxi, Hebei, Zhejiang, Wei, Beijing, Guangxi, Fujian, Jiangsu, Ping, Anhui, Xinjiang, Hai, Hong Kong, Guangdong, Malaya, and Shanghai; and only seven units for women, namely Beijing, Guangxi, Fujian, Hong Kong, Guangdong, Malaya, and Shanghai. The schedule for the first day includes five heats and three semi-finals. The events are the men's and women's 50-meter freestyle heats and semi-finals, the men's 100-meter freestyle heat, the women's 100-meter backstroke heat, and the men's 200-meter breaststroke heat and semi-finals. The strength of each unit in this competition is exceptionally strong, especially Hong Kong, Guangdong, Malaya, and Shanghai. Xu Chengji Is Polite

Without Fully Displaying His Talents

National player Xu Chengji's tennis skills have reached the pinnacle, needless to say. He is very confident of winning the singles championship this time. From the second set onwards, Xu still took the lead with four games, but because he was intentionally being polite, not wanting to embarrass the opponent, he gave away another big gift, eventually ending the match with 6-1.

Zeng Duancai Is Steady and Admirable

Winning Two Sets Consecutively

Java's Zeng Duancai's tennis skills are just so-so, but he is steady and admirable. Jiangsu's Xu Cida is an unknown and lacks both talent and knowledge. Unexpectedly, he then fell into a slump and was repeatedly scored on by Zeng, leading remotely with 5-2. Although he pulled back a game later, it was of no help to the overall situation, ending with 6-3.

Lin Wangsu Escaped from the Jaws of Death

Becoming Famous Overnight

Left-arm General Lin Wangsu was well-known and invincible two years ago. His tennis skills have not improved in recent days. Beiping's Xie Hua is not well-known, but his skills are quite commendable. His forehand strokes are heavy and powerful, but his backhand lacks confidence, and his experience is also lacking. Otherwise, he could have defeated Wangsu yesterday and ascended to glory in one step. But the result of yesterday's battle surprised the audience, and Wangsu was also very frightened. As soon as the bell rang, the war broke out. Xie was not Wang's opponent, but he was unwilling to succumb to the powerful enemy, so he resisted desperately, running tirelessly. In the end, he was slightly weaker and lost the first set 2-6. In the second set, Xie was extra careful, sweeping left and right, using both strength and gentleness, and even won three consecutive games. Wangsu also had to sigh at the ball. Then Lin got the service game, and Xie steadily and softly drew the ball, sending it to the left, right, front, and back continuously. Lin was exhausted and resigned. Xie won back a set with 6-1, tying the score.

Although Defeated, Still Glorious

The next set was a matter of life and death. During the preliminary competition, Xie had admitted that he was no match, but at this time, he had the hope of seeing the sun and overwhelming the strong enemy, which was his wish to become famous overnight. So he was ambitious and tried to expand his potential. Lin knew that the opponent was not weak, and he had received a lesson in the previous set, so he was extra careful and did not dare to panic. Otherwise, if he failed, not only would the championship prospects be greatly affected, but also his personal reputation would be swept away. With such psychology on both sides, the competition became even more intense. Lin served first and won, and Xie paid tribute in the same way and gave back even more. Lin also won two consecutive games, taking the lead with 3-2. In the next game, Xie served, remembering a 1-2 lag, followed by an out-of-bounds ball, and the referee mistakenly judged that Xie won, getting the game, and then getting two more games, Xie led with 5-3. Lin tried hard to catch up with a game, and fell behind with 4-5, Xie served in the next game, which was the key to victory or defeat. Unexpectedly, Xie was too eager to win, but he couldn't control himself, and his wild balls appeared repeatedly, resulting in a 5-5 tie. Lin served and won the first game, taking the lead with 6-5. Xie fought back carefully, playing to a 6-6 tie. At this time, Xie was extremely anxious, not as calm as in the second set, so there were occasional mistakes, giving the opponent a chance to attack. Although they played another 7-7 tie, the overall situation was gone, and there was nothing he could do. In the end, Wangsu won the final victory with 9-7.

Chen Qi'an Almost Suffered a Mishap

After Suffering Comes Happiness

Chen Qi'an is a famous player from Malaya. He almost failed in his battle against Beiping's Wen Yawen yesterday. At the beginning of the match, Wen used beautiful strokes, intercepting both sides, sometimes far, sometimes near, suddenly left, suddenly right, swinging the plague array. Little Chen had no way to go and lost five camps in a row. Although he pulled back a game later, he eventually lost the set 1-6. At the beginning of the second set, Qi'an found the way and won two consecutive games. The situation turned around, and General Wen was confident and didn't take it seriously. 3-2, 4-3, repeatedly taking the lead, Chen then followed closely, never leaving. The air was quite tense for a while. Then Chen desperately counterattacked, instead coming from behind with 5-4, 6-5. After a very long battle in the next game, they reached a 6-6 tie. At this time, General Wen broke out again, randomly scattering the plague sand. It really worked immediately, and he turned defeat into victory again with 7-6, 8-7. Although Little Chen suffered a small setback, he was unwilling to give up. He raised his arms and shouted, and pulled out three cities in a row, so the situation of one set each was barely created with 10-8. In the third set, both sides felt exhausted, but victory or defeat was at this critical moment, so they all fought to the death. Little Chen was particularly brave, 4-2, 5-3, leading all the way. Inadvertently, General Wen used his old trick, long strokes and short interceptions, attacking from left and right, and winning three consecutive games, taking the lead again with 6-5. Jiang Chao is agile, Shao Yougong is stable, Huang Jingui is refreshing, Fu Zhibin is fierce, and Huang Guorong is exquisite. The front and back are connected, forming a cohesive force. The generals of the Shanghai mixed team, such as Tang Zuolin and Shen Longzhang guarding the iron gate, Yu Qiaxing and Yu Chuhua as defenders, Zhang Jinhai and Cao Qinfang as forwards, and Shen Jinda and Li Zushou, are like a tiger with wings. The combat effectiveness is also very strong. At that time, when the two heroes fight each other, who will win is difficult to predict.

According to the performance, the leather ball used is the Yong Zi brand leather ball approved by the Shanghai Small Ball Association, produced by Yonghe Industrial Company, which can be called a standard leather ball.

Soccer

Old Rivals Meet Again on a Narrow Road; Shanghai and Guangdong Obtain the Right to the Quarterfinals; Shanghai Eliminates Hubei 10-1; Guangdong Defeats Nanjing 12-1

Yesterday, soccer entered the semi-quarterfinal stage. Shanghai played against Hubei at 9:00 AM, and Guangdong played against Nanjing at 4:00 PM. The strength difference between the two sides was too great, and both sides became one-sided. In addition, the field was muddy and the water had not dried up, so the performances were not exciting, and the audience lost interest. As a result, Shanghai won against Hubei 10-1, and Guangdong won against Nanjing 12-1, obtaining the right to the quarterfinals. Shanghai and Guangdong will meet on the afternoon of the 18th at 3:00 PM to compete for the right to the finals. Who will win in the Central Plains competition? In the previous National Games, Guangdong was defeated by Shanghai in the finals. Now they meet again in the quarterfinals. Will they avenge their humiliation? Tens of thousands of fans are watching and waiting.

Shanghai Beats the Hubei Team Soundly; Hubei Finally Scored One Point in the End

Yesterday morning at 9:00, the soccer match between Shanghai and Hubei began. The strength difference between the two sides was huge. Hubei was always under the Shanghai team's siege. They could not attack, nor could they defend. Eleven minutes after the kickoff, Li Yichen attacked the hinterland and lightly kicked the ball into the net. The Hubei army defended with all its might, using the muddy and waterlogged terrain to its advantage to deal with the Shanghai army. For twenty minutes, no further goals were scored. The Shanghai army then unleashed its divine power and changed its strategy. Sun Jinshun, Feng Yunyou, and Dai Linjing each scored a goal, ending the first half with a score of 4-0. Changing sides and fighting again, Shanghai's momentum grew stronger. Within three minutes, Zhan Linjing scored with a header. Soon, the Hubei side conceded two more goals. Although they had a free kick opportunity, they did not score. After a long struggle, Sun Jinshun and Dai Linjing of Shanghai each scored another goal. Soon, the Hubei army counterattacked and won a corner kick. Right inside forward Fu Zhibin received the ball and lightly shot it into the net, scoring the most precious goal. The whole stadium erupted in cheers, because the audience's psychology was to sympathize with the weak. Finally, Li Yichen seized an opportunity and scored another goal. The second half was 6-1, and the total score was 10-1. The Hubei army was defeated.

Shanghai Team

Zhang Rongcai, Li Ning, Jiang Shanjing, Gu Shangquan, Feng Yunyou, Liang Shutang, Wan Xianghua, Li Yichen, Dai Linjing, Sun Jinshun, Jia Youliang

Guangdong Eliminates Nanjing; Twelve to One, Avoiding a Shutout

Yesterday afternoon at 4:00, the soccer match between Guangdong and Nanjing began. After two or three rounds, the ball was at the feet of Xiao Heitan, who showed his power and rushed in, successfully opening the scoring. Soon, Yang Shuiyi received the ball and shot from a distance, sending the ball into the net. Nanjing launched a counterattack, but their passing was poor, and the ball was often intercepted midway. After a fierce battle, Nanjing did not gain anything, while Guangdong's score gradually increased. Tan Jiangbai, Yang Shuiyi, and others frequently scored. The first half ended with Guangdong leading 7-0.

After the break, the battle resumed. The Guangdong army's five tigers clashed left and right, as if they were in no man's land. Xiao Heitan roamed the entire field, his power undiminished. The Beijing side was helpless and unable to resist, and successively lost four cities. At this time, Yang Renwei, the left winger of Beijing, had a plan of borrowing an arrow with his back to the domain. He broke into the enemy camp alone and attacked the goal with lightning speed. With good luck, he scored, and the cheering crowd avoided a shutout. Finally, Li Hongqing, the left forward of Hong Kong, completed a dozen goals in the twilight, winning 12-1.
