Women's Volleyball

The Guangdong Team Demonstrates Power and Skill, Defeating Hong Kong

2-3: The Women Display Their Majestic Power and Divine Abilities, a Fierce Battle That Is Hard to Resolve

In the second round of the women's volleyball competition, there were two matches yesterday. (1) Shanghai versus Henan: Henan had already declared their forfeit, so Shanghai automatically gained the right to advance to the next round. (2) Guangdong versus Hong Kong: A close sibling rivalry, exceptionally intense. In the end, Guangdong won. The match results are as follows:

Siblings Clash, Court Heats Up

When it comes to volleyball talent, due to the convenience of competition and training, most successes belong to the daughters of the South. This is originally governed by talent and environment, and cannot be forced upon others. Both Hong Kong and Guangdong are skilled in this area. When heroes meet, each focusing on their own future, their fight will naturally be a cut above. With fame and fortune at stake, their fraternal feelings, however strong, can only be set aside. Based on this stance, the audience at the women's volleyball court became even more crowded. Men and women mixed together, and the side stands were packed. Boy Scouts were busy maintaining order, demonstrating the strong appeal of both teams. The excitement of the volleyball court was indeed the greatest of this year's event.

Fit and Beautiful Women Display Their Divine Abilities

Around 2:00 PM, the Guangdong team, led by Yang Xingfen, took to the court. The Hong Kong team, led by Zhu Yingfen, followed. These heroines, amid their flowery beauty, possessed a spirit of fortitude and strength. Their demeanor was magnificent, truly worthy of being called fit and beautiful women. The match began at 3:00 PM, with Hong Kong taking the initiative and setting records. Zhu Jiaoxin gritted his teeth, unwilling to easily concede his former glory. He quickly caught up, making progress and adjustments in both offense and defense. However, the back row defense was weak, so when the ball entered shallowly into their territory, it was difficult to recover. As a result, they easily lost the first set with a score of 21-17.

Roaring, They Retake a Set

With Hong Kong winning the first set, the entire stadium became even more lively. They seemed to be sailing smoothly, full of momentum. At 5-5, Yan Xiurong and Yang Yuqiong of the Guangdong team became determined to win, whispering to each other and plotting a decisive move. Sure enough, a ball entered the territory, and they roared in victory. Despite their small stature, their strength was extraordinary. Leaping and striking from afar, they entered the enemy's baseline. The Hong Kong team was busy defending the net and did not expect such a surprise attack. The ball entered their rear, and they couldn't recover. From then on, the momentum shifted, and they switched sides at 11-7. Lin Dezhen of the Guangdong team committed a serving error, and the Hong Kong team also scored some points. In the end, Guangdong won with a score of 21-17.

Fierce Battle, Veteran Assassin

With both sides winning and losing, the competition was exceptionally fierce under the premise of equally matched opponents. The audience on the sidelines shouted and cheered. The sharp cries of "Wonderful, wonderful, wonderful" from some of the female athletes created a chaotic atmosphere. The first half of the third set was uneventful. In the second half, the scores became close, and both sides grew anxious. They engaged in close combat, with no flaws to exploit. Thus, they advanced from 20-20 to 22-22. Finally, Yan Xiurong took advantage of a high ball opportunity, rushed to the net, and made a decisive kill. Although Yan Xiurong is not old, she has the demeanor of a veteran. Calm and composed, she is indeed admirable. The score was 24-22.

Dazzling, the Guangdong Army Suffers Another Setback

The fourth set began amidst the majestic power of the women. Like dense clouds and sudden rain, it was difficult to distinguish the victor. Hong Kong could attack, but their killing blows lacked strength. The back-row players, Ye Huiwen and Tang Meiyu, were also relatively weak. Under such circumstances, they felt exhausted. To the audience, it was dazzling, and they immediately felt overwhelmed. In the first half of the fourth set, Guangdong took an 11-7 lead and switched sides. However, they carelessly lost Jingzhou in the second half. The Central Plains were again overrun with invaders, and as a result, Hong Kong created a 21-18 lead.

Blood and Passion, Skillful Control

The fifth set was the crucial point for the right to advance to the next round. The Guangdong team gave it their all, pouring out their blood and passion. Sure enough, they achieved remarkable results, narrowly winning 11-9. When they switched sides, the Hong Kong team unexpectedly adopted a polite and humble attitude, giving away points. The Guangdong players were able to roam freely on the volleyball court, attacking relentlessly. The Hong Kong team, knowing that the situation was hopeless, played casually, as if strumming a pipa. Guangdong skillfully controlled the situation and won 21-12. The reason for their victory was partly due to Hong Kong's relaxation and partly due to their rich experience. The overall score was 3-2.

Strange Behavior, Zhejiang Defeated

The Hong Kong team arrived for practice at 12:30 PM yesterday. Their heroic spirit was evident as they were supported by ten female athletes. Their veteran demeanor was fully displayed. At the beginning, the Zhejiang team came onto the court, ready to serve. He Shuju's first serve failed. Li Wolin of Hong Kong rescued the ball and passed it to the left corner. Lu Baining saw an opportunity, raised his arm, and struck quickly, opening the scoring. Lu Xitie, the captain of the Zhejiang team, had always been resolute and unwilling to be outdone. During Hong Kong's serve, he stood alone, blocking the incoming attacks. There were some tricks, and the scores remained close from 6-6, 7-7, to 8-8 and 9-9. Although Hong Kong was experienced, they felt at a loss. In the second half, after switching sides, Lu Baining of the Hong Kong team served. The ball was flat and hard, and there was no one to receive it in Zhejiang's backcourt. As a result, a series of shots hit their mark, scoring six consecutive points and leaving Zhejiang with no chance of survival. Amid strange behavior, Zhejiang lost the first set 17-21.

Farewell to the Old, Welcome to the New, Another Loss

In the second set, Zhejiang hoped to recover their lost ground, but they were unlucky. They lost four points early on. After gradually catching up, Hong Kong added to the score again. When Zhang Xihu served, Hong Kong returned the ball. Zhang then rushed to the net, blocking the way out. With self-created plays, it was a scene of "farewell to the old, welcome to the new." From this, it was evident that Zhejiang lacked organization. Hong Kong took an 11-7 lead before switching sides. Zhejiang's counterattack was fierce, but unfortunately, there were many setbacks. Under the psychological pressure of a narrow win, they widened the score difference. The final score was 21-13. The athletes from the West Lake region remained under the control of the Hong Kong team.

Breaking Through Barriers, Surprisingly Turning the Tide

In the third set, Zhejiang showed some progress. Hong Kong failed to be humble and retained some arrogance. As a result, He Shusheng and others in Zhejiang successfully coordinated their attacks. In an instant, they boldly broke through barriers, miraculously escaping death and turning the tide. However, the score never reflected this newfound energy, with the final score being a narrow 19-21.

Strengthening Defenses, Ultimately Winning

In the fourth set, after a break, Zhejiang intended to launch a rapid attack, but due to a lack of coordination and defensive work in the entire team, Zhang Xihu found it difficult to fight alone. Thus, the score gap widened again. The first half ended hastily, with Hong Kong taking an 11-5 lead. The outcome was largely determined. After switching sides, before Zhejiang could launch an attack, the three players in Hong Kong's front row had strengthened their defenses, preventing any disruption of the internal order. Amid the audience's cheers, Hong Kong again defeated Zhejiang by a large margin of 21-9. The overall score was 2-1.

(2) Shanghai Wins Against Hebei

Stealing Camps, Conquering Strategically

The second match was held at 3:00 PM. Qian Jima summoned the Shanghai and Hebei teams to battle. The Shanghai team included national team veterans such as Cao Tingzan and Qiu Guangxie. Their glorious records had been established long ago. Zhang Yicheng of Hebei took the initiative and scored two points. Chen Dongcai of the Shanghai team effectively countered, tying the score. From then on, in the chaotic situation, the Shanghai team's attacks through the middle were lacking. Knowing that Hebei was known for its Nankai veterans, their net blocking and attacks were blocked by the opponent's high jumps. However, they took advantage of the gaps, stealing camps and conquering strategically, a proven tactic in warfare. A small display of skill caused the honest Hebei to fall apart. Shanghai won the set 21-17 by conquering strategically.

Qiu and Cao Display Their Power, Winning Two More Sets

In the second set, Shanghai pressed the attack. Qiu Guangxie served with great accuracy, contributing significantly. Cao Tingzan coordinated in the middle, and his skills were unique. Hebei relied on situational changes, focusing on opportunities. Thus, when high balls came, they were sent to the front, where the middle row raised high and the front row gently hit them down, creating a clever coordination between the front and back. They once led 7-6. However, when Qiu Guangxie served again, the momentum shifted back to Shanghai, and they faced a do-or-die situation. With smooth and rapid attacks, Shanghai won another set. The score was 21-7.

Artillery Bombardment, Three Straight Sets

In the third set, Hebei showed some progress in their struggle. However, their counter-attacking power was extremely weak. They were busy parrying the attacks. Unable to withstand the heavy pressure from the Shanghai team, the tense situation did not improve. When both sides reached 12 points, Shanghai launched an artillery bombardment, destroying all defensive structures. In this set, Shanghai achieved final success, quickly advancing to the next round with three straight sets. The score was 21-14.

All-Around Championship Prediction: Liaoning Highly Favored, Shanghai Second

Pentathlon

Guo Jie of Liaoning is the most skilled in the pentathlon, with excellent performance in running, jumping, and throwing. Chen Baoqiu of Hubei will participate in the pentathlon. Baoqiu excels in the triathlon, but his javelin and discus throws are likely to be inferior to Guo Jie's. In addition to Guo, Liaoning also has Li Shiming. Li's javelin throw is 47 meters, long jump is 6 meters, discus throw is 30 meters, 200-meter run is 24 seconds, and the 1500-meter run is his forte. Hao Chunde of Shanghai has been disqualified. Wang Jizhun is the national record holder, but his recent performance has declined, and he may not be able to defend his championship. Ji Demao of Shanxi and Peng Yongxin of Beiping are also expected to finish in the top five or six.

Decathlon

The championship likely belongs to veteran Zhang Lingjia. Zhou Changxing of Liaoning was the decathlon champion at last year's North China Games. He has a chance of winning the silver medal this year. Wang Shilin of Beiping and Liang Zhichu of Guangdong are also expected to score points.

Two Relay Races

In the 400-meter relay, the Malayan team has the strongest overall strength, followed by Liaoning and Shanghai. Liaoning's team includes Liu Changchun, Wu Jingyao, Jin Changxian, and Li Shiming. Shanghai's team includes emerging young athletes Chen Yongfu, Huang Feilong, Dong Shichu, and Jiang Songping. In the 1600-meter relay, Shanghai should have no problem winning the championship with Dong Shuzhao and Dai Shuguo. Liaoning will also strive for the silver medal in the 1600-meter relay. Liu Changchun will run the 400-meter leg, and Li Shiming and Dong Hanwen are also strong. However, they face strong opponents such as Fu Jincheng from the Malayan team.

Men's and Women's National Martial Arts

National Martial Arts Pellet Shooting Finals: Wei Wenqing of Henan First, Liu Yuhua Has a One-Woman Show

The National Games Martial Arts competition began yesterday morning at 9:00 AM with the men's and women's pellet shooting finals. Because the number of participants was small, it ended at 11:00 AM. From 1:00 PM in the afternoon, the men's group equipment sparring preliminary rounds were held. Finally, the men's wrestling second round was held, ending around 5:00 PM. The details are recorded separately below.

Pellet Shooting Finals

In the men's and women's pellet shooting competition in the morning, there were twelve male athletes participating: Wang Fuhai, Ning Haiting, Qu Guotian, and Liu Chenheng from Beiping; Zhang Haiqin, Liu Quantu, Zhang Qing, and Wei Wenqing from Henan; Zhao Xiuting from Shandong, who withdrew from the competition; Zhao Youlian and Zheng Liren from Shanghai; and Jian Fengxiang from Hunan. There was only one female participant, Ms. Liu Yuhua from Henan, who could be said to have a one-woman show. The pellet distance for women was 15 meters. Liu Yuhua started first, firing three pellets in a row, none of which hit the target. It wasn't until the second round of shooting that she hit one pellet out of three, scoring two points, just barely avoiding getting a zero score. Most interestingly, after the competition, Ms. Liu playfully shot two pellets with the bow, both hitting the bullseye. Ms. Liu exclaimed, "How infuriating, how infuriating!" The men's group competition resulted in the selection of six athletes as winners. Their ranks, names, and scores are listed below.

Wrestling Finals Today

The second round of martial arts wrestling was held after the equipment sparring preliminary rounds. Zhang Wenshan, the big fat man from Beiping, waddled onto the stage. His opponent was Ma Wenkui, a wrestler from Nanjing. Although Ma was not as fat as Zhang, he was tall, strong, and muscular. The two began their fight, and after three rounds, they were evenly matched, true rivals. When the fourth round began, Ma knew that he could not win by force, so he used skill. As he grabbed Zhang's clothing, he raised his right foot and hooked Zhang's calf. Zhang fell, and the onlookers applauded. Judging from yesterday's events, Ma Wenkui has a good chance of winning the championship. How will it turn out? We'll have to wait for today's finals.

Review of Men's and Women's Track and Field: Commendable Progress in All Events

The 6th National Games men's and women's track and field competitions concluded yesterday after six days of hard work. The all-around competitions will begin today. There were 31 male track teams, 33 male field teams, and 21 female track and field teams participating, which is more than in the previous National Games, a welcome phenomenon. Shanghai, relying on its average talent and gathering of athletes, won three championships, which was expected. The Malayan compatriots returned to China for the first time and showed their talent, posing a great threat to all teams. They won the silver medal in the men's track and the women's track and field competitions, and also ranked seventh in the men's field competition, which is commendable. Other teams such as Sichuan, Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Jiangxi, Guangxi, and Weihaiwei, which failed to score in previous games, also made inroads, showing that track and field sports have gradually become popular throughout the country. It is expected that the next games will be even more heated and that the results will be further improved. In terms of individual event results, Fu Baolu's pole vault of 3.90 meters and Peng Yongxin's javelin throw of 50.275 meters both broke national records, and Liu Furun's shot put of 12.30 meters broke the Games record. These performances were outstanding. Especially Fu Baolu's pole vault, which almost broke the Far East record and approached the world record, was the biggest harvest of the Games. The other events, although not breaking records, were very close to the old records. In the high jump event, if Wu Bixian had not been disqualified, he might have set a new standard. In the men's track events, Dai Shuguo's 400-meter time of 52.2 seconds broke Liu Changchun's national record of 52.6 seconds, which had stood for seven years. Jia Lianren's 800-meter time of 2 minutes and 2.1 seconds was also remarkable, and the second and third place finishers, Li Shiming and Dong Shuzhao, also exceeded the old record. It is a pity that the other events did not break all the records, either due to weather conditions or the looseness of the track. In the women's track and field events, except for the 100-meter hurdles and the shot put, all national and Games records were shattered, which is a shame for the men's group. The increasing development of women's sports in China is evident here. In terms of individuals, Li Sen is undoubtedly the most outstanding athlete, and she is now firmly established as the top sprinter in China. Deng Yinjiao, who returned from abroad, showed her talent, and her long jump result was able to break the 5-meter barrier, which added a lot of color to the Games. Qian Xingsu and Chen Rongtang were able to maintain their inherent prestige. It is hoped that the winners will not be arrogant and the losers will not be discouraged, but will continue to work hard and strive for excellence, so that they will be able to enter the world stage in the future, which is not a luxury.

Mayor Wu Hosts a Banquet for Athletes Tonight: 6:30 PM in the Gymnasium

Mayor Wu will host a banquet for all athletes, team leaders, and staff in the gymnasium at 6:30 PM this afternoon, and will also show a movie.

Shanghai YMCA Welcomes Team Leaders at Yesterday's Banquet

The Shanghai YMCA held a banquet on the ninth floor of its building in Baixianqiao at 7:30 PM last night to welcome the National Games athletes and leaders. All directors and staff of the YMCA were present to warmly greet the guests. In addition to the invited athletes and leaders, there were also National Games staff and journalists. More than 200 people attended. After the dinner, the chairman, Mr. Lu Gan Chen, the general secretary of the YMCA, gave a welcome speech on behalf of all members. He was followed by Mr. Wang Zhengting, the honorary president of the YMCA, who said that the YMCA was the first to promote sports, and that the rapid progress of sports in China is a cause for national celebration. However, compared with the level of sports in other countries, there is still a gap, and he hoped that everyone would work hard. Finally, there was music by the Zhu brothers and songs by the YMCA's public singing group to add to the entertainment. All attendees enjoyed themselves immensely and dispersed.

Wu Xingya Receives Hubei Athletes

The National Games opened, and athletes from all over the country gathered in Shanghai. Wu Xingya, the Director of the Shanghai Social Affairs Bureau, originally from Hubei, hosted a reception at the Dadong Restaurant last night for the athletes and representatives from Hubei province attending the National Games, due to their shared hometown relationship. Those attending included Chen Shucheng, President of Wuchang Zhonghua University, Liu Changhe, General Leader, Ke Nanshan, Deputy Leader, and Song Ruhai, totaling 70 people, as well as Guan Jiongzhi, Wang Shao cheng, and the journalists Fang Guoxi and Liu Zhangbing from the Hubei Shanghai Native Place Association, totaling about 100 people. Due to insufficient student ridership, there appears to be no need to continue operating

However, it has been reported that each special train carries only a dozen or so students, making its continued operation unnecessary. Liang Yunsen Breaks Two New Records

Javelin thrower Liang Yunsen exceeded the national record twice yesterday, to his delight. He quickly leaped forward to check the record. It happened twice.

Dai Shuguo's forte is the 400-meter race. In the preliminary rounds two days ago, he was outshone by Singaporean star Chuan Jincheng in both races. Yesterday, in the final, he didn't allow any more surprises, leaving Chuan behind by two meters and setting a new national record of 52.2 seconds. This proves that his skill is truly extraordinary.

A total of thirty-one athletes participated in yesterday's 10,000-meter race, varying in height and build. A quick sketch: the tallest was the Beiping's Niu Qunzhi, the shortest was Shanghai's Zhang Liang, the thinnest was Shanghai's Wang Zhenglin, and the fattest was Weihai's Cao Yanyou.

Guangxi was represented by only one athlete in this National Games, Huang Wenyi. In yesterday's 10,000-meter final, Yang stuck close to Monkey King from behind, eventually securing fifth place and earning two valuable points for Guangxi in track and field. He is certainly more dedicated than those who normally perform well but abandon the race on the spot.

Miss Li Sen Asks, "Do You Still Want More?"

During the 200-meter final yesterday afternoon, female running champion Li Sen showed her prowess and set a new national record. The audience cheered, "Amazing girl!" Immediately, over a dozen photographers surrounded Li Sen, requesting photos one after another for a full three minutes. Li Sen, still catching her breath, exclaimed, "Please hurry! Do you still want more?"

Spectators Yesterday Complained of Being Duped

The weather two days ago was uncomfortably hot, an odd phenomenon for late autumn. The previous night, the heavens were unkind and poured down heavy rain. Yesterday, overcast skies and fog enveloped the area. A few spectators carried umbrellas and wore raincoats. Sadly, the heavens played a trick and did not rain. Those who had not brought umbrellas were relieved, while those who had were complaining of being "duped."

Loud Roll Call Causes Embarrassment

During the softball game yesterday, when the referee called out the numbers of the female athletes, one of them responded softly. However, the announcer searched around but couldn't find her, so he raised his voice and called her again. She suddenly turned towards the referee and smiled shyly, causing the referee great embarrassment.

The Games' Music is Very Pleasing

The most attention-grabbing aspect of this National Games is the music played by the two Public Security and Security Music Bands on both sides of the commander's stand at the beginning and end of each event, when records are broken, awards are given, and finals are held. The melodious sounds invigorate the entire audience, and even the athletes feel more energized.

Tu Zhenglin Was Prescient

Yesterday at noon, before the 10,000-meter race, we visited Wang Zhenglin, Shanghai's star long-distance runner, at his dormitory. We asked for his thoughts on the upcoming 10,000-meter race. Initially, Wang refused to speak directly, only offering a wry smile. After the reporter's persistent questioning, he finally said, "Then my 1,500..." He indeed won the silver medal after the race, as if Wang had foreseen it, displaying a sense of prescience.

Female Athletes Mistake Chen Zhenxing, the Water Monster, for Lin Baohua

Yesterday, while Chen Zhenxing, the "Water Monster," was swimming in the corridor, several female athletes from Henan mistakenly identified him as Lin Baohua. After the Zhejiang women's basketball team defeated Shandong, the players became extremely proud and insisted on the team leader throwing a celebration banquet. As a result, a banquet was held at the New Asia Restaurant on Guoguang Road, where the entire team of athletes feasted.

After the women's 200-meter final, the announcer shouted, "Please will the medal-winning athletes come to the commander's stand to receive their awards." After waiting for a long time, only five female athletes arrived, and Qian Xing Su was missing. Some say that Miss Qian had been ill for several days, resulting in poor performance and constantly outdone by Miss Li, completely disheartened, so she didn't even want the prize.

Everyone Says, "Hello, Fellow Townsman!"

When athletes from Shandong, Hebei, Henan, Shanxi, and other northern provinces meet, their first words are always, "Hello, fellow townsman!" Yesterday, after Gu Desheng won the 10,000-meter race, a reporter went up to shake his hand and also said, "Hello, fellow townsman!" causing much laughter among the bystanders.

Miss Meng Says, "A Terrible Misunderstanding!"

Miss Meng Jianli's wrestling uniform was torn during the match the day before, leading to yesterday's report that "Meng Jianli's Spring Revealed." Miss Meng said, "A terrible misunderstanding!" and asked the reporter to correct it, clarifying that only the hem of her jacket was torn the day before, and no "spring light" was revealed.

The Barefoot Immortal Is Truly Brave

During the 10,000-meter final, Hei Longjiang athlete Lu Yongfeng suddenly took off his running shoes and competed barefoot halfway through the race. The audience hailed him as the "Barefoot Immortal." Running in last place, the starter specially fired a shot for him, and the photographers swarmed around him. His moment in the spotlight was no less than that of Gu Desheng.

Special Notes From The Games

The National Games has been open for a week, and so far, it seems to have more than 300,000 people in attendance. Judging from reporter observation, the spectators consist of mostly 90% from urban, professional women and above. As far as the rural farmer population is concerned, looking around the venue, except for service workers, there are hardly any in attendance. At the very least, their attendance is an exceptionally small number, meaning that the interest in sports seems to only be accessible to the cities and has yet to spread throughout the rural countryside.

Guest seating at the sports grounds are divided into two jiao, four jiao, six jiao, and one yuan seating prices. The two-yuan seats are best, followed by the six and four jiao seats. Two jiao seats are at the northern and southern end of the sports grounds and are in a terrible location, but more often than not, these seats are full and always have new people trying to find a foothold, but they never can. On the contrary, the one yuan seats are usually empty. This shows that the purchasing power of spectators is very limited. The most interest lies in all the ball-related games; with the exception of baseball. With each match, the small amount of viewers resemble the morning stars, giving off a cold and desolate sight. This is probably because those from Shandong are eating Mantou: they don't understand the game.

In the past three days, the wind of athletes signing autographs has risen. Children in Boy Scout uniforms are now holding notebooks and waiting for the winning athletes to award the prizes at the games. This causes the mob to surge to the front and takes an extended amount of time. Even if it is a point of pride for the athlete, spectators have already grown impatient.

The name for the fifth-place athlete from Guangxi, Huang Ruiwen, was listed as Wang Ruiwen on the athlete roster. After running the 10,000 meters yesterday, Huang went to the broadcasting booth and did a full 90-degree bow towards Wu Bangwei to clarify the error. After stating the correction, he bowed again and left, exhibiting polite manners and commanding respect. All other athletes should follow this example. National Library Survey Published

The National Library Survey is a compilation by Xu Wancheng, who has served as the librarian of the Wuxi National Studies College Library, director of the Shanghai Daxia Middle School Library, and staff member of the Suzhou Provincial Library. The survey covers 3,000 libraries nationwide, providing detailed and accurate information on each library's address, establishment date, whether it is private or public, the total number of books and their classifications, the number of daily readers, and the names of the librarians and staff. This survey is unprecedented in its scope and serves as an essential reference book for library management. It also includes several articles on library management and research. The book is priced at three yuan per copy and is distributed by the Longwen Bookstore at the Dananmen in Shanghai. To connect library professionals, Xu has issued discount coupons to libraries, charging only for printing costs.

Telecom Special Edition

The Voice of the Telecommunications Industry

Long-Distance Phone Night Rate Reduction Measures

— Zhen

Prices will be 30% Lower Than Day Rates

—Effective December 1st—

When the pricing system for long-distance calls between Beijing and Shanghai was changed to a three-minute system, some users misunderstood and expressed dissatisfaction with the changes. After the journalist clarified it in the previous edition of this publication, they likely understood the change. In the countries of Europe and America, there are specific night rates for long distance calls in order to allow for people to make use of the phone during the day. The Ministry of Transportation created a similar measure and designed the Long-Distance Phone Night Rate Reduction Measure and designated Shanghai, Nanjing, Hangzhou, Zhenjiang, Wujin, Wuxi, Wuxian, and seven other locations for a trial run and will be implemented starting December 1st. If this is successful, they will spread the use further. All prices will be at a 30% discount from day rates. These times run from 8 PM to 6 AM of the next day. This period is usually used by news agencies for distributing their media reports, showing the support from the Ministry of Transportation for news organizations.

Over the recent years, the telegraphy business operated by the Ministry of Transportation has had the slogan, "cooperate with the masses" as the first priority. The public can give opinions, and if the Transportation Department finds these claims to be useful, they are likely to use them to improve the system and satisfy public demand. The creation of a night rate is a testament to the spirit of cooperation. If these procedures, sincerity and understanding were not enacted, and instead only surmised through speech, then that would hinder the transport policies, which would cause a problem for leaders within society.

Meaning Behind the Ministry of Transportation's Tibetan Telegraphy Code

— Qinghua

Recently, the Ministry of Transportation, at the request of Gesang Tsering, a survey specialist from the Gan Qing and Kang provinces, developed a Tibetan telegraphy code, to facilitate the transmission of telegraphs in the Kang-Tibetan region. This code was publicly tested on the 7th of this month in Nanjing, and the results were very good. They soon will be formally adopted by the telegraph offices of the Kang-Tibetan region. We should not disregard the creation of this code for the fact that it might not be related to the majority of our nation, but the code itself is very important for these three reasons:

(1) Improved Transmission of Telegraphic Text: Telegraphs are the most useful means of communication and its mission is to transmit text from one place to another. In order for telegraphs to be, "fast and simple", telegraphic symbols must be able to directly transmit text. The languages of Europe, America and Japan are mostly comprised of alphabets and letters. To telegraph this, all one would need to do is assign each telegraphic symbol to each letter, and all that is left is the transcription of the message. But Chinese language is made up of 5 forms: Han, Manchu, Mongolian, Hui, and Tibetan. Among them, Han text is most often used, but it's format is completely different from western text and cannot use symbols to transmit text letter by letter, so they had to use four numerical codes to represent each character. This means each telegraph must be translated twice to transmit the text and greatly reduces the efficiency of the telegraph which is a detriment! Because Tibetan language is organized similar to western alphabets, with the exception being that the alphabets usually have different symbols added to the tops and bottoms of the characters, with forty-two letters and a total of seventeen symbols, with a total of fifty-nine letters and symbols. Compared to Roman letters, these are a whole multiple more, but still within the telegraph system, a telegraph symbol can barely be assigned to each of the fifty-nine Tibetan alphabets and symbols to reach the goal of directly transmitting text, opening a new chapter within the history of Chinese telegraphs! (Using phonetic symbols or the Romanized national pronunciation system for Chinese text can allow for direct transmission and is something that will soon be tested)

(2) Facilitating Kang-Tibetan Public Communications: Remote areas that border other countries usually have very simple communication structures. In recent years, the government has slowly been paying attention, and the communication stations of Lhasa, Tibet, as well as Kangding, Ba'an, Ganzi and Dege in Xikang have been founded at different times. But the people that make use of these lines of communication are still few in number. This is mostly due to the fact that the populace has not developed much as well as the fact that telegraphs cannot transmit Tibetan text. (Most Kang-Tibetan government or religious organizations often create temporary codes to allow for the transmission of Tibetan text, but the common folk do not have the means to translate this telegraphy as well as the fact that communication stations often do not have official translations so the people cannot use the telegraphy.) After adopting the Tibetan telegraphy system, communication stations can receive and transmit Tibetan telegraphic messages, allowing for the people of the Kang-Tibetan region to benefit from using the telegraph. The benefits are apparent during the times where communication is difficult and the amount of postal routes is rare!

(3) To Unite the Kang-Tibetan Region and Fortify National Defense: Since the Xuantong Emperor of the Qing Dynasty's dethronement, our country has often been titled a republic of the five ethnicities, but in reality, the Han ethnicity takes the majority of roles within government. Over the last twenty years, the Manchu, Mongolian, Hui and Tibetan compatriots may not have experienced conspicuous discrimination, but they have been left to the devices of their own lives. The central government should work towards unity and take this opportunity to develop the Kang-Tibetan transport and communication networks to allow for all provinces and cities in the Kang-Tibetan region to communicate with ease to promote solidarity! The development of Kang-Tibetan transport, both economically and time-wise, should focus on the development of telegraphy and communication, because the opening of roadways and the construction of railroads take a lot of money and time, but establishing telegraphic routes is an easier feat. Establishing new communication stations within the Kang-Tibetan region would not only connect each region within the Kang-Tibetan region, but allow for those provinces and cities to connect with ease and remove alienation. In the future, the Tibetan telegraph will be open for the public to allow for quick and easy access to information, which will allow for those in the Tibetan region to understand that the national government is prioritizing the regions to increase their unity. This shows another one of the meanings behind the creation of the Tibetan telegraphy code!

Can Multiple Destination Names Be Included in One Telegram?

— Hua

Please Note and Correct this, Governmental and Military Institutions

According to regulations, each telegram should only have one destination name. If there are two return telegrams to be sent to two different places, then it should be treated the same as two separate telegrams and written separately. Absolutely, it's prohibited to put two destination names in one telegram. The reason is simple: telegrams are like postal letters. Would you write two addresses on one letter and ask the post office to send it to two different recipients? Surely, anyone would answer: "No, you can't." If that's the case for postal mail, why should telegrams be any different! This is easy to understand for anyone with common sense.

However, governmental and military institutions have traditionally followed this practice of listing multiple destination names in one telegram, then submitting it to the telegraph office to be sent to recipients in various locations. This type of telegram often causes unexpected disputes and unavoidable errors for the telegraph office. For example, the recent sensational case in Wu-hu involving a rice merchant suing the telegraph office (details can be found in issue 43 of this publication) occurred because the sending agency—the Anhui Provincial Government—included multiple destination names in one telegram, leading to misunderstandings along the way by the receiving telegraph office—the Wuhu Bureau—and ultimately, to a strange lawsuit. If the sending agency had sent the multiple destination names separately, there would have been no misunderstanding or delay! Of course, until governmental and military institutions change this habit, such misunderstandings may occur at any time. Needless to say, this is a significant loss for both the telegraph office and the governmental and military institutions.

Besides the misunderstandings mentioned above, telegrams with multiple destinations are also prone to being missed or resent by relaying telegraph offices. The routing of telegrams often changes due to circuit obstructions. As a result, when relaying offices encounter telegrams with multiple destinations, they often assume that a particular destination should be relayed by a specific office and that no further action is needed. However, if that particular office happens to have a circuit obstruction, the telegram may be missed. Conversely, some particularly cautious offices may resend telegrams that should have been relayed by another office, leading to double sending. This is another unavoidable error on the part of the telegraph office, which can have unfavorable results for governmental and military institutions.

In reality, it doesn't take much effort for the sending agency to use carbon paper to make multiple copies of the telegram. If the nature of the announcement requires that a certain location be informed while simultaneously notifying other locations, it can be clearly stated in the telegram or indicated with a designated marker without any difficulty. I believe that once the authorities in governmental and military institutions understand the pros and cons mentioned above, they will be able to cooperate effectively with the telegraph office, quickly make corrections, and usher in a new era for official and military telegrams.

A Visit to the Temporary Telegraph Office at the National Games

— Wei Li

The highly anticipated Sixth National Games opened on October 10th at the stadium in the center of Shanghai!

Spectators from home and abroad flocked to Shanghai to watch the National Games. The number reached at least hundreds of thousands!

However, countless numbers of compatriots at home and abroad who were unable to come to Shanghai are eagerly awaiting news of the event!

We know that telegrams are the quickest and most accurate way to transmit news about the games!

To promote sports, the Ministry of Transportation has established a temporary telegraph office at the venue. I visited the office and was warmly received by Mr. Zhao Cuiru, the director. Here is a brief record of what I saw to share with our readers!

The temporary telegraph office at the National Games venue is located at number 3, on the right side of the west gate hall. As I walked through the west gate of the National Games venue, I saw the blue and white enamel signs for the "Shanghai Telegraph Office Temporary Receiving and Sending Station" and the "Temporary Post Office." The post office and telegraph office were combined in a double-bay room. The counter was just inside the door, with the post office occupying one-third of the space on the left and the telegraph office occupying two-thirds. Behind the counter was the telegraph room, equipped with the latest machines, including a Creed Keyboard, which can send 300 to 350 letters per minute; a Wheatstone Perforator, which can send 130 to 150 letters per minute; a Teleprinter, which allows direct sending and receiving of letters without pre-perforated paper, operating similarly to a regular typewriter, with a sending and receiving speed of 250 to 300 letters per minute; and a Wheatstone Transmitter-Receiver, which can send and receive 450 to 600 letters per minute.

It is said that the office sends out hard news about the Games to 21 different places every day, amounting to hundreds of thousands of words. Other soft news, news from various newspapers, private telegrams, and social telegrams number in the hundreds. The level of activity is conceivable! All national direct lines can be connected to the office by the Shanghai Telegraph Office for direct reporting. As a result, the speed at which news from the venue is transmitted is unparalleled! News from the Games can be sent to all parts of the country at any time. In addition to the director, the office has three receiving operators, two decoding operators, seven sending operators, and three messengers, who can promptly deliver telegrams to athletes at various venues. All incoming and outgoing telegrams can be processed with maximum speed and accuracy.

The office is open daily from 9 a.m. to 9 p.m., for 12 hours. Customers at the counter are constantly sending telegrams, creating a scene as busy as the road to Shanyin. There is a preferential rate for athletes, who can send social telegrams for only 40 cents per telegram, or 20% of the original price, which is cheaper than airmail. Because telegrams are sent and delivered quickly, athletes from various provinces and cities often use the office to report their whereabouts, daily life, sports news, and to thank relatives and friends for their congratulations. Spectators at the Games also crowd the office to send congratulatory telegrams to the athletes. When I visited, the staff were working diligently, their heads buried in their work. The sound of the machines and the sound of paper echoed the cheers from the venue, creating a kind of natural music that was pleasant to hear! I heard that the female swimmers on one team received the most social congratulatory telegrams from the audience. This shows that the people of our country have a deep understanding of the importance of promoting sports at the National Games and that they are using telegrams to avoid the hassle of writing letters, which is a great step forward in our lives! Spectators entering and exiting the venue always stop to look and praise the progress of the telecommunications industry, which has indeed become increasingly convenient for the public! After my visit, I felt that the office had set a model for a combined post and telegraph office, and that it was working hard to serve the athletes and the public faithfully. No wonder it had earned a good impression from the public! With that, I bid farewell and left.

The Front of the Temporary Receiving and Sending Station

Inside View of the Temporary Receiving and Sending Station

"Reporter"

— Written by Gao Longsheng

The Situation of Telegraphs in England and the United States and the Reasons for Their Development

— Li Jiqing

Having served in various transportation agencies and telegraph offices in China for seventeen or eighteen years, I have a great interest in telegraphs and consider it my lifelong career. At the end of last year, I was sent to the United States to study and investigate in various telegraph and wireless companies for more than eight months. I made a detailed study of the telegraph situation in the United States. Later, I went to Canada to investigate the telegraph companies and learned about their operations. In August of this year, I went from New York to London and then visited the General Post Office of the United Kingdom, the Eastern Telegraph Company, and the Marconi Wireless Telegraph Company to observe and investigate. In early November, I will go to Copenhagen, Denmark, to observe the Great Northern Telegraph Company. In the future, when I return to China via Germany, Belgium, France, and Italy, I plan to visit various telegraph and wireless companies along the way to learn about everything. Now, I will describe the situation of newspaper management and the reasons for its development in the United States and the United Kingdom, as follows, for the reference of those in China who are concerned about the telegraph business:

(1) The United States

In the United States, all kinds of businesses are commercial, and the government is in a supervisory position and does not participate in management. The telegraph industry is no exception and is operated by private individuals who raise shares. Under this principle, there are many private telegraph and wireless companies in the United States, such as Western Union Telegraph Company, Postal Telegraph Company, Radio Corporation of America, Machay Radio Company, Commercial Pacific Cable Company, All America Cable Company, and Glcbe Wiieless Company, etc. All of them send and receive various telegrams and compete for business. As a result of their competition, the methods are novel, and the use of telegrams is widespread among the public. However, since the competition among the companies is fierce, there are often conflicts in business methods and telegram prices, which are not beneficial to all parties. If this situation continues, it may have a major impact on the entire telegraph industry in the United States in the future. Therefore, the United States government is aware of this and has convened a meeting of representatives from various companies in Washington to discuss remedies, so that the companies do not engage in excessive competition, which will affect the entire telegraph industry in the United States. If necessary, the government will exercise control and may even consider merging the companies.

Although the various telegraph and wireless companies in the United States are usually operated commercially, according to United States law, all companies are managed and uniformly directed by the government during wartime. At ordinary times, the companies do not easily allow outsiders to enter, in order to prevent the leakage of telegram messages. The United States government has promulgated laws to restrict this, and all companies must strictly abide by them.

The buildings, equipment, and machines used by the various telegraph and wireless companies in the United States are all very perfect and new. Although there are many companies, they all have considerable income from telegraph fees. Therefore, in addition to various expenses, there is still surplus money to seek their development. If the equipment is not good and the machines are old, it will be difficult for any company to survive in this fierce competition.

(2) The United Kingdom

The telegraph business in the United Kingdom is the same as in China, and is operated by the government. The agency in charge is the General Post Office, which is like the Ministry of Transportation in China. Therefore, the postal, telegraph, and telephone businesses in the United Kingdom are all handled by the General Post Office. However, there is also a commercially operated telegraph and wireless company in the United Kingdom that handles international telegrams. This company is called Cable and Wireless Co. The Great Eastern Telegraph Company, which is related to the history of telegraph administration in China, is part of this company. The company is supervised by the government and is in close contact with the General Post Office, exchanging telegrams with each other. In addition, there are branches of the American Western Union Telegraph Company, the Commercial Cable Company, and the Danish Great Northern Telegraph Company in London and elsewhere. However, these companies are only limited to sending and receiving international telegrams and are subject to various legal restrictions of the American government.

The telegraph business in the United Kingdom is also very developed. Although it is government-run, the business methods used are very commercial and public-oriented. Its equipment and everything else are comparable to those of the telegraph companies in the United States. However, the British national character is slightly more conservative, so some equipment does not seem as new as that of the American companies. A few years ago, the British General Post Office sent people to the United States to investigate and study the various companies, and then followed suit. Therefore, the business situation is generally the same as in the United States. (To be continued)

The Significance of Inspecting Broadcast Radio Receivers

— Chu

It has been almost two months since the Ministry of Transportation issued an order for local telegraph offices to send personnel to inspect broadcast radio receivers. I heard that most radio owners in various places understand the truth of the matter and allow the inspection without any difficulty. However, there are also quite a few who do not know the details and have doubts, so they make excuses to refuse. This has hindered the progress of this work. Now, I will briefly explain why the Ministry of Transportation wants to inspect radio receivers in various places, in order to make the public understand the truth of the matter and dispel their doubts.

As far as I know, the purpose of the Ministry of Transportation's order for local telegraph offices to inspect radio receiver users is nothing more than the following two points: First, it is for the safety of users. Since the Ministry of Transportation is responsible for managing the national broadcast telecommunications industry, it should do its best to ensure the safety of the public who listen to broadcast telecommunications. Because it is aware that most radio users have no knowledge of electricity, they often install antennas arbitrarily, often near telephone, telegraph, lamp, and other power lines. Or the antennas introduced into the house are not equipped with lightning arresters, so they often disrupt communications or cause dangers such as electric lights and antennas getting tangled. For example, two months ago, a family surnamed a certain name in Nanjing's Fengfu Alley had an incident where the antenna and the light were tangled together. Fortunately, it was discovered early and did not cause a major disaster. Therefore, when the radio inspectors from various telegraph offices inspect, they pay attention to whether the installation of the antenna is appropriate and whether the antenna lead-in line is safe. If there are any problems, they will immediately provide guidance and corrections to avoid danger. Second, it is to prevent radio users from setting up private radio stations. Those who install broadcast radio receivers are often of mixed quality, and there are inevitably some unscrupulous elements who operate for personal gain and take advantage of the registration method for broadcast radio receivers to try to be clever. On the surface, they report the installation of a radio receiver to deceive the public, but secretly, they are stealing the day and changing the sun, setting up private radio stations to engage in secret communications, in order to undermine the state-run telecommunications industry. Therefore, it is necessary to send personnel to each household to inspect one by one whether the installed equipment is consistent with the registered equipment, whether there have been any changes to the internal installation, and whether it is used for sending or talking, in order to prevent abuses. From this point of view, the Ministry of Transportation's implementation of radio receiver inspection is on the one hand to ensure the safety of users, and on the other hand to protect the state-run telegraph business. The purpose is very pure and simple, and it is only beneficial and not harmful to users.

As for this kind of inspection work, it has already been stipulated in Article 4 of the Provisional Regulations for the Registration of Broadcast Radio Receivers, and it is not a temporary issuance. All personnel engaged in this inspection work are technical personnel with rich knowledge of telecommunications, their attitude is amiable, and they handle things quickly and efficiently. There will never be any disturbance to the public. Moreover, when they go out to perform their duties, they wear badges with them for identification. They fulfill their obligations and never ask for a single cent. After reading this article, I hope that radio users in various places can understand the meaning of the Ministry of Transportation's implementation of radio receiver inspection, and in the future, when personnel from various telegraph offices come to inspect, they can trust each other sincerely and no longer have any doubts in their minds!

The Reduction of Telephone Charges in England

— Reporter

It is reported that telephone rates in England will be substantially reduced from October 1st, under conditions that permit. The quarterly fee for local lines in London will be reduced from one pound, twelve shillings, and six pence to six shillings. And the fee for various places (except Glasgow, Birmingham, Liverpool, and Manchester) was previously one pound, seven shillings, and six pence, now reduced to one pound. The price of group business and sales is also reduced considerably.

The loss from the above telephone price reduction is about 750,000 pounds in the current year and about 1.5 million pounds in the next year, but it is generally believed that this policy will not only enable the development of telephone services, help commercial prosperity, but also achieve significant benefits and increase telephone revenue.

How to Calculate the Number of Words in Plain English? (Continued)

— Wei Yu

…Please pay attention to the sender…

(10) The name of a horse in horse racing, Race-birse, is counted as one word.

Example 1. Castleribbon (counted as one word)

2. Operaeve (counted as one word)

(11) Combinations of commercial terms and abbreviated letters are counted as one word for every five letters.

Example 1. Feldors (counted as two words) 3. Tudor (counted as one word)

(12) For a group of letters that is customarily permitted, Current nsage is counted as one word for every five letters.

Example 1. Country names, province names, such as US.AUSSR.NY

2. Unit names, such as 16.cgs, cwt, KW.

3. Direction names, such as NW.NE.NNW

4. Commercial terms, such as TT.Fob, Cod,

5. Degree names, such as Dr.LLB, CEBA.

6. Abbreviations in letters, such as Mr.PIO, FS, AM, PM, OK,

7. Abbreviations of newspaper names, such as NRA.USS.CSS, SS,

8. Commercial symbols

(A) Trademarks such as GL

(B) Consecutive numbers such as A3760

(C) The capacity of goods is used as an adjective, such as 5jp, Hcyl

(D) Various symbols are counted as one word for every five letters, but the sender must explain their meaning if necessary.

For example, RS7551, 5F5ZN

(13) Arbitrary irregular unions should be charged separately according to their Components. Example, 1. P&O is written as PANDO (counted as three words) 2. B&S is written as BANDS (counted as three words)

(14) The following common words can be used as single words.

1. Percent (counted as one word) Oclock (counted as one word)

(15) One million is counted as one word (regardless of the number of digits) 30% is also counted as one word.

(16) AM3PM are all treated as complex words and charged as two words.

(17) The combination of the names of two countries to form an adjective, Adjictive, such as Sino Japanese, is calculated as one word

(18) Specialized names such as Stjohn, Stjames, Stgeorges, Stanna, etc. are all counted as one word.

(19) Prefix letters Pro, Pro, Post.ant, do not need to be charged separately. r, Progovenrnment, Prevar, Postgraduate, Antivice, (all counted as one word)

(20) "Cum", "Par" or "SANS" connected to a name should be charged separately.

(21) The prefix 孛EX is used to mean Former, such as Expresident, Expremier, which does not need to be charged separately.

(22) The prefix EX is used to mean "out of" or "Away from", such as Exnanking, exship, exgodown. All should be charged separately as complex words.

(23) Geographical names should be counted as one word.

Example r. Westlake, 2. Yelloriver, 3. Greatwall

(24) Word endings Suffixes such as -ward, -wide, -wise should all be charged separately.

(25) All military ranks, such as Major-general, LT-Commander, are charged as the following words. (End)

The Period of Interruption of the Shanghai-Nagasaki Submarine Cable

— Suo Yi

The submarine cable from Shanghai to Nagasaki was interrupted on September 15th and was only repaired by a ship after ten days.

The so-called cable is to sink a conductor that conducts electricity into the vast ocean, with the ends landing on the shore and entering the bureau, so as to communicate. Occasionally, obstacles occur, and the repair work is very troublesome. First, it must be measured to know the place where the obstacle occurred, and then a cable repair ship must be sent to the sea to repair it. When it is cloudy and rainy or there are storms, the repair work is even more difficult to carry out. Therefore, the interruption of submarine cables spanning the ocean causes considerable losses to the telegraph office. But once the interruption occurs, the telegram is not available, and merchants suffer greatly.

How to connect the reports from Shanghai to Nagasaki or other places in Japan during the Shanghai-Nagasaki cable interruption is worthy of our attention.

The Shanghai International Telegraph of the Ministry of Transportation has a direct line to Tokyo, so the international telegraph can undertake this work and remedy the shortcomings of the above-mentioned cable. It is not afraid of strong winds and heavy rains, not afraid of high mountains and ridges, and there is no worry about cable interruption. It can communicate 24 hours a day. When a merchant sends a telegram, the international radio station immediately sends out radio waves. Radio waves are like the air on the earth, which are everywhere. It can be immediately transmitted to the other end of the communication, and then it can be received as a report.

During the Shanghai-Nagasaki cable interruption period, telegrams from Shanghai to Nagasaki that were previously transmitted via the cable were all sent to the International Radio Station for transmission. Usually, the International Radio uses one transmitter for sending and one receiver for receiving. Because of the Shanghai-Nagasaki cable interruption, the incoming and outgoing reports were unusually crowded, so two large-capacity transmitters were opened to undertake the sending work, and two receiving buildings were used to undertake the receiving work. Therefore, during the cable interruption period, because the International Radio Station's equipment was perfect, the merchants not only had no delay, but also, on the contrary, it was faster!

Shanghai Supplement of Shen Bao

Discussion

The Anti-Slavery Movement

— Meng Ruo

Recently, I heard that the Hong Kong Anti-Slavery Society has scheduled an anti-slavery movement publicity week from the 14th to the 20th. The declaration was issued the day before yesterday, requesting all social organizations, newspapers, churches, schools, etc. to work together to eliminate the slavery system. This move is extremely gratifying.

Slavery is very common in our country. Most families above the middle class use maids. The reason is that the average wealthy person has a comfortable life, and of course he is unwilling to do all the housework himself, and he needs someone to act as an agent. They keep one or two maids at home for their use. All daily chores in the home are assigned to the maids. Being a maid is really a hard life. Getting up early and resting late every day, they are so busy that they don't even have time to catch their breath. This kind of life of cattle and horses and slaves often completely destroys the life of a maid.

There is another difficulty in being a maid, that is, sometimes she is abused by the owner. Every time I see a group of people who are masters, their treatment of maids is simply not human, and they are cruel in every way. If anything is slightly unsatisfactory, they will be stern and abusive, and those with vicious hearts will even inflict inhuman tortures. It is not uncommon in society for maids to be injured or killed by abuse. Not long ago, a case of a young lady abusing a maid occurred in Tianjin, and recently a similar incident has been noisy in Shanghai. This is just an example, and there are countless similar facts.

Slavery is a kind of slavery system. Here we don't want to raise issues such as equality between men and women or the personality of women. What we doubt is, to what extent has human civilization progressed today, is there any reason for the existence of this system? What's more, slavery is a kind of trafficking in human beings, which violates both humanity and laws. In general, families keep maids, and they are all redeemed or bought with money. A group of poor people, due to family difficulties, often redeem or sell their daughters to wealthy people as maids. Under this circumstance, the maid becomes a commodity, and her unfortunate experience is even more pitiful. Therefore, we believe that the slavery system should be abolished.

As for the slavery system, what methods are needed to abolish it? On the active side, the government authorities should enact a law to ban people from keeping maids, and those who violate it will be punished. On the passive side, we must first start with rescuing maids. The establishment of a system has its historical relationship, and it is not easy to overthrow it for a while. Therefore, before the slavery system can be fundamentally prohibited, the society must show sympathy for the maids and try to change their attention. A maid rescue center should also be established to accommodate maids who are unwilling to be maids or who have been abused, so that they can escape the status of slaves. The anti-slavery movement is even more necessary. Like this anti-slavery movement held by the Hong Kong Anti-Slavery Society, its significance is significant, and all parties should work hard to support it, so as to achieve the goal of eliminating the maid system.

Terror

— Hua

Random Notes on Returning Home

I have finally arrived home.

In the evening, under the somewhat bright lamplight (I guess the lamp is only lit on New Year's Eve?), I scrutinized the old house with sensitive eyes, that old ancestral shrine, that paint-peeled long bench, and the faded spring couplets. Like my father, they had all weathered the storms of human existence and had grown old. The two street doors were tightly shut, which made me recall the scene from ten years ago. At that time, the spacious open space outside the door must have been filled with the songs of children, and the adults would have been waving fans, chatting idly with neighbors. But now, there was only a dead silence outside, not a single sound of happy children's songs could be heard. Who could believe such a drastic change?

Page 24

After everyone dispersed, the lamps were also extinguished. The frosty moonlight bathed the eaves, and autumn insects chirped incessantly, singing songs unknown to humans. The flame of the small sesame oil lamp on the table flickered in the wind, casting a large and blurry shadow on the wall opposite my aged father's face. Finally, he spoke in a low and feeble voice:

"The village is getting worse year by year. You should also support your younger siblings. It's really impossible to live here anymore!" I was about to ask, but he started coughing dryly. I hurriedly poured him a cup of tea. Then, he continued:

"For example, Yi Sheng..." He coughed again. The family hadn't used pork lard for cooking in a long time, but tonight they made an exception, so he coughed especially hard.

"Yi Sheng's fate is still unknown. He was taken to the county by the defense corps almost a year ago because the construction of the highway occupied his land, and he wasn't compensated. Alas, land is the life of a farmer..." He paused, but I couldn't say a word. "Yi Sheng's wife is suffering enough now, with four children, two of whom are daughters, all just freeloaders who can't do any work. Last year, they planted tangerines, hoping to sell them for a bit more money to pay off their debts. Little did they know that after a year of careful tending, they ended up selling three tangerines for the price of one. I heard it's because the cannery closed down. Alas, these days, it's really..."

He took a sip of tea. In the silence, the empty hall felt even more eerie. I listened blankly, and the face of an honest, rural farmer flooded my mind, so kind, so amiable, but now his fate is unknown...

"Now there are also more bandits. Some only kidnap people with status, while others only oppose the defense corps. Some homicides often occur at night. You shouldn't stay at home for too long!"

As my father spoke, I felt as if I were sitting in a movie theater. Before my eyes, those desolate people, faces ravaged by wind and rain, swollen eyes, and chests and lungs as hard as iron; also, ruined homes, ruined fields, ruined Tung tree orchards, familiar and unfamiliar, all rushed past my eyes, along with fire, blood, wailing, and shouting, and...

Suddenly, we noticed that the barking of dogs grew louder and closer, from sparse to dense, from low to high. We listened carefully, intently. It was clear that something had happened! My father hurriedly stood up, trembling all over.

"Xuan, Xuan, hurry... quickly...!" He just trembled, unable to finish his sentence.

The footsteps grew closer and were very noisy. I quickly turned off the small lamp with my hand.

Someone knocked on the door! My father pulled me aside and asked in a trembling voice:

"Who is it?"

"It's me, sir... Not asleep yet, huh? Cough! Cough!..."

"Are you Gei Yu?" My father's voice was a bit louder now. "Come in and have a cup of tea. Is there any news outside?"

"I still have official duties. I heard that the third young master has returned. I think it's best for him to go somewhere else tonight. The corps headquarters just called and said that things are very tight outside. Cough... Cough," he said as he coughed, then turned to leave.

"Ah!" My father sighed, unable to speak for a long time. We listened quietly as their footsteps faded away before slowly sitting down.

"Let's rest for a bit and discuss it tomorrow. Let's spend the night in the grass shed tonight. I think that's a bit safer," my father said.

I had no choice but to listen to him, lighting a lantern and walking into the mountains. The wind blowing against my face carried the scent of soil, along with the intoxicating fragrance of rice. The countryside was very quiet. Only the barking of dogs drifted from afar, interspersed with one or two gunshots, which were the signals of the night watchmen. An endless expanse of wilderness was covered with a layer of frosty moonlight. In the moonlight, I vaguely saw a huge watchtower in the distance, half swallowed by darkness. This didn't exist ten years ago. Ten years ago, children would have been carrying small lanterns in the fields, catching crickets and fireflies.

Is Dancing One More Time Saving One More Life?

— Written by Chen Jingsheng

Before the Grave

— Hu Weixiong

It was the child's first anniversary.

The night before, I deliberately invited my wife to see a movie. The movie was a comedy. My intention was to use external stimuli to make my wife forget that unforgettable day. After leaving the cinema, we didn't take a car. We walked home slowly. On the way, I mentioned the film we had seen before with the same actor, and I told many of their unique jokes. My wife seemed very happy, and she did not mention anything about the child. It was already midnight when we got home,

but my wife did not forget the date of the child's anniversary. She said sadly: This is the first year, and we should go to his grave. He is waiting for me! As she said this, she almost shed tears. Maternal love is innate, and my wife especially liked children. Regardless of other people's or her own children, she would always snatch them to hold them. When she told me she was pregnant, I had never seen her so happy. She bought many books on prenatal hygiene and followed the rules in the books every day. At the same time, she was busy cutting and sewing children's clothes, making children's supplies, as if she lived for the children.

She fell ill after giving birth, but as instructed by the parenting knowledges, she opposed hiring a wet nurse. She took the responsibility of raising the child and did not resign to hard work. When the child was learning to speak, my wife nervously interpreted his "咿啞咿啞" sounds into various languages. Occasionally, when she heard a sound like "Mama," she would tell people that my child could speak...

But last autumn, on a drizzly night, the child passed away without getting to say her last words. She neglected sleep and food, and she craved the child almost madly. She collected the child's clothes and toys in a small cabinet. Every day, she imitated this and that like a madman and said to herself, "This is the child's..." She often woke up in the middle of the night and told me that the child had returned; although she knew it was a dream, she always explained to me in detail where she saw the child, or how the child treated her, as if it were true, until she was exhausted and could not support herself, then she continued to sleep.

I also loved the child. When the child suddenly passed away from an illness, I felt a sense of loss in my heart. But in order to relieve my wife's depression, I forced a smile and persuaded her. Every holiday, I rejected my friends' greetings and accompanied my wife to the countryside to broaden her mind, or watched slapstick movies, suppressed my own emotions, and gradually woke my wife up from her grief.

Recently, although she always misses seeing other people's children, she is no longer so stubborn. She accepted the doctor's advice. If she becomes ill from depression, she will never have children again! Her daily life and diet have returned to the right track as before she had children. She collected all the child's relics and hid them in a hidden place. She said: I want to forget the child from now on

But she did not forget the child's anniversary. We bought a bunch of flowers to go to his grave. The autumn morning was high-pitched and lonely. The sharp morning wind brushed, making the grave even more desolate. We stood side by side in front of the child's grave, and my wife couldn't help but cry out loud, as if she had suffered some grievance. I stood blankly. I did not shed tears. I could strongly stop the release of emotions, and I didn't stop my wife from crying her heart out. Otherwise, she would miss the child and become ill.

When the sun occasionally explored its rays, I turned back and patrolled the entire cemetery. The dew condensed on each tombstone, reflecting golden light, as if each smiling face was sleeping peacefully in the tomb. Every soul in the cave has already forgotten the pain of the world, right? I told my wife this meaning, and she raised her head and said: My eye sockets also reflect golden light

The Lame Beggar

— Yafei

He lies at the bottom of this dilapidated watchtower every day. For more than twenty years, no one has ever seen him leave. This rickety old body, however, has never been sick, perhaps because "the blind wild boar is taken care of by heaven."

This watchtower is right next to my house. He often comes to my house to beg for leftovers. He also helps us watch the door. When guests come, he replies for us, or asks the names of the visitors, and he knows almost all of our relatives or friends.

Begging is different from other begging. He doesn't carry a dog-beating stick when he goes out. He doesn't call people "Madam." He only carries a broken bowl and two bamboo chopsticks to the east and the west. Regardless of whether it is sunny or rainy, spring, summer, autumn, or winter, he is always barefoot. He doesn't know how to sing anything, and he only murmurs words in his mouth, like chanting Buddhist scriptures or scolding people, and he doesn't even know what he is praying for. If there is a celebration in the village in front today, or a funeral in the alley behind tomorrow, even if people don't notify him, he will definitely come to the celebration or funeral no matter how far or near it is, whether it is sunny or rainy, he will definitely arrive on time. Naturally, half a cup of leftovers and a bowl of cold rice, people will never let him down.

I really wanted to find out about his life, but when I asked him, he always seemed blank and didn't know how to answer. Once, my grandmother came to my house and told me some stories about him.

Many years ago, a small fishing boat came to the harbor in front of our door. The owner of the boat was a middle-aged couple. They fished, caught shrimp, and dug silt for others to make a living here. After a year, a white and chubby child was added to the boat.

When the child was about ten years old, one summer, the couple contracted a plague at the same time and died, leaving the child behind; thus, he became a poor child without parents. Soon, the small fishing boat also sank to the bottom of the water because it was old and no one took care of it.

The child had no relatives or dependents. He was so young, and he didn't know how to make a living, so he relied on the leftovers of others to live. He slept under this watchtower at night, and now it has been more than fifty years.

When he walked into this watchtower, this watchtower was still new, and the owner of this alley was a prominent court official at the time. Now, the descendants of the prominent officials are unknown, and the owner of the alley has been replaced by a businessman. But he still stays there, although the watchtower has been dilapidated, it can still shelter him from wind and rain.

As for his lame leg, it was thirty years ago, because there was a theft in the alley, those arrogant servants suspected him, and they tortured him with private punishment to force him to confess. One of his legs was crippled by them! When the truth came out, it was discovered that the main culprit of the theft was not him, but the owner's nephew, but Chu was already disabled. Hearing my grandmother talk about his history, I felt a sense of loss in my heart.

Movie

Let's Open the Dam Together

—A Scene from "Triumphant Song"—

"It's been so dry for days. If it doesn't rain in a few more days, won't everything be over? The only way we can do it now is to work together to open the dam. What dragon king is asking for, that's all just nonsense. We can't believe it, we have to know that everything in the world depends on ourselves..."

"Okay, sir! Let's open the dam together."

This is a classroom in a "Peasant Children's Primary School" that has been converted from the Dragon King Temple. Many peasant students have raised their hands in agreement under the drought relief method proposed by teacher Wei Heling.

"If we want to go, we will go now. You go home first and tell your fathers and brothers, call everyone to bring all the dam opening tools to Zhoujiaba to gather..."

After Wei Heling ordered this to the crowd, the crowd cheered and went home to call their fathers and brothers and brought their farm tools. He himself took Wang Yin to Zhoujiaba to survey the location.

This is a scene from "Triumphant Song" directed by Bu Wancang of Yihua Company. Because the atmosphere is very tense and the emotions are very enthusiastic, there is no doubt that it is one of the wonderful performances in "Triumphant Song".

"Metropolitan Scenery" Two Newcomers — Tang Na Zhang Xinzhu

The Premiere of the First Full-Color Stereoscopic Film "Vanity Fair"

Since the transition of films from silent to sound, there hasn't been such a significant revolution as the so-called "New Color" stereoscopic filming, or New Technicolor. However, the attempt at color films has a long history, and the use of three primary colors to capture images and present them on the screen with pure, natural, clear, and vibrant colors, while also creating a three-dimensional effect due to the deeper parallax, should be praised as the latest and most wonderful gift of science. The American RKO Pictures, due to the unexpected success of the three-primary-color experimental short film "La Cucuracha" last year, which won a special award from the Academy of Motion Picture Arts and Sciences and gained unanimous praise from the world, painstakingly selected the famous and romantic novel "Vanity Fair" by the great British writer William Makepeace Thackeray. The story revolves around the romantic life of the heroine Becky Sharp (according to the original name) and incorporates historical traces of the French eccentric Napoleon and the British court to create a drama. They hired the talented superstar Marlene Dietrich to star in it, spending astonishing amounts of money and energy on the creation of a three-color, full-length film. Now that it is premiering in "Nanjing," its sensation is to be expected. However, "Vanity Fair" also bears the mission of the second major transformation of the eighth art, not just as the highest-valued entertainment product in its art.
